Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Recommended Prayer Times on Cloudy Days
Ruling on preferred timing for each prayer when skies are overcast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each prayer's recommended timing on a cloudy day and explain the rationale based on congregation and avoidance of disliked times.

Core Idea
On cloudy days, hasten 'Asr and 'Isha; delay Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib — because of congregation and avoiding disliked times.

In clear weather, each prayer has a preferred time based on visible signs. When the sky is overcast, those signs are obscured. The Hanafi school therefore provides a specific guideline for cloudy days, balancing precaution, congregation, and the avoidance of makruh times. This ruling, as stated in al-Hidayah, distinguishes between the five prayers based on practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups of prayers
From the passage, note that on a cloudy day, three prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib) are to be delayed, while two prayers ('Asr and 'Isha) are to be hastened. Distinguish clearly between the groups.
The mnemonic 'al-ayn ma' al-ayn' helps remember: prayers with the letter 'ayn in their names are hastened.
2
Understand the 'illah for hastening 'Isha
The reason given is that delaying 'Isha on a cloudy/rainy day would reduce the congregation because people would stay home due to rain. Hastening ensures maximum congregation.
The Prophet's (ﷺ) practice on rainy days supports this: he would announce 'Pray in your dwellings.'
3
Understand the 'illah for hastening 'Asr
Delaying 'Asr risks falling into the disliked time (makruh) at the end of 'Asr when the sun yellows. Hastening avoids this risk.
The end of 'Asr time is makruh tahrimi for prayer.
4
Understand why Fajr is delayed
Fajr's time (from true dawn to sunrise) is long, so even if delayed, there is no fear of entering a makruh time. Therefore delaying is recommended.
This contrasts with 'Asr, where the time is shorter and the end is makruh.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variant
Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to delay all five prayers on a cloudy day for precaution, since performing after the time is permissible but before is not. However, the relied-upon position is the distinction as above.
The later Hanafi masters (Marghinani) preferred the distinction, balancing caution and congregation.

مطلع ابر آلود ہو تو صلوٰۃ خمسہ کے مستحب اوقات
وَإِذَا كَانَ يَوْمُ غَيْمٍ فَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ فِى الْفَجْرِ وَالظُّهْرِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ تَاخِيرُهَا وَفِي الْعَصْرِ وَالعِشَاءِ تَعْجِيْلُهَا لِأَنَّ فِي تَاخِيرِ العِشَاءِ تَقْلِيلُ الْجَمَاعَةِ عَلَى اِعْتِبَارِ الْمَطَرِ وَفِي تَاخِيرِ الْعَصْرِ تَوَهُمُ الوُقُوعِ فِي الْوَقْتِ الْمَكْرُوهِ وَلَا تَوَهُمَ فِى الْفَجْرِ لِأَنَّ تِلكَ المَدَّةُ مَدِيدَة وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ التَّاخِير فِي الْكُلّ لِلْإِحْتِيَاطِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ الأَدَاءِ بَعْدَ الْوَقْتِ لَا قَبلَة

ترجمہ اور جب ابر کا دن ہو تو مستحب فجر، ظہر اور مغرب میں تا خیر نماز ہے اور عصر اور عشاء میں تقبیل نماز ( مستحب ) ہے کیونکہ عشاء کو مؤخر کرنے میں بارش کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے جماعت میں کمی کرنا ہوگا اور عصر کو مؤخر کرنے میں وقت مکروہ میں وقوع کا وہم ہوگا۔ اور فجر میں کوئی وہم نہیں کیونکہ یہ مدت دراز ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے، احتیاط کی وجہ سے تمام نمازوں میں تاخیر مروی ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ وقت کے بعد ادا کرنا جائز ہے نہ کہ وقت سے پہلے۔

تشریح سابق میں ان اوقات مستحبہ کا بیان تھا جبکہ مطلع صاف ہو اور اگر مطلع صاف نہ ہو بلکہ آسمان ابر آلود ہو تو اس صورت میں صاحب عنایہ نے ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے۔ العین مع العین یعنی ہر وہ نماز کہ جس میں لفظ عین ہو یعنی عصر اور عشاء ۔ تو اس میں ابر کے دن عجات کی جائے اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ باقی نمازوں میں تاخیر مستحب ہے۔ ابر کے دن عشاء میں جلدی کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایسی حالت میں عشاء کی نماز کومؤخر کیا گیا تو جماعت میں کمی واقع ہوگی اور بارش کی وجہ سے لوگ ستی کریں گے اور رخصت پر عمل کریں گے کیونکہ جب بارش کا دن ہوتا تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اذان کے بعد اعلان کر دیتے کہ الاصلوا فِي رِحَالِكُم خبردار ہو جاؤ کہ اپنے اپنے ٹھکانے پر نماز پڑھ لو۔ عصر میں تجھیل کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عصر کو مؤخر کرنے میں مکروہ وقت میں نماز واقع ہونے کا وہم ہے۔ کیونکہ عصر کا آخر وقت مکروہ ہے اس لئے عصر کی نماز میں تقبیل مستحب ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف فجر کی نماز کہ اس میں یہ وہم نہیں ہے کیونکہ فجر کی نماز کا وقت ( صبح صادق سے طلوع آفتاب تک ) دراز ہے لہذا فجر کی نماز کو مؤخر کرنے کے باوجود طلوع شمس کے وقت نماز واقع ہونے کا وہم نہیں ہو گا۔ اس وجہ سے ابر کے دن فجر کی نماز میں تاخیر مستحب ہے۔ اور ظہر اور مغرب میں تاخیر اس لئے مستحب ہے کہ ابر کے دن اگر ان کو جلدی ادا کیا گیا تو وقت سے پہلے ادائے نماز کا امکان ہے در آنحالیکہ وقت سے پہلے نماز ادا نہیں ہوتی اس لئے ان میں تاخیر کو مستحب قرار دیا گیا۔ حسن بن زیاد نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی کہ ابر کے دن احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ تمام نمازوں میں تاخیر کی جائے کیونکہ جلدی کرنے میں وقت سے پہلے نماز واقع ہونے کا احتمال ہے اور تاخیر میں وقت کے بعد واقع ہونے کا احتمال ہے۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ وقت کے بعد نماز ادا کرنا جائز ہے گو قضا ہو۔ لیکن وقت سے پہلے ادا کرنا جائز نہیں نہ ادان اور نہ قضاء جمیل عفاعنہ
When the sky is cloudy, the recommended (mustahab) is: for Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib, to delay them; for 'Asr and 'Isha, to hasten them. Because in delaying 'Isha, there is a reduction of the congregation due to consideration of rain. And in delaying 'Asr, there is fear of falling into the disliked time. And there is no fear in Fajr because that period is long. And from Abu Hanifa: delaying all of them for precaution. Do you not see that performing after the time is permissible, not before? Translation: And when it is a cloudy day, it is mustahab to delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib, and to hasten 'Asr and 'Isha, because delaying 'Isha would reduce the congregation due to rain, and delaying 'Asr risks falling into the disliked time. And in Fajr there is no such fear because its period is long. And from Imam Abu Hanifa, it is transmitted to delay all prayers for precaution. Do you not see that performing after the time is permissible and not before? Explanation: In the previous [section], the discussion was on the recommended times when the sky is clear. But if the sky is not clear but cloudy, then the author of al-'Inayah stated a rule: al-'ayn ma' al-'ayn, i.e., every prayer that contains the letter 'ayn, i.e., 'Asr and 'Isha, should be hastened on a cloudy day, and for the remaining prayers, delay is mustahab. The reason for hastening 'Isha on a cloudy day is that if it is delayed, the congregation would be reduced, and people would stay home due to rain, acting upon the concession, because when it was a rainy day, the Prophet (ﷺ) would announce after the adhan: 'Pray in your dwellings.' The reason for hastening 'Asr is that delaying it risks falling into the disliked time, because the end of 'Asr time is disliked. Therefore, hastening 'Asr is mustahab. In contrast, for Fajr, there is no such fear because the time of Fajr (from true dawn to sunrise) is long, so even if Fajr is delayed, there is no fear of it falling at sunrise. Hence, delay is mustahab for Fajr on a cloudy day. For Zuhr and Maghrib, delay is mustahab because if they are performed early on a cloudy day, there is a possibility of performing before the time, whereas performing before the time is invalid. So delay is recommended. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that precaution on a cloudy day is to delay all prayers, because hastening risks performing before the time, and delay risks performing after the time. And it is established that performing after the time is permissible, even if qada, but performing before the time is not permissible, neither as ada nor as qada. Jameel 'Afaa 'Anhu.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary discusses the recommended (mustahab) timings for the five daily prayers when the sky is cloudy. The ruling distinguishes between prayers based on practical considerations. For Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib, delaying is recommended; for 'Asr and 'Isha, hastening is recommended. The reasoning: delaying 'Isha could reduce the congregation due to rain, as people may stay home; delaying 'Asr risks falling into the disliked time near sunset; Fajr has a long period so no such risk. Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to prefer delaying all five for precaution, as performing after the time is permissible but before is not. However, the relied-upon position is the distinction, as it balances congregation and avoiding disliked times. The commentary also mentions a mnemonic: prayers with the letter 'ayn in their names ('Asr, 'Isha) should be hastened on cloudy days.

Key Terms
غيم (ghaym): Cloud in the sky; a day with overcast conditions.
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended; an act whose performance is rewarded but omission is not sinful.
تأخير (ta'khir): Delaying the prayer to a later part of its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On a cloudy day, which prayers should be hastened according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib
B) 'Asr and 'Isha
C) All prayers
D) None

Key Takeaway
On cloudy days, hasten 'Asr and 'Isha to avoid makruh time and ensure congregation; delay Fajr, Zuhr, Maghrib to avoid praying before time.

Salah — Prayer

The Three Disliked Times for Prayer: Hanafi Ruling and Disputes
Ruling on three prohibited times with hadith and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three disliked times for prayer, explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf positions.

Core Idea
No prayer is valid at sunrise, zenith, or sunset—the hadith's general prohibition overrides exceptions.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary introduces the chapter on disliked times for prayer. The Hanafi school holds that no prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, is permissible at three specific times: sunrise, midday zenith, and sunset. The proof is the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, which the Hanafis interpret generally. The passage also addresses two scholarly disputes: Imam al-Shafi'i's restriction of the prohibition to Mecca for obligatory prayers, and Imam Abu Yusuf's exception for Friday supererogatory prayer at zenith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
What are the exact times mentioned? Sunrise, zenith (when the sun is directly overhead), and sunset.
These times are based on celestial events, not clock hours.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, no prayer—whether fard, wajib, or nafil—is permissible at these times anywhere.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir uses 'nahana' (forbade), indicating prohibition. The word 'naqbur' is interpreted as funeral prayer, not actual burial.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is makruh tahrimi, not haram.
4
Understand the Shafi'i dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts the prohibition to only supererogatory prayers in Mecca, allowing obligatory prayers elsewhere. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is general and does not specify location.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Shafi'i can pray fard outside Mecca at these times, while a Hanafi cannot.
5
Understand the Abu Yusuf dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf allows supererogatory prayer on Friday at zenith, citing a hadith with an exception. The Hanafi response is that the general hadith of 'Uqbah is stronger and the exception is not accepted.
Abu Yusuf's view is marjuh; the mufta bihi is the general prohibition.

Source Text

مکروہ اوقات ... طلوع شمس، زوال شمس اور غروب شمس میں نماز پڑھنا نا جائز ہے
فَصْلٌ فِي الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي تَكْرَهُ فِيهَا الصَّلَاةُ لَا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا عِندَ قِيَامِهَا فِى الظَّهِيرَةِ وَلَا عِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا لِحَدِيثِ عُقْبَةَ ابْنِ عَامِرٍ قَالَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَوْقَاتٍ نَهَانَا رَسُولُ اللهِ أنْ نُصَلِّي وَأنْ نَقْبُرَ فِيهَا مَوْتَانَا عِندَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ وَعِندَ زَوَالِهَا حَتَّى تَزُولَ وَعِنْدَ تَضَيُّفِهَا لِلْغُرُوبِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ وَالْمُرَادُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَأَنْ نَقْبُرَ صَلَاةُ الجَنَازَةِ لأَنَّ الدَّفَنَ غَيْرُ مَكْرُوهِ وَالْحَدِيْثُ بِإِطْلَاقِهِ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِي تَخْصِيصِ الْقَرَائِضِ بِمَكَّة وَحُجَّةٌ عَلى أَبِى يُوسُفَ فى إباحة النَّفْلِ يَوْمَ الجُمُعَةِ وَقتَ الزَّوَالِ

ترجمہ یہ فصل ان اوقات کے بیان میں ہے جن میں نماز مکروہ ہے۔ نماز جائز نہیں آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے وقت اور نہ دو پہر میں آفتاب کے قیام کے وقت اور نہ غروب آفتاب کے وقت، کیونکہ عقبہ بن عامر کی حدیث ہے فرمایا کہ تین اوقات ہیں جن میں ہم کو نماز پڑھنے اور اپنے مردے دفن کرنے سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع کیا ہے طلوع آفتاب کے وقت یہاں تک کہ وہ بلند ہو جائے اور زوال آفتاب کے وقت یہاں تک کہ وہ ڈھل جائے اور جس وقت کہ غروب ہونے لگے یہاں تک کہ غروب ہو جائے اور مصنف کے قول و ان نقبر سے مراد نماز جنازہ ہے کیونکہ دفن کرنا مکروہ نہیں اور حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے فرائض اور مکہ کی تخصیص کرنے میں اور ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت ہے جمعہ کے روز ، زوال کے وقت نفل نماز مباح قرار دینے میں۔ تشریح ماقبل میں وقت کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک کا بیان تھا یعنی اوقات مستحبہ کا اس فصل میں دوسری قسم یعنی اوقات مکروہ کا بیان ہے۔ یہاں کراہت عام ہے جو جواز مع الکراہت اور عدم جواز دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ حاصل مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک طلوع آفتاب، نصف النہار اور غروب کے وقت نہ فرض نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے اور نہ نفل نماز ، امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ان اوقات میں تمام شہروں اور تمام جگہوں میں فرض نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے اور مکتہ المکرمہ میں ان اوقات میں نوافل کی اجازت ہے۔ (عنایہ ) صاحب فتح القدیر نے لکھا ہے کہ ان اوقات میں مکتہ المکرمہ میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک مطلقا نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے خواہ فرض ہو خواہ نفل ہو
اور حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ جمعہ کے دن قیام شمس کے وقت نفل نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو حضرت ابو ہریرہ اور ابو سعید خدری نے روایت کیا ہے: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ نِصْفِ النَّهَارِ حَتَّى تَزُولَ الشَّمْسُ إِلَّا يَومَ الجُمَعَةِ يعنى حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نصف النہار میں نماز پڑھنے سے منع کیا یہاں تک کہ سورج ڈھلے مگر جمعہ کے دن
Disliked times... It is not permissible to pray at sunrise, at midday (when the sun is at its zenith), and at sunset.
Chapter on the times in which prayer is disliked: Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor when the sun stands at midday, nor at sunset, due to the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir who said: 'Three times the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade us to pray and to bury our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises high, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines towards setting until it sets.' By his saying 'and to bury,' the intended meaning is funeral prayer, because actual burial is not disliked. The hadith, in its generality, is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his specification of the obligatory prayers to Mecca, and a proof against Abu Yusuf in his permitting supererogatory prayer on Friday at the time of zenith.

Translation: This chapter is about the times in which prayer is disliked. Prayer is not permissible at the time of sunrise, nor at midday when the sun stands, nor at sunset, because of the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir... Explanation: In the previous [section], the discussion was on one of the two categories of times, i.e., the recommended times. In this chapter, the second category, i.e., the disliked times, is discussed. Here the dislike is general, encompassing both permissibility with dislike and impermissibility. The gist of the issue is that in our view, at sunrise, midday, and sunset, neither obligatory nor supererogatory prayer is permissible. Al-Shafi'i said that at these times, obligatory prayer is permissible in all cities and places, and in Mecca, supererogatory prayers are allowed at these times. (From al-'Inayah) The author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that in Mecca, according to al-Shafi'i, it is absolutely permissible to pray at these times, whether obligatory or supererogatory. And Imam Abu Yusuf stated that on Friday, at the time of zenith, supererogatory prayer is permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is the hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.' Meaning, the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary introduces the chapter on disliked times for prayer. The three prohibited times are: sunrise, zenith (midday when the sun is directly overhead), and sunset. The proof is the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, which explicitly prohibits prayer and funeral prayer at these times. The hadith uses 'nahana' (he forbade us), indicating a prohibition. The Hanafi school applies this prohibition generally to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers, everywhere including Mecca. The passage then addresses two disputes: (1) Imam al-Shafi'i restricts the prohibition to Mecca for obligatory prayers and allows supererogatory there; the hadith's generality is a proof against this specification. (2) Imam Abu Yusuf allows supererogatory prayer on Friday at the zenith due to a hadith that makes an exception for Friday; the general hadith is considered stronger, so the Hanafi position rejects this exception. The commentary explains that 'and to bury our dead' in the hadith refers to funeral prayer, not actual burial, since burial is not disliked. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that no prayer is valid at these three times, whether obligatory or supererogatory, anywhere, including on Friday.

Key Terms
قبر (qabr): To bury; in the hadith 'naqbur' means 'we bury' but is interpreted as 'we pray the funeral prayer'.
حجة (hujjah): Proof or argument that establishes a ruling, especially against an opposing view.
كراهة (karaha): Dislike; here it encompasses both tanzih (preferred avoidance) and tahrim (prohibition), but the context indicates tahrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the funeral prayer (janazah) at sunrise?
A) Permissible
B) Not permissible
C) Permissible only if urgent
D) Permissible in Mecca

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits all prayers at sunrise, zenith, and sunset based on the general hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, rejecting specifications for Mecca or Friday.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Disliked Times for Prayer and Hanafi Rebuttal of Exceptions
Explains the three disliked times for prayer and defends Hanafi position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the three disliked times for prayer, identify the opposing views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal using the hadith of Uqba bin Amir.

Core Idea
No prayer at sunrise, zenith, or sunset – the general prohibition outweighs all exceptions.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the permissibility of prayer during three specific times: sunrise, zenith (midday), and sunset. While all schools agree that these times are problematic, the Hanafi school maintains the strictest position: absolutely no prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, is valid at these times. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf (a leading Hanafi scholar himself) argued for certain exceptions, but the Hanafi school upholds the general prohibition based on a clear hadith and a fundamental usul principle. In this lesson, we will dissect the arguments and understand why the Hanafi position is preponderant.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying the three disliked times and the Hanafi ruling: no prayer (obligatory or supererogatory) is permissible at sunrise, zenith, or sunset.
The Arabic term used is 'la tajuzu' (not permissible), which in this context indicates makruh tahrimi (prohibited but not conclusively haram).
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The primary evidence is the hadith of Uqba bin Amir, which explicitly forbids prayer and burying the dead at these three times. Understand why this hadith is considered general and binding.
The term 'prayer' in the hadith is general, covering all types of prayer, including Janazah (funeral prayer).
3
Recognize the opposing positions
Examine the views of Imam al-Shafi'i (obligatory prayers permissible everywhere, and in Makkah all prayers) and Imam Abu Yusuf (supererogatory prayer allowed on Friday at zenith). Note their proofs.
Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'whoever misses a prayer, let him pray when he remembers' and special ahadith about Makkah. Abu Yusuf cites a hadith with an 'illa' (exception) for Friday.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
For each opposing proof, the Hanafi school provides a response: 1) The exception in Abu Yusuf's hadith is disconnected or actually means 'and not on Friday.' 2) When permissibility and prohibition texts conflict, prohibition takes precedence (usul principle). 3) The 'exception' for Makkah is interpreted as 'and not in Makkah,' meaning no exception.
This step requires careful attention to the usul principle of preferring prohibition (hurmah) over permissibility (ibahah) when dalils conflict.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Understand how the different rulings affect actual worship: Hanafis delay any prayer (including Janazah and missed obligatory prayers) until after the disliked time passes; Shafi'is pray obligatory prayers at any time and supererogatory in Makkah; Abu Yusuf's view would allow supererogatory prayer on Friday at zenith.
This step connects theory to practice, emphasizing why knowing the mufta bihi position matters.

مذکور ہے کہ اگر ا باحت اور حرمت جمع ہو جا ئیں تو حرمت کو ترجیح ہوگی اس وجہ سے یہاں حدیث عقبہ راجح ہوگی۔ اور حدیث ابوذر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ إِلا بَمَكَةَ کے معنی ہیں ولا بمكة ، جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول إِلا خَطَاء" کے معنی وَلَا خَطَاء کے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں یہ حدیث امام شافعی کا مستدل نہیں ہوسکتی، واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Chapter on the times in which prayer is disliked. Disliked times... It is not permissible to pray at sunrise, nor at its standing at noon, nor at its sunset, due to the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir who said: Three times the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us to pray and to bury our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises high, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines towards sunset until it sets. By his saying 'and to bury' is meant the funeral prayer, because actual burial is not disliked. And the hadith in its generality is an argument against al-Shafi'i for making an exception for the obligatory prayers in Makkah, and an argument against Abu Yusuf for permitting supererogatory prayer at the time of zenith on Friday. Translation: This chapter is about the times in which prayer is disliked. Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor at noon, nor at sunset, because of the hadith of Uqba bin Amir: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from praying and burying our dead in three times... The author's phrase 'and to bury' means the funeral prayer, because burial itself is not disliked. The hadith in its generality is a proof against Imam Shafi'i for his specification regarding the obligatory prayers in Makkah, and a proof against Abu Yusuf for his permission of supererogatory prayer at the time of zenith on Friday. Explanation: In the preceding section, one of the two types of times was discussed, i.e., the recommended times. In this section, the second type, i.e., the disliked times, is discussed. Here the dislike is general, including both permissibility with dislike and impermissibility. The gist of the issue is that according to us, at sunrise, midday, and sunset, neither obligatory nor supererogatory prayer is permissible. Imam Shafi'i said that in these times, obligatory prayer is permissible in all cities and places, and in Makkah, supererogatory prayers are permitted at these times. (Inayah) The author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that in these times, according to Imam Shafi'i, prayer is absolutely permissible in Makkah, whether obligatory or supererogatory. Imam Abu Yusuf said that on Friday, supererogatory prayer is permissible at the time of the sun's standing at noon. The evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith narrated by Abu Huraira and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.' Regarding the obligatory prayers, Imam Shafi'i's evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time.' This hadith indicates that it is permissible to pray obligatory prayers at these times. For permission of supererogatory prayers in Makkah at these times, the hadith of Abu Dharr is cited: Abu Dharr said that prohibition of prayer at these times is except for Makkah. And in another hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O Banu Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying in any hour he wishes, night or day.' This also indicates permission at all times in Makkah. Our evidence is the hadith of Uqba bin Amir: 'Three times the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from praying and burying our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines to sunset until it sets.' In the hadith of Uqba, 'prayer' includes both obligatory and supererogatory, and 'bury our dead' refers to the funeral prayer, because burying the dead at these times is not disliked. So the meaning is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) absolutely forbade praying at these times, whether obligatory or supererogatory, and forbade the funeral prayer. Therefore, because this hadith is general, it serves as a proof against Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf. The response to Imam Abu Yusuf's hadith is that the exception 'except on Friday' is disconnected (munqati'). A second response is that 'except on Friday' means 'and not on Friday,' so the meaning is: the Prophet forbade prayer at midday, and also forbade it on Friday at that time. Regarding Imam Shafi'i's hadith about sleeping through a prayer, the response is that this hadith indicates permissibility of prayer at these three times, while the hadith of Uqba indicates prohibition. According to usul al-fiqh, when permissibility and prohibition conflict, prohibition takes precedence, so the hadith of Uqba is preponderant. The response to the hadith of Abu Dharr is that 'except in Makkah' means 'and not in Makkah,' just as Allah's saying 'except a mistake' means 'and not a mistake.' In this case, this hadith cannot be used as evidence by Imam Shafi'i. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the permissibility of prayer during the three disliked times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The author first presents the Hanafi ruling that no prayer—whether obligatory or supererogatory—is permissible at these times, based on the hadith of Uqba bin Amir. The hadith explicitly mentions three times and includes a prohibition of prayer and of burying the dead (interpreted as funeral prayer). The author then addresses the positions of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf, who made exceptions. Imam Shafi'i argued that obligatory prayers are permissible at these times everywhere, and that in Makkah even supererogatory prayers are allowed. His evidence includes the hadith that whoever misses a prayer should pray when they remember, as that is its time. Imam Abu Yusuf argued that on Friday, supererogatory prayer is allowed at the time of zenith, citing a hadith that explicitly excludes Friday. The Hanafi response counters each proof: The exception in Abu Yusuf's hadith is interpreted as disconnected or as emphasizing that Friday is also included in the prohibition. Regarding Shafi'i's hadith, the principle is that when a permissive text and a prohibitive text conflict, prohibition is given precedence. The hadith of Abu Dharr about Makkah is interpreted to mean that Makkah is also included in the prohibition (i.e., 'except' means 'and not'). Thus the Hanafi position that prayer is absolutely prohibited at these times is upheld.

Key Terms
لَا تَجُوزُ (la tajuzu): Not permissible; here it indicates prohibition (haram or makruh tahrimi).
الظَّهِيرَةِ (al-zahirati): The midday time when the sun is at its zenith.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer; included in the prohibition of prayer at disliked times.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the hadith of Uqba bin Amir considered preponderant over the hadith that permits prayer on Friday at zenith?
A) Because the hadith of Uqba is mutawatir.
B) Because the exception in Abu Yusuf's hadith is disconnected (munqati') or interpreted as 'and not on Friday.'
C) Because the Hanafi school's imam preferred it without evidence.
D) Because the hadith of Uqba mentions three times while the other mentions only one.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits all prayers at the three disliked times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) based on the general prohibition in the hadith of Uqba, overriding any exceptions for obligatory prayers, Friday, or Makkah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Funeral Prayer and Sajda Tilawah in Disliked Times
Ruling on funeral prayer and prostration of recitation in the three disliked times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer and sajda tilawah during the three disliked times, explain the rationale of deficient obligation (naqisah), and distinguish this from the prohibition of complete prayers.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer and sajda tilawah are valid but disliked in disliked times because they are deficient by nature.

In this passage, the author addresses a common question: what is the ruling on performing funeral prayer or the prostration of recitation during the three times when prayer is generally prohibited? The text clarifies that while these acts are not absolutely forbidden, they are disliked (makruh tanzih). The key insight is that these obligations are inherently incomplete (naqisah) because they arise from an immediate cause, unlike standard prayers which require a complete time period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage initially negates funeral prayer and sajda tilawah during disliked times, but then clarifies that the negation means dislike (karahah), not prohibition. Identify that the hukm is makruh tanzih.
The term 'naf' (negation) is qualified to indicate dislike, not absolute forbiddance.
2
Understand the exception for Asr prayer
The text mentions an exception for 'Asr of that day at sunset (ghurub). This helps illustrate the principle of cause (sabab) and how part of the time can suffice for obligation.
The exception is not for funeral prayer but for Asr; it serves as a comparison to show the difference in obligation.
3
Analyze the ta'lil (reasoning) for the ruling
The reasoning is that funeral prayer and sajda tilawah are inherently deficient (naqisah) because their obligation is tied to an immediate cause (presence of corpse or recitation) rather than a fixed time. Thus, they can be performed deficiently, even in disliked times.
Other prayers (like fard prayers) are complete obligations (kamilah) and cannot be performed deficiently, hence they are prohibited in disliked times.
4
Apply the ruling: validity with dislike
Conclude that if one performs funeral prayer or sajda tilawah during a disliked time, the act is valid (jaza) but disliked. The dislikedness is tanzih, not tahrimi.
The phrase 'adiha naqisatan kama wajabat' confirms that the deficiency matches the obligation.

اوقات ثلثہ میں نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت کا حکم
قَالَ وَلَا صَلوةُ جَنازَةٍ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلَا سَجَدَةُ تِلَاوَةٍ لأَنَّهَا فِي مَعْنَى الصَّلوةِ إِلَّا عَصْرَ يَوْمِهِ عِنْدَ الْغُرُوبِ لأَنَّ السَّبَبَ هُوَ الجُزْءُ القَائِمُ مِنَ الْوَقْتِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِالْكُلِّ لَوَجَبَ الأَدَاءُ بَعْدَهُ وَلَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِالْجُزْءِ الْمَاضِي فَالْمُؤَدّى فِي آخِرِ الوَقْتِ قَاضٍ وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذلِكَ فَقَدْ أَداهَا كَمَا وَجَبَتْ بِخِلَافِ غَيْرهَا مِنَ الصَّلَوَاتِ لأنَّها وَجَبَتْ كَامِلَةٌ فَلَا تَتَادَى بِالنَّاقِضِ قَالَ وَالمُرَادُ بِالنَّفَى المَذْكُورَ فِى صَلَاةِ الْجَنَازَةِ وَ سَجَدَةِ السّلاوَةِ الْكَرَاهَةُ حَتَّى لَوْ صَلَاهَا فِيْهِ أَوْ تَلَا سَجْدَةً فِيْهِ وَسَجَدَهَا جَازَ لِإِنَّهَا أَدِيَتْ نَاقِصَةُ كَمَا وَجَبَتْ إِذِ الوُجُوبُ بِحُضُورِ . الجنازة والتلاوة
The ruling on funeral prayer and prostration of recitation in the three times. He (the author) said: There is no funeral prayer based on what we have narrated, nor prostration of recitation, because it is in the meaning of prayer, except the Asr of that day at sunset, because the cause is the remaining part of the time. If it were connected to the whole time, then it would be obligatory to perform it after that; if it were connected to the past part, then the one performed at the end of the time would be a make-up. When that is the case, then he has performed it as it was obligatory, unlike other prayers because they are obligatory as complete, so they cannot be performed deficiently. He said: What is meant by the negation mentioned regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is dislike (karahah), so if one performs them at that time, or recites a verse of prostration and prostrates, it is permissible, because they are performed deficiently just as they were obligatory, since the obligation arises due to the presence of the corpse or the recitation.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on performing funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and the prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa) during the three disliked times. The author states that these acts are not absolutely prohibited but rather disliked (makruh). However, an exception is made for performing 'Asr prayer on the same day at sunset if one has missed it—this is because 'Asr at sunset is performed as the actual prayer due to the cause (sabab) being only a part of the time. The reasoning: if the obligation were tied to the entire time, one would have to pray after it; if to the past part, the one performed at the end would be a make-up (qada'). But the 'Asr prayer at sunset is still the ada' (on-time) prayer because the cause (the time remaining) is sufficient. Other prayers are obligatory in a complete manner, so they cannot be performed deficiently during these times. For funeral prayer and sajda tilawa, they are considered deficient by nature (obligated due to immediate cause like presence of corpse or recitation), so performing them during disliked times is permissible (though disliked). Thus, the negation in the text refers to dislike, not absolute prohibition.

Key Terms
صَلوةُ جَنازَةٍ (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer, a communal obligation (fard kifayah) performed over the deceased.
سَجَدَةُ تِلَاوَةٍ (sajdat tilawah): Prostration required upon reciting or hearing a verse of sajda in the Quran.
نَاقِصَةُ (naqisah): Deficient; here it means that funeral prayer and sajda tilawa are inherently incomplete acts compared to other prayers, so they can be performed even in disliked times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is it permissible (though disliked) to perform funeral prayer during a disliked time?
A) Because it is a fard kifayah and urgency overrides the prohibition.
B) Because it is performed deficiently just as it is obligated deficiently.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically allowed it.
D) Because it is not a prayer in the full sense.

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer and sajda tilawah are valid but disliked in disliked times because they are deficient obligations (naqisah) and can be performed deficiently.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Funeral Prayer and Sajdat al-Tilawah During Prohibited Times
Ruling on funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah during the three prohibited times with exception for 'Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah during the three prohibited times, explain the exception for 'Asr of the same day, and distinguish between an act that is makruh tahrimi and one that is invalid.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah are valid but makruh tahrimi during prohibited times, except 'Asr of the same day.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling: the Hanafi school considers funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) as prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) during the three prohibited times—sunrise, zenith, and sunset—yet validates them if performed. The key is that these acts are deficient obligations (wajib naqis) that are performed as they become obligatory. An exception is made for 'Asr prayer of the same day at sunset due to its unique cause (sabab). We will unpack the proof, the exception's rationale, and clarify why 'makruh' here does not mean invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). Both are ruled as makruh tahrimi during the three times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The text explicitly says the negation implies karahah, not absolute prohibition.
The three prohibited times are based on the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet forbade prayer and burying (i.e., funeral prayer) at these times. Sajdat al-tilawah falls under the same prohibition because it shares the same conditions as prayer (tahara, satr, qibla), thus it is analogous.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and others; the text refers to it as 'the hadith we narrated'.
3
Explain the exception for 'Asr
The exception is 'Asr of the same day at sunset. This is because the cause (sabab) of its obligation is the remaining part of the time. If one delays 'Asr until sunset, the obligation becomes deficient, so performing it at that moment fulfills it as it was obligated.
Other prayers become obligatory as complete (with full time) and cannot be performed deficiently.
4
Understand the meaning of karahah
The negation in the text indicates karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitive dislike), meaning the act is sinful but valid if performed. This is because funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah are deficient obligations; they are valid even when performed deficiently.
Contrast with voluntary prayers, which are invalid if performed during these times because they are complete obligations.
5
Resolve the objection about laughing
An objection arises: if sajdat al-tilawah is like prayer, why doesn't laughing break wudu? The answer: the hadith about laughing breaking wudu refers to full prayer (with takbir, ruku', sujud); sajdat al-tilawah is not full prayer, so wudu remains intact.
This highlights that sajdat al-tilawah is like prayer in conditions but not in all rulings.

نقصان کے ساتھ ادا کرنے سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ اب دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہو گا کہ جو شخص غروب آفتاب کے وقت عصر کی نماز ادا کرتا ہے تو اس کے سبب میں تین احتمال ہیں:۔
The ruling on funeral prayer and prostration of recitation in the three times. He said: And do not perform funeral prayer, due to what we have narrated, nor prostration of recitation, because it is in the meaning of prayer, except the 'Asr of that day at sunset, because the cause is the remaining part of the time. For if it were attached to the whole, performance would be obligatory after it; and if attached to the past part, the one performing at the end of the time would be performing it as qada. And if that is the case, then he has performed it as it became obligatory, unlike other prayers, because they became obligatory as complete and are not performed with the defective [time]. He said: And the intended meaning of the negation mentioned in funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is dislike (karahah), such that if one prays it during that time, or recites a verse of prostration and prostrates, it is valid, because it was performed deficiently as it became obligatory, since the obligation arises from the presence of the funeral and the recitation. Translation: And do not perform funeral prayer, due to the hadith that we narrated, nor prostration of recitation, because prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, except the 'Asr of that day at sunset. Because the cause is the remaining part of the time; if the cause were attached to the whole time, performance would be obligatory after it; if attached to the past part, the one performing at the end of the time would be performing qada. When that is the case, he has performed it as it became obligatory, unlike other prayers, because they became obligatory as complete, so they cannot be performed with the defective [time]. The author said: The intention of the negation mentioned in funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is dislike (karahah), such that if one prays it during that time, or recites a verse of prostration and prostrates, it is valid, because it is performed deficiently as it became obligatory, since the obligation arose from the presence of the funeral and the recitation. Explanation: The author said: Do not perform funeral prayer nor prostration of recitation in the three times. The proof is the hadith that has passed, i.e., 'and that we bury our dead in them'. As for the non-permissibility of prostration of recitation, the proof is that prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, in that the conditions of prayer - purification, covering the 'awrah, facing the qibla, etc. - are also conditions for it. So when prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, it falls under the prohibition of prayer in the three times. As has been said: 'Three times the Messenger of Allah forbade us from praying in them.' Question: But here an objection arises: Since prostration of recitation is equivalent to prayer, then just as laughing out loud invalidates wudu and prayer, similarly laughing out loud in prostration of recitation should break wudu. However, laughing out loud in prostration of recitation does not break wudu. Answer: The prayer in which laughing is said to break wudu in the hadith refers to the prayer with takbir and bowing and prostration; prostration of recitation is not like that, so if one laughs out loud, wudu is not broken. And prayer was prohibited during these three times so that resemblance to sun worshippers would not occur. Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: Prayer is absolutely prohibited in the three times, except the 'Asr of that day. That is, if someone did not pray 'Asr until sunset approached, he may pray that day's 'Asr at sunset. But no other prayer, nor 'Asr of another day, is permissible at that time. Before the proof, note a few things: 1) The times of prayer are the cause (sabab) of its obligation. 2) The cause precedes the effect. 3) As the cause is, so will the obligated effect be: if the cause is complete, the effect is complete; if the cause is deficient, the effect is deficient. 4) If a prayer becomes obligatory as complete, it must be performed completely; if it becomes obligatory as deficient, performing it with deficiency still constitutes performance. Now the gist of the proof is: The person who performs 'Asr at sunset has three possibilities in its cause:
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) during the three prohibited times. The ruling is that both are makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) during these times, but if performed, they are valid. The proof is the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir where the Prophet forbade praying and 'burying' (i.e., funeral prayer) at those times. Sajdat al-tilawah is included because it shares the same conditions as prayer (tahara, satr, qibla) and thus falls under the general prohibition. However, an exception is made for the 'Asr prayer of the same day if one delays it until sunset; this is because the obligation of 'Asr arises from the remaining part of the time (the cause is the remaining time, not the whole period). If one prays it at the edge of sunset, it is performed as it was obligated—deficiently—and is valid. Other prayers become obligatory as complete (with their full time) and cannot be performed deficiently. The passage also addresses a seeming contradiction: if sajdat al-tilawah is like prayer, why doesn't laughing break wudu? The answer distinguishes between full prayer (with takbir, ruku', sujud) and prostration alone. The prohibition is to avoid resembling sun worshippers. Al-Quduri's view is cited affirming the absolute prohibition except for 'Asr of the same day.

Key Terms
صلاة جنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer, which is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) upon the Muslim community for a deceased Muslim.
سجدة تلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in the Quran.
كراهة (karahah): Dislike, here meaning prohibition (makruh tahrimi) that makes the act sinful but does not invalidate it if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs sajdat al-tilawah during sunset, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) It is prohibited and invalid.
D) It is recommended (mustahabb) at sunset.

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah during the three prohibited times are makruh tahrimi but valid, except 'Asr of the same day at sunset.

Funeral Prayer and Sajdah Tilawah in Prohibited Times: Karahah, Not Invalidity
Ruling on karahah of funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah during the three prohibited times and explain why they are valid if performed.

Core Idea
Both funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah are makruh but valid in prohibited times because their obligation arises from an incomplete cause.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on performing funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). While these acts are generally prohibited based on a hadith, the Hanafi school classifies the prohibition as karaah tahrimiyyah, meaning they are valid if performed. This is due to the nature of their obligation: both become obligatory due to an immediate cause (presence of funeral or recitation of ayah) that occurs in an incomplete time, making the obligation itself incomplete. Performance in that state fulfills the duty. The lesson also addresses the objection regarding laughter invalidating wudu in sajdah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the default ruling for funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah in prohibited times? The text states they are not to be performed, based on a hadith.
2
Understand the classification of the prohibition
Is the prohibition absolute (haram) or a lesser degree? The author clarifies that the negation refers to karahah (disliked), not invalidity.
This is a key Hanafi distinction: karahah tahrimiyyah is close to haram but with weaker evidence, and performance is valid.
3
Recognize the exception
What exception is mentioned? 'Asr of the same day at sunset is allowed (this is the starting point for the next lesson).
4
Analyze the proof
How does the hadith support the ruling? The hadith prohibits prayer in these times, and sajdah tilawah is considered in the meaning of prayer due to shared conditions (purity, covering, facing qiblah).
5
Address the objection
Why doesn't laughter invalidate wudu in sajdah tilawah? The hadith about laughter refers to the full ritual prayer with takbir and ruku', not to sajdah tilawah.
This clarifies that sajdah tilawah is a distinct act, not identical to formal prayer.

یعنی سبب اگر کامل ہے تو مسبب بھی کامل واجب ہوگا اور اگر سب ناقص ہے تو مسبب بھی ناقص واجب ہوگا۔ ۴) یہ کہ نماز اگر کامل واجب ہوئی تو کامل ادا کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور اگر ناقص واجب ہوئی تو صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا کرنے سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ اب دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہو گا کہ جو شخص غروب آفتاب کے وقت عصر کی نماز ادا کرتا ہے تو اس کے سبب میں تین احتمال ہیں:۔ ایک یہ کہ پورے وقت کو سبب قرار دیا جائے ، دوم یہ کہ وقت کا جو حصہ گذر چکا وہ سبب ہو ، ہوم یہ کہ جزء متصل لعلا داء سبب ہو سر اول کے دو احتمال باطل ہیں اس لئے کہ اگر پورے وقت کو سبب مانا جائے تو وقت کے بعد نماز ادا کرنا واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مسبب ، سبب سے مؤخر ہوتا ہے حالانکہ نماز وقت کے اندر واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ وقت کے بعد ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ پورا وقت، وجوب صلوۃ کا سبب نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرا احتمال اس لئے باطل ہے کہ اگر جزء ماضی یعنی گذرے ہوئے جز کو سبب مانا جائے تو جو شخص آخر وقت میں نماز پڑھے گا تو اس کو قضاء کرنے والا کہنا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ اس کو قضاء کرنے والا نہیں کہا جاتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ جو جز ء ادائے صلوۃ کے متصل ہے وہ وجوب صلوۃ کا سبب ہے اور مسئلہ مذکور میں جزء متصل للاداء وقت ناقص ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ وقت ( سبب ) اگر ناقص ہو تو نماز بھی ناقص ہی واجب ہوگی پس اس شخص پر جیسی نماز واجب ہوئی تھی ویسی ہی ادا کی ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ آج کی عصر غروب آفتاب کے وقت پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف دوسری نمازیں جو اس روز کی عصر کے علاوہ ہوں وہ غروب کے وقت ادا کرنے سے ادا نہ ہوں گی کیونکہ وہ نماز میں کے ادا ہو گی کیونکہ وہ بصفت کمال واجب ہوئی تھیں لہذا نا قص وقت کے ساتھ ادا نہ ہوں گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت میں جو جواز کی نفی کی گئی اس سے کراہت مراد ہے یعنی یہ دونوں ان اوقات میں مکروہ ہیں۔ حتی کہ اگر مکروہ وقت جنازہ آیا اور اسی مکر وہ وقت میں نماز جنازہ پڑھ لی، یا مکروہ وقت میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کر کے وقت مکروہ ہی میں سجدہ ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ کے واجب ہونے کا سبب جنازہ کا حاضر ہونا ہے اور سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہونے کا سبب آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کرنا ہے اور چونکہ یہ دونوں سبب وقت ناقص ( وقت مکروہ) میں پائے گئے اس لئے نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت بھی ناقص ہی واجب ہوں گے پس یہ دونوں جیسے واجب ہوئے تھے ویسے ہی ادا کر دئیے اس لئے ادا ہو گئے۔ اس کے بر خلاف فرائض کہ وہ ان اوقات شاھ میں جائز نہیں ہیں۔
Translation: And do not pray the funeral prayer due to this hadith which we narrated, and the prostration of recitation is also not permissible because the prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, except for the 'Asr of the same day at sunset. Because the cause is that part of the time which is present; because if the cause is related to the entire time, then performing it after the time would be obligatory. And if the cause is related to that part which has passed, then the one performing at the end of time would be a qada performer. And when that is the case, he has performed it as it was obligatory. Unlike other prayers, because they were obligatory as complete, so they will not be performed with an incomplete (time). The author said that in the negation mentioned regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, the meaning is karahah. Even if he performs the funeral prayer in a makruh time, or recites an ayah of sajdah and performs sajdah, it is permissible, because the prostration of recitation and funeral prayer are performed as incomplete as they were obligatory. Because the obligation arose from the presence of the funeral and from reciting the ayah of sajdah. Explanation: The author said that during the three times, do not perform funeral prayer nor prostration of recitation. The proof is the hadith that has passed, i.e., 'Do not bury your dead' and the proof for the impermissibility of prostration of recitation is that prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer in that the conditions of prayer—purity, covering the private parts, facing the qiblah, etc.—are also conditions in prostration of recitation. So when prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, it will be included under the prohibition of prayer in the three times. Thus, the hadith is: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited us from praying in them.' Question: Here an objection arises that when prostration of recitation is equivalent to prayer, then just as laughing out loud invalidates both wudu and prayer, similarly, laughing out loud during prostration of recitation should break wudu. Yet, laughing out loud during prostration of recitation does not break wudu. Answer: In the hadith where laughing is said to be a nullifier of wudu, what is meant is the prayer with takbir tahrimah and ruku' and sajdah, and prostration of recitation is not like that. Therefore, if one laughs during prostration of recitation, wudu will not break. And the reason for prohibiting prayer during these times is to avoid resemblance to sun worshippers. Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that prayer is absolutely prohibited during the three times, but the 'Asr of the same day is exempted. That is, if someone did not pray 'Asr until the time of sunset, he can pray that day's 'Asr at the time of sunset. But no other prayer or 'Asr of another day is permissible at that time. Before the proof, keep a few things in mind: (1) That the times of prayer are the cause for its obligation. (2) That the cause precedes the effect. (3) That as is the cause, so is the effect obligatory. That is, if the cause is complete, then the effect is also obligatory as complete; and if the cause is incomplete, then the effect is also obligatory as incomplete. (4) That if prayer becomes obligatory as complete, then it is necessary to perform it completely; and if it becomes obligatory as incomplete, then performing it with the quality of incompleteness will also fulfill it. Now the gist of the proof is that the person who prays 'Asr at sunset, there are three possibilities regarding its cause: First, that the entire time is made the cause; second, that the portion of time that has passed is the cause; third, that the part connected to the performance is the cause. The first two possibilities are invalid because if the entire time is considered the cause, then performing the prayer after the time would be obligatory, because the effect is delayed from the cause, whereas prayer is obligatory within the time, not after. So it is known that the entire time is not the cause for the obligation of prayer. The second possibility is invalid because if the past part is considered the cause, then the person who prays at the end of time would be called a qada performer, whereas he is not called a qada performer. So it is established that the part connected to the performance is the cause for the obligation of prayer. And in the mentioned case, the part connected to performance is an incomplete time. And it has passed previously that if the time (cause) is incomplete, then prayer is obligatory as incomplete. So this person has performed the prayer as it was obligatory. Therefore, we say that praying today's 'Asr at sunset is permissible. Unlike other prayers besides that day's 'Asr, they will not be fulfilled by performing at sunset, because they were obligatory with complete quality, so they will not be performed with an incomplete time. The author of Hidayah says that in the negation of permissibility regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, the meaning is karahah. That is, both are makruh in these times. Even if the funeral occurs in a makruh time and he performs the funeral prayer in that same makruh time, or he recites an ayah of sajdah in a makruh time and performs the sajdah in that same makruh time, it will be permissible. The proof is that the cause for the obligation of funeral prayer is the presence of the funeral, and the cause for the obligation of prostration of recitation is reciting the ayah of sajdah. And since both causes occurred in an incomplete time (makruh time), therefore the funeral prayer and prostration of recitation also become obligatory as incomplete. So as they were obligatory, they have been performed, and thus they are fulfilled. Unlike the obligatory prayers, which are not permissible in these times.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion of the Hidayah's rulings on what prayers are permissible during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The author begins by stating the general ruling: funeral prayer and sajdah al-tilawah are not performed during these times, based on the hadith prohibiting burial of the dead at those times. However, an exception is made for the 'Asr prayer of the same day at sunset. The reasoning is detailed: the cause (sabab) for obligation of a prayer is the time, but for 'Asr at sunset, only a part of the time is present, which is an incomplete cause. Therefore, the obligation itself is incomplete, and performing it in that incomplete state fulfills it. For other prayers (like other missed prayers or the next day's 'Asr), the complete time has passed, so they are not valid at sunset. The author then clarifies that the prohibition of funeral prayer and sajdah is not absolute impermissibility but karahah (disliked). If one performs them in a makruh time, it is valid because their causes (presence of funeral, recitation of ayah) occur at that moment, making the obligation incomplete; thus performance with incompleteness suffices. The passage also addresses an objection: if sajdah tilawah is like prayer, why doesn't laughter break wudu? The answer is that the hadith about laughter nullifying wudu refers specifically to the formal prayer with takbir and bowing, not sajdah tilawah. The prohibition of prayer at these times is to avoid imitating sun-worshippers. This is a classic Hanafi position that distinguishes between complete and incomplete causes, a key principle in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that brings about the obligation; here, the time for prayer or the presence of the funeral/recitation.
کراہت (karāhah): Disliked but not strictly forbidden; the prohibition is not absolute, so performance is valid.
جزء متصل للاداء (juz' muttasil li-al-adā'): The part of time immediately connected to the performance of the prayer; this is the effective cause for obligation when the full time is not present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing the funeral prayer at sunrise?
A) Haram and invalid
B) Makruh but valid
C) Must be performed later
D) Only valid if no other time is available

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah are makruh tahrimi in prohibited times but valid if performed due to the incomplete nature of their obligation.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
The Exception of 'Asr at Sunset: Incomplete Cause and Valid Performance
Detailed proof for 'Asr at sunset exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits performing the current day's 'Asr prayer at sunset and distinguish it from other prayers using the concept of juz' muttasil li-al-ada'.

Core Idea
The cause for 'Asr at sunset is the part of time connected to performance, making the obligation incomplete and performance valid.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi exception that permits performing the current day's 'Asr prayer at sunset, even though it is one of the three prohibited times. The author provides a detailed causal analysis, demonstrating that the effective cause for the obligation of a prayer is not the entire time but the part of time immediately connected to its performance (juz' muttasil li-al-ada'). This part is incomplete at sunset, so the obligation is incomplete and performance in that state is valid. Other prayers, which have a complete cause (full time), are not valid at sunset.

Guided Path
1
State the exception
What is the exception mentioned by al-Quduri? Prayer is absolutely prohibited in the three times, except for the current day's 'Asr at sunset.
2
Understand the four premises
What are the four premises about cause and effect? (1) Times are cause for obligation. (2) Cause precedes effect. (3) Cause determines the completeness of the obligation. (4) Incomplete obligation can be performed incompletely.
These are foundational for the proof.
3
Analyze the three possibilities
What are the three possible causes for 'Asr at sunset? (a) entire time, (b) past time, (c) part connected to performance. Which are valid and why? The first two are refuted; the third is established.
This is a classic talil (reasoning) exercise.
4
Apply the conclusion
Given that the cause is the part connected to performance, and that part is incomplete at sunset, what is the ruling? The obligation is incomplete, so performing it at that time fulfills it.
5
Distinguish other prayers
Why are other prayers (like missed Zuhr or next day's 'Asr) not valid at sunset? Because their cause was the complete time, making the obligation complete; an incomplete time cannot fulfill a complete obligation.

ہے جو قائم ہے کیونکہ سبب اگر کل وقت کے ساتھ متعلق ہو تو ادا کرنا وقت کے بعد واجب ہوگا ۔ اور اگر سبب اس جز کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جو گزر گیا تو آخر وقت میں ادا کرنے والا ، قضا کرنے والا ہو گا اور جب ایسا ہے تو اس نے ادا کی جیسی واجب ہوئی تھی۔ برخلاف دوسری نمازوں کے اس لئے کہ وہ کامل واجب ہوئی تھیں تو ناقض (وقت) کے ساتھ ادا نہ ہوں گی۔ مصنف نے فرمایا کہ نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت میں نفی مذکور سے مراد کراہت ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر مکروہ وقت میں نماز جنازہ پڑھی یا اس میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کی اور سجدہ کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ سجدہ تلاوت اور نماز جنازہ ناقص ادا کر دی گئی جیسے واجب ہوئی تھی۔ اس لئے کہ وجوب، جنازہ حاضر ہونے اور آیت سجدہ تلاوت کرنے سے ہوا ہے۔ تشریح مصنف نے کہا کہ اوقات ثلاثہ میں نہ نماز جنازہ پڑھے اور نہ سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔ دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی يعنى ان تقبر موتانا اور سجدہ تلاوت کے عدم جواز پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت نماز ہی کے معنی میں ہے بایں طور کہ جو شرطیں نماز میں ہیں طہارت، ستر عورت، استقبال قبلہ وغیرہ وہ سجدہ تلاوت میں بھی شرط ہیں۔ پس جب سجدہ تلاوت نماز کے معنی میں ہے تو وہ اوقات ثاثہ میں نہی عن الصلواۃ کے تحت داخل ہوگا۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے تُلثَةٌ أَوْ قَاتٍ نَهَانَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنْ تُصَلِّيَ فِيهَا - سوال : لیکن یہاں اشکال ہو گا وہ یہ کہ جب سجدہ تلاوت نماز کے ہم معنی ہے تو جس طرح قہقہہ لگا کر بننے سے وضو اور نماز دونوں باطل ہو جاتے ہیں اسی طرح سجدہ تلاوت میں قہقہہ لگا کر بننے سے وضو ٹوٹ جانا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ سجدہ تلاوت میں قہقہہ لگا کر بننے سے وضو نہیں ہو تا ۔ جواب: حدیث میں جس نماز میں قہقہہ کو ناقض وضو کہا گیا اس سے مراد تحریمہ اور رکوع سجدہ والی نماز ہے اور سجدہ تلاوت ایسا نہیں ہے اس لئے سجدہ تلاوت میں اگر قہقہہ لگایا تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا اور ان اوقات ثاثہ میں نماز پڑھنے سے اس لئے منع کیا گیا ہے تا کہ سورج پوجنے والوں کے ساتھ مشابہت لازم نہ آئے۔ شیخ ابو السن قدوری نے کہا کہ اوقات ثالثہ میں مطلقا نماز پڑھنا ممنوع ہے لیکن اسی دن کی عصر اس سے مستفی ہے یعنی اگر کسی نے عصر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی۔ یہاں تک کہ غروب کا وقت ہو گیا تو وہ اس دن کی عصر کی نماز غروب کے وقت پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ لیکن دوسری کوئی نماز یا کسی دوسرے روز کی عصر کی نماز اگر اس وقت میں پڑھنا چا ہے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ دلیل سے پہلے چند باتیں ذہن نشین کر لیجئے۔ یہ کہ نماز کے اوقات اس کے واجب ہونے کا سبب ہوتے ہیں۔ یہ کہ سبب مسبب سے مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ (۳) یہ کہ جیا سب ہوگاو سیاہی مسبب واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی سبب اگر کامل ہے تو مسبب بھی کامل واجب ہوگا اور اگر سب ناقص ہے تو مسبب بھی ناقص واجب ہوگا۔ ۴) یہ کہ نماز اگر کامل واجب ہوئی تو کامل ادا کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور اگر ناقص واجب ہوئی تو صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا کرنے سے بھی ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ اب دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہو گا کہ جو شخص غروب آفتاب کے وقت عصر کی نماز ادا کرتا ہے تو اس کے سبب میں تین احتمال ہیں:۔ ایک یہ کہ پورے وقت کو سبب قرار دیا جائے ، دوم یہ کہ وقت کا جو حصہ گذر چکا وہ سبب ہو ، ہوم یہ کہ جزء متصل لعلا داء سبب ہو سر اول کے دو احتمال باطل ہیں اس لئے کہ اگر پورے وقت کو سبب مانا جائے تو وقت کے بعد نماز ادا کرنا واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مسبب ، سبب سے مؤخر ہوتا ہے حالانکہ نماز وقت کے اندر واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ وقت کے بعد ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ پورا وقت، وجوب صلوۃ کا سبب نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرا احتمال اس لئے باطل ہے کہ اگر جزء ماضی یعنی گذرے ہوئے جز کو سبب مانا جائے تو جو شخص آخر وقت میں نماز پڑھے گا تو اس کو قضاء کرنے والا کہنا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ اس کو قضاء کرنے والا نہیں کہا جاتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ جو جز ء ادائے صلوۃ کے متصل ہے وہ وجوب صلوۃ کا سبب ہے اور مسئلہ مذکور میں جزء متصل للاداء وقت ناقص ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ وقت ( سبب ) اگر ناقص ہو تو نماز بھی ناقص ہی واجب ہوگی پس اس شخص پر جیسی نماز واجب ہوئی تھی ویسی ہی ادا کی ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ آج کی عصر غروب آفتاب کے وقت پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف دوسری نمازیں جو اس روز کی عصر کے علاوہ ہوں وہ غروب کے وقت ادا کرنے سے ادا نہ ہوں گی کیونکہ وہ نماز میں کے ادا ہو گی کیونکہ وہ بصفت کمال واجب ہوئی تھیں لہذا نا قص وقت کے ساتھ ادا نہ ہوں گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت میں جو جواز کی نفی کی گئی اس سے کراہت مراد ہے یعنی یہ دونوں ان اوقات میں مکروہ ہیں۔ حتی کہ اگر مکروہ وقت جنازہ آیا اور اسی مکر وہ وقت میں نماز جنازہ پڑھ لی، یا مکروہ وقت میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کر کے وقت مکروہ ہی میں سجدہ ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ کے واجب ہونے کا سبب جنازہ کا حاضر ہونا ہے اور سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہونے کا سبب آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کرنا ہے اور چونکہ یہ دونوں سبب وقت ناقص ( وقت مکروہ) میں پائے گئے اس لئے نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت بھی ناقص ہی واجب ہوں گے پس یہ دونوں جیسے واجب ہوئے تھے ویسے ہی ادا کر دئیے اس لئے ادا ہو گئے۔ اس کے بر خلاف فرائض کہ وہ ان اوقات شاھ میں جائز نہیں ہیں۔
Translation: And do not pray the funeral prayer due to this hadith which we narrated, and the prostration of recitation is also not permissible because the prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, except for the 'Asr of the same day at sunset. Because the cause is that part of the time which is present; because if the cause is related to the entire time, then performing it after the time would be obligatory. And if the cause is related to that part which has passed, then the one performing at the end of time would be a qada performer. And when that is the case, he has performed it as it was obligatory. Unlike other prayers, because they were obligatory as complete, so they will not be performed with an incomplete (time). The author said that in the negation mentioned regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, the meaning is karahah. Even if he performs the funeral prayer in a makruh time, or recites an ayah of sajdah and performs sajdah, it is permissible, because the prostration of recitation and funeral prayer are performed as incomplete as they were obligatory. Because the obligation arose from the presence of the funeral and from reciting the ayah of sajdah. Explanation: The author said that during the three times, do not perform funeral prayer nor prostration of recitation. The proof is the hadith that has passed, i.e., 'Do not bury your dead' and the proof for the impermissibility of prostration of recitation is that prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer in that the conditions of prayer—purity, covering the private parts, facing the qiblah, etc.—are also conditions in prostration of recitation. So when prostration of recitation is in the meaning of prayer, it will be included under the prohibition of prayer in the three times. Thus, the hadith is: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited us from praying in them.' Question: Here an objection arises that when prostration of recitation is equivalent to prayer, then just as laughing out loud invalidates both wudu and prayer, similarly, laughing out loud during prostration of recitation should break wudu. Yet, laughing out loud during prostration of recitation does not break wudu. Answer: In the hadith where laughing is said to be a nullifier of wudu, what is meant is the prayer with takbir tahrimah and ruku' and sajdah, and prostration of recitation is not like that. Therefore, if one laughs during prostration of recitation, wudu will not break. And the reason for prohibiting prayer during these times is to avoid resemblance to sun worshippers. Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that prayer is absolutely prohibited during the three times, but the 'Asr of the same day is exempted. That is, if someone did not pray 'Asr until the time of sunset, he can pray that day's 'Asr at the time of sunset. But no other prayer or 'Asr of another day is permissible at that time. Before the proof, keep a few things in mind: (1) That the times of prayer are the cause for its obligation. (2) That the cause precedes the effect. (3) That as is the cause, so is the effect obligatory. That is, if the cause is complete, then the effect is also obligatory as complete; and if the cause is incomplete, then the effect is also obligatory as incomplete. (4) That if prayer becomes obligatory as complete, then it is necessary to perform it completely; and if it becomes obligatory as incomplete, then performing it with the quality of incompleteness will also fulfill it. Now the gist of the proof is that the person who prays 'Asr at sunset, there are three possibilities regarding its cause: First, that the entire time is made the cause; second, that the portion of time that has passed is the cause; third, that the part connected to the performance is the cause. The first two possibilities are invalid because if the entire time is considered the cause, then performing the prayer after the time would be obligatory, because the effect is delayed from the cause, whereas prayer is obligatory within the time, not after. So it is known that the entire time is not the cause for the obligation of prayer. The second possibility is invalid because if the past part is considered the cause, then the person who prays at the end of time would be called a qada performer, whereas he is not called a qada performer. So it is established that the part connected to the performance is the cause for the obligation of prayer. And in the mentioned case, the part connected to performance is an incomplete time. And it has passed previously that if the time (cause) is incomplete, then prayer is obligatory as incomplete. So this person has performed the prayer as it was obligatory. Therefore, we say that praying today's 'Asr at sunset is permissible. Unlike other prayers besides that day's 'Asr, they will not be fulfilled by performing at sunset, because they were obligatory with complete quality, so they will not be performed with an incomplete time. The author of Hidayah says that in the negation of permissibility regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, the meaning is karahah. That is, both are makruh in these times. Even if the funeral occurs in a makruh time and he performs the funeral prayer in that same makruh time, or he recites an ayah of sajdah in a makruh time and performs the sajdah in that same makruh time, it will be permissible. The proof is that the cause for the obligation of funeral prayer is the presence of the funeral, and the cause for the obligation of prostration of recitation is reciting the ayah of sajdah. And since both causes occurred in an incomplete time (makruh time), therefore the funeral prayer and prostration of recitation also become obligatory as incomplete. So as they were obligatory, they have been performed, and thus they are fulfilled. Unlike the obligatory prayers, which are not permissible in these times.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion of the Hidayah's rulings on what prayers are permissible during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The author begins by stating the general ruling: funeral prayer and sajdah al-tilawah are not performed during these times, based on the hadith prohibiting burial of the dead at those times. However, an exception is made for the 'Asr prayer of the same day at sunset. The reasoning is detailed: the cause (sabab) for obligation of a prayer is the time, but for 'Asr at sunset, only a part of the time is present, which is an incomplete cause. Therefore, the obligation itself is incomplete, and performing it in that incomplete state fulfills it. For other prayers (like other missed prayers or the next day's 'Asr), the complete time has passed, so they are not valid at sunset. The author then clarifies that the prohibition of funeral prayer and sajdah is not absolute impermissibility but karahah (disliked). If one performs them in a makruh time, it is valid because their causes (presence of funeral, recitation of ayah) occur at that moment, making the obligation incomplete; thus performance with incompleteness suffices. The passage also addresses an objection: if sajdah tilawah is like prayer, why doesn't laughter break wudu? The answer is that the hadith about laughter nullifying wudu refers specifically to the formal prayer with takbir and bowing, not sajdah tilawah. The prohibition of prayer at these times is to avoid imitating sun-worshippers. This is a classic Hanafi position that distinguishes between complete and incomplete causes, a key principle in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that brings about the obligation; here, the time for prayer or the part of time.
جزء متصل للاداء (juz' muttasil li-al-adā'): The part of time immediately connected to the performance of the prayer; this is the effective cause for obligation when the full time is not present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the current day's 'Asr prayer permissible at sunset?
A) Because the hadith allows it
B) Because the cause for its obligation is the part of time connected to performance, which is incomplete
C) Because it is a sunnah prayer
D) Because one can always make up missed prayers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits 'Asr at sunset based on the reasoning that the cause is the part of time connected to performance, which is incomplete, rendering the obligation incomplete and performance valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
