Voluntary Prayers After Fajr and Asr: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on voluntary prayers and permissible acts after Fajr and Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr and distinguish between permissible and impermissible acts during these times.

Core Idea
After Fajr and Asr, only voluntary prayers are disliked; missed obligations, sajdah tilawah, and janazah are allowed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on performing prayers after the Fajr and Asr prayers. While voluntary prayers are considered makruh tahrimi, the school makes exceptions for missed obligatory prayers, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer. The reasoning centers on the nature of the prohibition: it is not because the time itself is inherently bad, but to ensure the time is reserved for the obligatory prayer of the period.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its default ruling
Identify the act: performing voluntary prayer (nafl) after Fajr and Asr. The default ruling is makruh tahrimi based on the hadith prohibition.
The term 'yata-naqqala' specifically refers to voluntary prayers.
2
Identify the exceptions mentioned
The text explicitly allows missed prayers (fawa'it), sajdah tilawah, and janazah prayer during these times.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (illah)
The karahah is due to the time being considered occupied by the current fard prayer, not an inherent evil in the time itself. Thus, obligations and wajib acts are not included.
The phrase 'ka al-mashghuli bihi' captures this legal fiction.
4
Apply the reasoning to tawaf rak'ahs and invalidated prayer
The text also mentions two rak'ahs of tawaf and a prayer invalidated after starting as permissible, because they have a basis in obligation or necessity.
The OCR is unclear, but the overall sense is that these are exceptions.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is prohibit all prayers (including qada) at these times; Hanafis allow obligations. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فجر اور عصر کے بعد نوافل کا حکم
وَ يَكْرَهُ أَن يَتَنَقَّلَ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ نَهى عَنْ ذلِكَ وَلَا بَأسَ بِأَنْ تُصَلِّيَ فِي هَذَيْنِ الْوَقْتَينِ الْفَوَائِتَ وَيُسْجَدَ لِلتِّلَاوَةِ وَيُصَلِّى عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ لِأَنَّ الْكَرَاهَةَ كَانَتْ لِحَقِّ الْفَرْضِ لِأَنَّ الْوَقْتَ كَالْمَشْغُولِ بِهِ لَا لِمَعْنَى فِى الْوَقْتِ فَلَمْ تَظْهَرُ فِى حَقِّ الْفَرَائِضِ وَفِيمَا وَجَبَ لِعَيْنِهِ كَسَجَدَةِ التِّلَاوَةِ وَظَهَرَ فِى حَقِّ الْمَنْدُورِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ وَجُوبُهُ بِسَبَبٍ مِنْ جِهَةٍ وَفِي حَقٌّ رَكْعَتَى الطَّرَافِ وَفِي الَّذِى شَرَعَ فِيهِ ثُمَّ أَفْسَدَهُ لِأَنَّ NON : وهو مُ الطَّافِ وَصِيَانَةُ المُؤدَى عَنِ الْبُطْلَانِ
ترجمہ اور فجر کے بعد نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو اور عصر کے بعد یہاں تک کہ آفتاب غروب ہو کیونکہ روایت کیا گیا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس سے منع کیا ہے اور کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ ان دونوں وقتوں میں قضا نمازیں پڑھے اور تلاوت کا سجدہ کرے اور جنازہ کی نماز پڑھے کیونکہ کراہت تو حق فرض کی وجہ سے تھی تا کہ پورا وقت گویا اسی وقت کے فرض میں مشغول ہو جائے ۔ نہ کہ کسی ایسے معنی
Translation: Ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr: And it is disliked (makruh) to perform voluntary prayers after Fajr until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited that. And there is no harm in praying missed prayers (fawa'it) in these two times, and performing prostration of recitation, and praying the funeral prayer, because the dislike (karahah) was due to the right of the obligatory prayer (i.e., to occupy the time with the current obligatory prayer), as the time is considered as occupied with it, not due to any inherent meaning in the time. So it does not appear in the case of obligatory prayers (missed ones) and what is obligatory due to itself (like prostration of recitation). And it appears in the case of voluntary prayers (mandub) because its obligation is attached to a cause from one aspect. And in the case of the two rak'ahs of tawaf, and in the case of one who has started a prayer and then invalidated it, because ... (text unclear) ... and safeguarding the performed act from nullification. Urdu: And after Fajr, performing voluntary prayers is makruh until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited that. And there is no harm in praying missed prayers (qada) in these two times, and performing prostration of recitation, and praying the funeral prayer, because the dislike was due to the right of the obligatory prayer, so that the entire time becomes as if occupied with the obligatory prayer of that time, not due to any other meaning.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of al-Hidayah on voluntary prayers (nawafil) after Fajr and Asr. The matn states that it is makruh to perform voluntary prayers after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset, based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited prayer at these times. However, it clarifies that this prohibition does not apply to missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it), prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The reason is that the karahah is not due to an inherent evil in the time itself, but rather to ensure that the time is devoted to the obligatory prayer of that period. Since the time is considered as 'occupied' by the obligatory prayer, voluntary prayers are disliked because they might distract from the obligation. But when one is performing a missed obligation, there is no such conflict because the obligation is already due. Similarly, sajdah tilawah and janazah prayer have their own causes and are not purely voluntary. The Urdu commentary reinforces this by explaining that the prohibition is to avoid resembling sun worshippers. The text also mentions the two rak'ahs of tawaf and the case of one who starts a prayer then invalidates it (possibly meaning he must finish it), but the OCR is unclear. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that the prohibition of prayer at these times is makruh tahrimi for nafl, but permissible for obligations and special acts like sajdah and janazah.

Key Terms
يَتَنَقَّلَ (yata-naqqala): To perform voluntary (nafl) prayers.
الفَوَائِتَ (al-fawā'it): Missed obligatory prayers that are made up (qada).
كَالْمَشْغُولِ بِهِ (ka al-mashghūli bihi): As if occupied with it; here, the time is considered as already occupied by the obligatory prayer, so nafl is discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is permissible to pray after Fajr prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) A two-rak'ah voluntary prayer for entering the mosque
B) The missed Fajr prayer (qada) from a previous day
C) Any nafl prayer
D) The witr prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows missed obligations, sajdah tilawah, and janazah after Fajr and Asr, restricting only purely voluntary prayers.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Voluntary Prayer After Fajr and Asr with Exceptions
Explaining the prohibition and exceptions with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr, identify the exceptions, and distinguish between wajib li dhatihi and wajib li ghayrihi.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr are disliked, but obligations that are wajib li dhatihi (like qada fard, sajdah tilawah, janazah) are exempt.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on praying after the obligatory Fajr and Asr prayers. While the general rule is that voluntary prayers are disliked during these times, there are important exceptions based on a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: whether an act is obligatory in itself (wajib li dhatihi) or becomes obligatory due to an external cause (wajib li ghayrihi). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr: they are makruh tanzih. Note the primary proof: the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
The ruling is not haram because the hadith is ahad.
2
Resolve the apparent conflict
Understand the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed after Asr. Learn the Hanafi reconciliation: those two rak'ahs were a make-up for missed sunnah of Zuhr and were specific to the Prophet.
This preserves the general prohibition for the Ummah.
3
Identify the exceptions
List the acts that are not disliked after Fajr and Asr: qada fard, sajdah tilawah, janazah. Note the common factor: they are wajib li dhatihi.
Their obligation is from Allah, not from the servant.
4
Distinguish wajib li dhatihi from wajib li ghayrihi
Learn the definition: wajib li dhatihi is obligatory in itself; wajib li ghayrihi is obligatory due to an external cause. Recognize that acts like nadhr, tawaf rak'ahs, and makeup of invalidated nafl are wajib li ghayrihi and thus remain disliked.
This distinction is crucial for applying the exception correctly.
5
Apply to new cases
Practice applying the rule: given a scenario, determine if the prayer is exempt from karahah based on its obligation type.
Use the examples from the practice tasks.

وَ رَكْعَتَانِ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ - یعنی دور کعتیں ہیں جن کو رسول اللہ سے نہیں چھوڑتے تھے نہ پوشیدہ اور نہ علانیہ دور کعتیں نماز صبحت پہلے اور دو رکعتیں نماز عصر کے ، بعد ۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے مَا كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَأْتِينِي فِي يَوْمٍ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ إِلَّا صَلَى رَكْعَتَين - مینی کبھی نہیں ہوا کہ رسول اللہ ۔ یقینی ہوا کہ میرے پاس آئے بعد عصر مگر دور کعتیں پڑھیں۔ ان دونوں ان دورکعتوں سے منع فرماتے تھے۔ چنانچہ علامہ ابن الہمام نے بخاری اور مسلم کے حوالہ سے پورا واقعہ اس طرح قلمبند کیا ہے: عَن كُرَيْبٍ مَوْلَى ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِى اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ عَبْدِ وَسَلْهَا عَنِ * الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ وَقُلْ بَلَغَنَا إِنَّكَ تُصَلِّيْنَهُمَا وَأنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْهُمَا قَالَ كَرَيْبٌ فَدَخَلْتُ عَلى عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهَا فَأَخْبَرْتُهَا فَقَالَتْ سَلْ أُمَّ سَلَمَةَ رَضِى الله تَعَالَى عَنْهَا فَرَجَعْتُ إِلَيْهم فَاَخَبَرْتُهُمْ فَرَدُّونِى إِلى أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ فَقَالَتْ أُمُّ سَلَمَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهى عَنْهَا ثُمَّ رَأَيْتُهُ يُصَلَّيْهَا فَقِيلَ لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ إِنَّهُ أَتَانِي نَاسٌ مِنْ عَبْدِ الْقَيْسِ بِالْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ قَوْمِهِمْ فَشَغَلُونِى الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ اللَّتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الظَّهْرِ وَهُمَا هَاتَانِ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ان دو وقتوں میں یعنی فجر کے بعد اور عصر کے بعد قضاء نمازیں پڑھنے اور سجدہ تلاوت کرنے اور نماز جنازہ پڑھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد کراہت فجر اور عصر کی نماز کی وجہ سے تھی تا کہ تمام وقت اسی وقت کے فرض میں مشغول ہو جائے۔ پس چونکہ کراہت حق فرض کی وجہ سے تھی لہذا حقیقت فرض کے حق میں کراہت ظاہر نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ حقیقت فرض کے ساتھ وقت کو مشغول کرنا اولی ہے بہ نسبت حق فرض کے ساتھ مشغول کرنے کے۔ اس لئے فرائض کے حق میں اور اس کے ہم معنیٰ ہے اس کے حق میں کراہت ظاہر نہیں ہوگی جیسے سجدہ تلاوت اس لئے کہ سجدہ تلاوت ذاتہ واجب ہے کیونکہ سجدہ تلاوت کا وجوب بندے کے فعل پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت جس طرح آیت سجدہ تلاوت کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح آیت سجدہ سننے سے بھی واجب ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ سنے کا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو لہذا سجدہ تلاوت واجب لذاتہ ہونے میں فرائض کے مانند ہو گیا۔ یہی حال نماز جنازہ کا ہے اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ کا وجوب بھی بندے کے فعل پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد نذر کی ہوئی نماز میں کراہت ظاہر ہوگی کیونکہ نذر کی ہوئی نماز واجب لذاتہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نذر کی نماز کا وجوب نذر کرنے والے کی طرف سے ہے۔ اور اسی طرح طواف کی دورکعتوں میں بھی کراہت ظاہر ہوگی۔ چنانچہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد ان کا ارادہ کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ ان دو رکعتوں کا وجوب طواف کرنے کی وجہ سے ہوا اور طواف کرنا اس کا اپنا فعل ہے۔ لہذا طواف کی دورکعتیں بھی واجب لذاتہ نہیں ہیں۔ اور اسی طرح اس نماز کے حق میں بھی کراہت ظاہر ہوگی جس کو شروع کر کے فاسد کر دیا مثلاً نما زنفل شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی۔ پھر اگر فجر یا عصر کے بعد اس کی قضا کرنا چاہے تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ نماز بھی لذاتہ واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ جو نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی اس کو بطلان سے بچانے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوئی ہے۔
Explanation of the issue: It is disliked (makruh) to pray voluntary prayers from after Fajr until sunrise and from after Asr until sunset. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Trustworthy men testified before me, and the most trustworthy among them to me was Umar, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade prayer after Fajr until the sun rises and after Asr until it sets.' (Agreed upon) Ibn Abbas says: 'Trustworthy beloved servants of truth testified before me, among whom the most beloved to me was Umar ibn al-Khattab, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade prayer after dawn until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets.' (Bukhari and Muslim) But the hadith of Aisha, narrated by the two Sahihs, contradicts it: 'Two rak'ahs which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) never omitted, secretly or openly: two rak'ahs before Fajr prayer and two rak'ahs after Asr.' And in another narration: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) never came to me on any day after Asr except that he prayed two rak'ahs.' These two hadiths indicate that he persisted in praying two rak'ahs after Asr. The answer is that the two rak'ahs after Asr were specific to him (peace be upon him); therefore, they are not permitted for his Ummah. The proof for this is that once after Zuhr, some people from Abd al-Qays came to him, and due to being occupied with them, he could not pray the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. So he prayed these two rak'ahs after Asr as compensation. And because his blessed habit was that whenever he performed an action, he would continue it, so he always prayed these two rak'ahs after Asr and forbade others from them. Thus, Allamah Ibn al-Humam recorded the complete incident with reference to Bukhari and Muslim: From Kuraib, the freed slave of Ibn Abbas, that Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abd al-Rahman ibn Azhar, and Miswar ibn Makhrama sent him to Aisha, wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), saying: 'Convey greetings to her from all of us and ask her about the two rak'ahs after Asr, and say: we have heard that you pray them, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade them.' Kuraib said: 'I went to Aisha and informed her. She said: Ask Umm Salamah. So I returned and informed them, and they sent me back to Umm Salamah. Umm Salamah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbid them. Then I saw him praying them. When asked, he said: Some people from Abd al-Qays came to me with Islam from their people, and they occupied me from the two rak'ahs after Zuhr, and these are those two.' (Bukhari in al-Maghazi) The author of al-Hidayah said: There is no harm in praying make-up prayers, performing the prostration of recitation, and praying the funeral prayer in these two times (i.e., after Fajr and after Asr). The proof is that the dislike after Fajr and Asr was due to the (obligatory) prayers of Fajr and Asr, so that the entire time would be occupied with the fard of that time. Since the dislike was due to the right of the fard, the dislike does not appear with respect to the essence of the fard itself, because occupying the time with the essence of the fard is more appropriate than occupying it with the right of the fard. Therefore, the dislike does not appear for fard prayers and what is equivalent to them, like the prostration of recitation, because the prostration of recitation is obligatory in itself (wajib li dhatihi), since its obligation is not dependent on the servant's action. The proof is that just as the prostration of recitation becomes obligatory by reciting a verse of prostration, it also becomes obligatory by hearing it, even if one did not intend to hear. Hence, the prostration of recitation becomes like fard in being wajib li dhatihi. The same applies to the funeral prayer, because its obligation is also not dependent on the servant's action. However, for a vowed prayer (salat al-nadhr) after Fajr and Asr, the dislike appears, because a vowed prayer is not obligatory in itself; rather, its obligation arises from the one who made the vow. Similarly, the two rak'ahs of tawaf are also disliked; indeed, intending them after Fajr and Asr is makruh, because the obligation of these two rak'ahs arises from performing tawaf, and tawaf is his own action. Therefore, the two rak'ahs of tawaf are also not obligatory in themselves. Likewise, the dislike appears for a prayer that one began and then invalidated, for example, by starting a voluntary prayer and invalidating it. Then if he wants to make it up after Fajr or Asr, it is makruh, because this prayer is not obligatory in itself but became obligatory due to saving the invalidated prayer from nullification.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, explains the ruling on praying after Fajr and Asr. The Hanafi position is that voluntary (nafl) prayers are disliked (makruh tanzih) during these two times. The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas narrated by Bukhari and Muslim, where the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. However, there is an apparent contradiction from Aisha's hadith that the Prophet regularly prayed two rak'ahs after Asr. The Hanafi response, following Ibn al-Humam's reconciliation, is that those two rak'ahs were specific to the Prophet (peace be upon him) because he was making up the missed sunnah of Zuhr. He did not intend them as voluntary prayers after Asr generally, and he forbade others from doing so. This shows that the prohibition remains for the Ummah. The passage then clarifies exceptions: make-up prayers (qada), the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) are not disliked because they are obligations that are obligatory in themselves (wajib li dhatihi). Their obligation comes from Allah directly, not from the servant's action. In contrast, vowed prayers (nadhr), the two rak'ahs after tawaf, and make-up of an invalidated voluntary prayer are disliked because they are obligatory due to an external cause (wajib li ghayrihi). The key principle is that the dislike after Fajr and Asr is intended to give priority to the fard of that time; any prayer that is more important or inherently obligatory takes precedence and is exempt from dislike.

Key Terms
کراہت (karahah): The legal ruling of dislike (makruh). In this context, it refers to the dislike of voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr.
واجب لذاتہ (wajib li dhatihi): An obligation that is obligatory in itself, not due to an external cause. Its obligation does not depend on a person's action; it is directly from Allah.
واجب لغیرہ (wajib li ghayrihi): An obligation that becomes obligatory due to an external cause, such as a vow, tawaf, or making up an invalidated prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After Fajr prayer, which of the following is NOT disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Praying the two rak'ahs of tawaf
B) Performing the make-up (qada) of a missed fajr prayer
C) Praying a vowed (nadhr) voluntary prayer
D) Praying the make-up of an invalidated nafl prayer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the dislike of prayer after Fajr and Asr does not apply to acts that are obligatory in themselves (wajib li dhatihi) such as missed fard prayers, sajdah tilawah, and janazah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Permissibility of Qada, Sajda, and Janaza After Fajr and Asr
Ruling with proof on permissibility of qada, sajda, janaza after Fajr/Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wajib lidhatihi and wajib li-ghayrihi and apply this distinction to determine which prayers are permissible after Fajr and Asr according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Prayers that are wajib lidhatihi are exempt from karahah after Fajr/Asr; incidental obligations are not.

This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi ruling regarding the permissibility of performing certain prayers after the Fajr and Asr prayers. While voluntary prayers are prohibited during these times, the Hidayah clarifies that acts of worship that are 'wajib lidhatihi'—obligatory in themselves, like missed fard prayers, sajda tilawat, and janaza—are exempt from this prohibition. The key is understanding the distinction between intrinsic and incidental obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exceptions
The text states that after Fajr and Asr, there is no harm in performing qada prayers, sajda tilawat, and janaza. However, nadhr prayers, tawaf rak'ahs, and qada of an invalidated nafl are makruh.
Focus on the list: permissible vs. disliked.
2
Understand the basis of the prohibition
The karahah after Fajr/Asr is due to the 'right of the fard' (haqq al-fard) of that time, i.e., to ensure the time is dedicated to the fard. This explains why the prohibition is not absolute.
The prohibition is not for the act itself but to prioritise the fard.
3
Grasp the key distinction: wajib lidhatihi vs. wajib li-ghayrihi
Acts that are wajib lidhatihi (intrinsically obligatory) have their obligation fixed by divine command, independent of the individual's action. Acts that are wajib li-ghayrihi (incidentally obligatory) become obligatory due to the individual's own action (e.g., vowing, doing tawaf).
Sajda tilawat and janaza are wajib lidhatihi; nadhr and tawaf rak'ahs are not.
4
Apply the distinction to the cases in the text
Sajda tilawat and janaza are wajib lidhatihi, so they are permissible after Fajr/Asr. Nadhr and tawaf rak'ahs are not, so they are makruh.
Check each case's source of obligation.
5
Test an additional case: qada of an invalidated nafl
If one starts a nafl prayer and invalidates it, making it up becomes wajib to 'save it from invalidity'. This obligation is incidental (li-ghayrihi), so it is also makruh after Fajr/Asr.
This confirms that only intrinsic obligations are exempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یعنی کریب مولیٰ ابن عباس سے روایت ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن عباس عبدالرحمن بن از ہر اور مسور بن مخرمہ نے مجھے ام المؤمنین عائشہ کی خدمت میں بھیجا کہ ہم سب کی طرف سے ام المومنین کی خدمت میں سلام پہنچا اور عصر کے بعد کی دورکعتوں کا حال دریافت کر اور عرض کر کہ ہم کو خبر پہنچی ہے کہ آپ ان کو پڑھا کرتی ہیں اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ کریب نے کہا کہ پھر میں نے ام المؤمنین عائشہ کی خدمت میں جا کر پیغام عرض کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تو جا کر ام سلمہ سے دریافت کرپس میں نے واپس ہو کر ان لوگوں کو خبر دی تو انہوں نے مجھے حضرت ام المؤمنین ام سلمہ کی خدمت میں بھیجا پس ام سلمہ نے فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے سنا کہ آپا نے عصر کے بعد نماز سے ممانعت فرمائی ۔ پھر میں نے دیکھا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دورکعتیں پڑھیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے اس بارے میں عرض کیا گیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ میرے پاس عبد القیس کے کچھ لوگ آ گئے اپنی قوم کی طرف سے اسلام لانے کے ساتھ تو ظہر کے بعد کی دورکعتوں کے پڑھنے سے مجھے مشغول کر دیا اور یہ وہی دو رکعتیں ہیں ۔ ( بخاری فی المغازی)
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ان دو وقتوں میں یعنی فجر کے بعد اور عصر کے بعد قضاء نمازیں پڑھنے اور سجدہ تلاوت کرنے اور نماز جنازہ پڑھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد کراہت فجر اور عصر کی نماز کی وجہ سے تھی تا کہ تمام وقت اسی وقت کے فرض میں مشغول ہو جائے۔ پس چونکہ کراہت حق فرض کی وجہ سے تھی لہذا حقیقت فرض کے حق میں کراہت ظاہر نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ حقیقت فرض کے ساتھ وقت کو مشغول کرنا اولی ہے بہ نسبت حق فرض کے ساتھ مشغول کرنے کے۔ اس لئے فرائض کے حق میں اور جھر اس کے ہم معنیٰ ہے اس کے حق میں کراہت ظاہر نہیں ہوگی جیسے سجدہ تلاوت اس لئے کہ سجدہ تلاوت لذاتہ واجب ہے کیونکہ سجدہ تلاوت کا وجوب بندے کے فعل پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔
اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت جس طرح آیت سجدہ تلاوت کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح آیت سجدہ سننے سے بھی واجب ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ سنے کا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو لہذا سجدہ تلاوت واجب لذاتہ ہونے میں فرائض کے مانند ہو گیا۔
یہی حال نماز جنازہ کا ہے اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ کا وجوب بھی بندے کے فعل پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد نذر کی ہوئی نماز میں کراہت ظاہر ہوگی کیونکہ نذر کی ہوئی نماز واجب لذاتہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نذر کی نماز کا وجوب نذر کرنے والے کی طرف سے ہے۔
اور اسی طرح طواف کی دورکعتوں میں بھی کراہت ظاہر ہوگی۔ چنانچہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد ان کا ارادہ کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ ان دو رکعتوں کا وجوب طواف کرنے کی وجہ سے ہوا اور طواف کرنا اس کا اپنا فعل ہے۔ لہذا طواف کی دورکعتیں بھی واجب لذاتہ نہیں ہیں۔ اور اسی طرح اس نماز کے حق میں بھی کراہت ظاہر ہوگی جس کو شروع کر کے فاسد کر دیا مثلاً نماز نفل شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی۔ پھر اگر فجر یا عصر کے بعد اس کی قضا کرنا چاہے تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ نماز بھی لذاتہ واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ جو نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی اس کو بطلان سے بچانے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوئی ہے۔
From Kuraib, the freed slave of Ibn Abbas: Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abdur-Rahman ibn Azhar, and Miswar ibn Makhrama sent me to Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha to convey their greetings and ask about the two rak'ahs after Asr, and to say that they heard she prays them while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade them. Kuraib said: So I went to Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha and delivered the message. She said: Go and ask Umm Salama. So I returned and informed them, and they sent me to Umm Salama. She said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbidding prayer after Asr. Then I saw him pray two rak'ahs, and when asked about it, he said: Some people from Abdul Qais came to me to embrace Islam, and they occupied me from praying the two rak'ahs after Zuhr, so these are the two (I prayed now). (Bukhari in Al-Maghazi)
The author of Al-Hidayah said: In these two times, i.e., after Fajr and after Asr, there is no harm in performing qada prayers, sajda tilawat, and janaza prayer. The proof is that the dislike (karahah) after Fajr and Asr was due to the right of the fard of that time, so that the entire time would be occupied with the fard. Since the karahah was due to the right of the fard, therefore the karahah does not appear regarding the essence of the fard itself, because occupying the time with the essence of the fard is more preferable than occupying it with the right of the fard. Therefore, in the case of fara'id and what is synonymous with it, karahah does not appear, like sajda tilawat, because sajda tilawat is wajib lidhatihi (obligatory in itself) since its obligation is not dependent on the action of the servant.
Another proof is that just as sajda tilawat becomes wajib by reciting a verse of sajda, similarly it becomes wajib by hearing it, even if one did not intend to hear. Thus, sajda tilawat became like fara'id in being wajib lidhatihi.
The same applies to janaza prayer because its obligation is also not dependent on the action of the servant. However, after Fajr and Asr, a prayer made by nadhr (vow) does have karahah, because a nadhr prayer is not wajib lidhatihi; its obligation comes from the one who vowed.
Similarly, the two rak'ahs of tawaf also have karahah. Thus, intending them after Fajr and Asr is makruh, because their obligation is due to performing tawaf, and tawaf is the person's own act. Therefore, the two rak'ahs of tawaf are not wajib lidhatihi. Likewise, karahah appears for a prayer that was begun and then invalidated, e.g., if one starts a nafl prayer and invalidates it, then if he wishes to make it up after Fajr or Asr, it is makruh because this prayer is not wajib lidhatihi but became wajib due to saving it from invalidity.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of certain prayers after Fajr and Asr. It begins by narrating a hadith from Bukhari showing that the Prophet forbade voluntary prayer after Asr, but he himself prayed two rak'ahs that were actually qada of Zuhr's sunnah. Then the author of Al-Hidayah states the ruling: qada prayers, sajda tilawat, and janaza prayer are not disliked after Fajr and Asr. The reasoning is that the prohibition (karahah) in these times is due to the right of the fard of that time—to ensure the time is devoted to the fard. Since the fard itself takes precedence over its right, performing an act that is wajib lidhatihi (essential obligatory) does not conflict with that right. Acts like sajda tilawat and janaza are wajib lidhatihi because their obligation is fixed by divine command, not dependent on the individual's action (e.g., hearing a sajda verse makes sajda wajib regardless of intent). In contrast, prayers that are wajib but not lidhatihi—such as a nadhr prayer (vowed) or the two rak'ahs of tawaf (obligated due to the act of tawaf)—are still makruh in these times because their obligation stems from the individual's own doing. Similarly, making up an invalidated nafl prayer is also makruh. The key distinction is whether the obligation is intrinsic (lidhatihi) or incidental (li-ghayrihi).

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory or sunnah prayer after its time.
سجدہ تلاوت (sajda tilawat): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of sajda; wajib lidhatihi.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship; the vowed act becomes wajib but not lidhatihi.
واجب لذاتہ (wajib lidhatihi): An obligation inherent to the act itself, not dependent on external factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sajda tilawat permissible after Fajr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is a sunnah, not a fard.
B) Because it is wajib lidhatihi, similar to fard.
C) Because it is short and does not delay the fard.
D) Because the Prophet himself performed it after Fajr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits qada, sajda tilawat, and janaza after Fajr and Asr because they are wajib lidhatihi; nadhr and tawaf prayers are subject to karahah.

Prohibition of Nafl After Fajr Beyond Two Rak'ahs
Ruling that only two rak'ahs of sunnah are allowed after true dawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayers after true dawn and explain the proof from the Prophet's consistent practice.

Core Idea
After true dawn, only the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr are allowed; extra nafl is makruh tanzihi.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that after subh sadiq (true dawn), no voluntary prayer beyond the two rak'ahs of sunnah should be performed. The text from Al-Hidayah provides a clear ruling with a strong proof from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this ruling helps us follow the sunnah in our daily prayer schedule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (legal classification)?
Here the act is performing voluntary prayers after true dawn; the ruling is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Is it from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas?
The proof is from the Prophet's practice (fi'li sunnah): he did not exceed two rak'ahs despite his eagerness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? What is the legal link?
The Prophet's consistent omission in the presence of ability and eagerness indicates that doing more is contrary to the better practice, hence makruh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? What is their basis?
Some other schools allow voluntary prayer at this time, citing general permission for nafl.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why?
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi because it is based on a strong inductive evidence from the Prophet's consistent action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبح صادق کے بعد دورکعتوں سے زائد نوافل مکروہ ہیں
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَتَنَقَّلَ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ بِأَكْثَرِ مِنْ رَكْعَتَيْنِ الْفَجْرِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَزِدُ عَلَيْهِمَا مَعَ حِرْصِهِ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ
ترجمہ اور طلوع فجر کے بعد فجر کی دورکعتوں سے زائد نوافل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان دو رکعتوں پر زیادہ نہیں کیا، باوجود یکہ آپ نماز کے بہت شوقین تھے ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ اور اس کی دلیل واضح ہے۔
After true dawn, performing more than two rak'ahs of nafl is makruh. And it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers after dawn more than the two rak'ahs of Fajr, because he (peace be upon him) did not increase beyond them despite his eagerness for prayer. Translation: And after the rising of dawn, performing nafl beyond the two rak'ahs of Fajr is disliked because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not exceed them, even though he was very keen on prayer. Commentary: The scenario and its proof are clear.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling: after true dawn (subh sadiq) and before the Fajr fard, only the two rak'ahs of sunnah (sunnat al-fajr) are allowed. Any additional voluntary prayers are makruh. The proof is from the Prophet's practice: despite his eagerness for prayer, he never prayed more than these two rak'ahs at that time. This indicates that the encouraged practice is limited to that, and exceeding it is disliked. The commentary simply notes that the proof is obvious.

Key Terms
تنفل (tatawwu'): Performing voluntary (nafl) prayers.
رکعتا الفجر (rak'ata al-fajr): The two sunnah rak'ahs before the Fajr fard.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but contrary to the better practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on performing four rak'ahs of nafl after true dawn?
A) Mustahab
B) Mubah
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
After true dawn, the Prophet's practice teaches us to limit voluntary prayer to the two sunnah rak'ahs; exceeding them is makruh tanzihi.

Prohibition of Nafl After Maghrib Before Fard and During Friday Sermon
Ruling with proof for two prohibited times for nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl after Maghrib before fard and during the Friday khutbah, and explain the reason (ta'lil) for each prohibition.

Core Idea
Performing nafl when it delays an obligatory act is makruh tahrimi.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two specific times when voluntary prayers (nafl) become disapproved. While nafl is generally recommended, the Hanafi school identifies situations where it conflicts with more important obligations: delaying the Maghrib prayer and missing the Friday sermon. Understanding these rulings helps prioritize obligatory acts over supererogatory ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited scenarios
Read the text and note the two cases: (1) nafl after sunset before the Maghrib fard, and (2) nafl during the Friday khutbah from when the imam steps out until he finishes.
The prohibition is specific to these two situations.
2
Extract the underlying reason (ta'lil)
For Maghrib, the reason is that it delays the Maghrib prayer, which is mustahabb to perform early. For the khutbah, the reason is that it distracts from listening to the khutbah, which is wajib.
The prohibition is based on the principle that obligatory acts take precedence over voluntary ones.
3
Understand the level of prohibition
The text uses 'makruh' but the Hanafi school classifies this as makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it involves delaying or missing a wajib act.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram in terms of sin, though the act itself is still valid if performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مغرب کے بعد فرائض سے پہلے نوافل کا حکم
وَلَا تَنفَّلَ بَعْدَ الْغُرُوبِ قَبْلَ الْفَرَضِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَأْخِيرِ الْمَغْرِبِ وَلَا إِذَا خَرَجَ الْإِمَامُ لِلْخُطْبَةِ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ إِلَى أَنْ يَفْرَغَ مِنْ خُطْبَتِهِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الِاشْتِغَالِ عَنِ اسْتِمَاعِ الْخُطْبَةِ
ترجمہ اور غروب کے بعد فرض سے پہلے نفل نہ پڑھے کیونکہ اس میں مغرب کو مؤخر کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ جمعہ کے دن جب امام خطبہ کے لئے نکلے تب بھی نفل نہ پڑھے یہاں تک کہ وہ خطبہ سے فارغ ہو۔ کیونکہ نفل پڑھنے میں خطبہ کی طرف کان لگا کر سننے سے اعراض کر کے دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہونا لازم آتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سورج چھپنے کے بعد فرض ادا کرنے سے پہلے نفل نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں مغرب کو مؤخر کرنا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ مغرب میں تعمیل مستحب ہے۔
اور اسی طرح اس وقت نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے جبکہ امام خطبہ کے لئے نکلا یہاں تک کہ امام خطبہ سے فارغ ہو جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں خطبہ سننے سے اعراض کرنا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ خطبہ سنا واجب ہے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Ruling on nafl before fard after Maghrib: And do not perform nafl after sunset before the fard because it necessitates delaying Maghrib; nor when the Imam comes out for the khutbah on Friday until he finishes his khutbah, because it involves engaging away from listening to the khutbah.
Translation: After sunset, do not pray nafl before the fard because it entails delaying Maghrib; on Friday when the Imam comes out for the khutbah, do not pray nafl until he finishes the khutbah, because praying nafl involves turning away from listening to the khutbah and engaging in other business.
Commentary: The issue is that it is disliked to pray nafl after sunset before performing the fard. The proof is that doing so would necessitate delaying Maghrib, whereas hastening to perform Maghrib is mustahabb. Similarly, it is disliked to pray nafl when the Imam has come out for the khutbah until he finishes, because it necessitates turning away from listening to the khutbah, whereas listening to the khutbah is wajib. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage covers two separate rulings on khiyar al-majlis. First, it is makruh to perform optional prayers after sunset before the Maghrib fard, because that would delay the obligatory prayer, and hastening to perform Maghrib is recommended (mustahabb). Second, it is makruh to pray any nafl during the Friday khutbah from the time the imam steps out until he finishes, because it distracts from listening to the khutbah, which is wajib. Both rulings are based on preventing delay or distraction from obligatory acts.

Key Terms
مغرب (maghrib): The sunset prayer; the time is brief so delaying is discouraged.
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before Friday prayer; listening is wajib.
استماع (istima'): Listening attentively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is nafl before Maghrib fard makruh according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the time for Maghrib is too short.
B) Because it delays the Maghrib prayer, which should be performed early.
C) Because the Prophet never prayed nafl after sunset.
D) Because it is a time of shaytan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits nafl after Maghrib before fard and during Friday khutbah to prevent delay and distraction from obligatory acts.

The Legislation (Mashru'iyyah) of the Adhan
Explains the origin and legal establishment of the call to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main narrations regarding the origin of the adhan and explain why the Hanafi school considers it a sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
The adhan is a divinely established sunnah mu'akkadah, specific to this ummah as a congregational call.

This lesson traces the historical and legal origin of the call to prayer (adhan). The passage presents multiple narrations—from revelation on the night of Isra' to the prophetic dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd—and clarifies the Hanafi school's reliance on sound evidence. Understanding this history helps you appreciate that the adhan is not a human invention but a commanded act of worship, with its legal status as a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the adhan (call to prayer). In the Hanafi school, its ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for men for the five daily prayers and jumu'ah.
Sunnah mu'akkadah means it is highly recommended; omitting it without reason is disliked but not sinful.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage cites a hadith from al-Daraqutni that Jibril commanded the Prophet with the adhan when prayer was made obligatory, and the Prophet's own teaching of the adhan to Bilal. However, these narrations are considered weak by some scholars like Hafiz Ibn Hajar.
The primary basis for the Hanafi position is the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd and Umar, confirmed by the Prophet, which is treated as a form of ilham (divine inspiration).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The dream, combined with the Prophet's endorsement ('Indeed this is true') and his order to Bilal to call the adhan, establishes the legitimacy and source of the adhan. This shows that divine guidance can come through dreams (ru'ya) when confirmed by prophetic authority.
The Hanafi usul accepts the Prophet's approval of a Companion's action as a form of sunnah (taqrir).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on whether the adhan was first prescribed in Makkah (based on Isra' narrations) or in Madinah (based on the dream story and historical context). The passage also notes that Hafiz Ibn Hajar declared the Makkan narrations unsound, while other scholars accept them.
The practical ruling (mufta bihi) is unaffected by this historical detail; the adhan is established regardless.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the more authentic dream incident and the practical implementation in Madinah. The weaker narrations do not undermine the established practice. The adhan remains a distinctive feature of the Muslim ummah, not found in previous religions.
The author concludes with 'Wa Allahu a'lam', indicating humility before differing opinions.

دار قطنی میں حدیث انس ہے کہ ان جبريل أَمَرَ النَّبِي بِالْأَذَانِ حِيْنَ فُرِضَتِ الصَّلوةُ یعنی جس وقت نماز فرض کی گئی اس وقت حضرت جبریل نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو اذان کا حکم دیا۔ ان دونوں روایات سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اذان ہجرت سے پہلے مکہ میں مشروع ہو گئی تھی لیکن حافظ ابن حجر نے ان احادیث کی عدم صحت کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔
مولا نا عبد الشکور صاحب لکھنوی نے علم الفقہ میں لکھا ہے کہ اذان کی ابتداء مدینہ منورہ میں [اٹھ؟] میں ہوئی۔ اس سے پہلے نماز بے اذان کے پڑھی جاتی تھی چونکہ اس وقت تک مسلمانوں کی تعداد کچھ ایسی کثیر نہ تھی۔ اس لئے ان کا جماعت کے لئے جمع ہو جانا بغیر کسی اطلاع کے دشوار نہ تھا۔ جب مسلمانوں کی تعداد [یو ما فیونا؟] ترقی کرنے لگی اور مختلف طبقات کے لوگ جوق در جوق اسلام میں داخل ہونے لگے تو اس امر کی ضرورت پیش آئی کہ نماز کا وقت آنے اور جماعت قائم ہونے کی اطلاع ان کو دی جائے جس سے وہ اپنے اپنے قریب و بعید مقامات سے جماعت کے لئے مسجد میں آسکیں۔ لہذا اذان کا یہ طریقہ اس غرض کے پورا کرنے کے لئے مقرر کیا گیا ، اور اذان اسی امت کے لئے خاص ہے پہلی امتوں میں نہ تھی۔
اذان کی مشروعیت کا واقعہ: اذان کی مشروعیت کا مختصر قصہ یہ ہے کہ جب صحابہ کو نماز اور جماعت کے اوقات کی اطلاع کی ضرورت محسوس ہوئی تو انہوں نے آپس میں مشورہ کیا ۔ بعض نے رائے دی کہ یہود کی طرح سنکھ بجایا جائے ، بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ آگ جلا دی جایا کرے۔ مگر نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو پسند نہیں فرمایا۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے یہ رائے دی کہ نماز کے وقت الصلوة جَامِعَة کہہ دیا جائے ۔ اس کے بعد عبد اللہ بن زید اور حضرت فاروق اعظم نے خواب دیکھا کہ ایک فرشتہ نے یہ طریقہ اذان کا جو آگے بیان کیا جائے گا۔ ان کو تعلیم کیا کہ اس طریقہ سے نماز کے اوقات اور جماعت کی اطلاع مسلمانوں کو کی جایا کرے۔ بعض روایات میں ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن زید فرماتے تھے کہ اگر مجھے بدگمانی کا خوف نہ ہوتا تو میں کہتا کہ میں بالکل سوتا ہی نہ تھا اسی لحاظ سے بعض علماء نے اس واقعہ کو حال اور کشف پر محمول کیا ہے [جوار باب باطن؟] کو حالت بیداری میں ہوتا ہے۔ المختصر صبح کوعبداللہ بن زید نے یہ واقعہ حضور نبوی علیہ اتحیہ والتسلیم میں عرض کیا تب حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بے شک یہ سچ ہے، اور حضرت بلال کو حکم ہوا کہ اسی طرح اذان دیا کرو۔
پھر فاروق اعظم نے بھی آکر اپنے خواب کو بیان کیا۔ بعض روایات میں ہے کہ اس سے پہلے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر وحی بھی نازل ہو چکی تھی ۔ چنانچہ عبد الرزاق نے اپنے مصنف میں اور ابو داؤد نے مراسیل میں یہ روایت لکھی ہے۔
بعض احادیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ شب معراج میں نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کو حضرت جبریل نے اذان کی تعلیم دی تھی مگر یہ احادیث صحیح نہیں اور بر تقدیر صحت اس میں وہ شب معراج مقصود نہیں جو مکہ میں ہوئی تھی کیونکہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کو روحانی معراج بار ہا ہوئی ہے۔ لہذا اس سے مقصود وہی رات ہوگی جس رات کو یہ خواب دیکھا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم
Book of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 1. He taught it to Bilal, meaning on the night of al-Isra', Allah revealed the adhan to the Prophet, so the Prophet descended with it and taught it to Bilal. In al-Daraqutni, the hadith of Anas: 'Indeed Jibril commanded the Prophet with the adhan when prayer was made obligatory,' i.e., when prayer was obligated, Jibril commanded the Prophet regarding the adhan. From both these narrations it is known that the adhan was prescribed in Makkah before the Hijrah, but Hafiz Ibn Hajar claimed these hadiths are unsound. Maulana Abdul Shakoor Sahib Lakhnawi wrote in 'Ilm al-Fiqh that the beginning of the adhan occurred in Madinah in [??]. Before that, prayer was performed without adhan because the number of Muslims at that time was not so large; thus their gathering for congregation without any notice was not difficult. When the number of Muslims [??] began to increase and people of different classes entered Islam in droves, the need arose to inform them of the prayer time and the establishment of the congregation, so that they could come from near and far to the mosque for congregation. Therefore this method of adhan was established to fulfill this purpose, and the adhan is specific to this nation; it was not in previous nations. The incident of the prescription of adhan: the brief story of the prescription of adhan is that when the Companions felt the need to be informed of the times of prayer and congregation, they consulted among themselves. Some suggested blowing a horn like the Jews, some said they should light a fire. But the Prophet did not approve of that. Umar suggested saying 'al-salat jami'ah' at the time of prayer. After that, Abdullah ibn Zayd and Umar saw a dream that an angel taught them this method of adhan, which will be explained later, that by this method the times of prayer and congregation should be announced to the Muslims. In some narrations, Abdullah ibn Zayd used to say: 'If I were not afraid of suspicion, I would say that I was not asleep at all.' Accordingly, some scholars considered this incident as a state of kashf (unveiling) which occurs in wakefulness [??]. In short, in the morning Abdullah ibn Zayd presented this incident to the Prophet, who said: 'Indeed this is true,' and Bilal was ordered to give the adhan in this manner. Then Umar also came and narrated his dream. Some narrations say that revelation had already descended upon the Prophet before this. Thus Abd al-Razzaq recorded it in his Musannaf and Abu Dawud in his Marasil. Some hadiths also mention that on the night of Mi'raj, Jibril taught the Prophet the adhan, but these hadiths are not authentic. If authentic, it does not refer to the night of Mi'raj that occurred in Makkah, because the Prophet had multiple spiritual ascents. So it refers to the same night as the dream. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah, explaining the legislation (mashru'iyyah) of the adhan. The author begins by presenting two narrations: one that the Prophet taught Bilal the adhan after it was revealed on the night of al-Isra', and another from al-Daraqutni that Jibril commanded the Prophet with the adhan when prayer was made obligatory. These indicate that the adhan was prescribed in Makkah before the Hijrah. However, Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, a Shafi'i scholar, claimed these narrations are unsound. Then the author presents the view of Maulana Abdul Shakoor Lakhnawi, who wrote in 'Ilm al-Fiqh that the adhan began in Madinah in the [year?]. He explains that before the Hijrah, the number of Muslims was small, so they could gather for prayer without notification. When the Muslim community grew, the need for a call to prayer arose. The adhan is specific to the Muslim ummah; it was not a practice of previous nations. The author then narrates the well-known incident of the prescription of adhan: the Companions consulted, suggesting a horn or fire, but the Prophet disapproved. Umar suggested 'al-salat jami'ah'. Then Abdullah ibn Zayd and Umar both dreamed of an angel teaching the adhan. The Prophet confirmed the dream's truth and ordered Bilal to call the adhan. Some later scholars considered this dream as kashf (spiritual unveiling) in wakefulness. The author also notes that some weak narrations connect the adhan to the night of Mi'raj, but he argues that even if authentic, it refers to a spiritual ascent different from the one in Makkah. The passage concludes with 'Wa Allahu a'lam' (And Allah knows best).

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The Islamic call to prayer consisting of specific phrases announced to indicate the time of salah and gather the congregation.
مشروعیت (mashru'iyyah): The legal legitimacy or prescription of an act by the Shari'ah; here referring to the initial legislation of the adhan.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah; an act that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, leaving it without excuse is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which event is considered the most reliable basis for the legislation of the adhan?
A) The Prophet teaching Bilal on the night of Isra'
B) The dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd and Umar confirmed by the Prophet
C) The suggestion of Umar to say 'al-salat jami'ah'
D) The consensus of the Companions in Madinah

Key Takeaway
The adhan is a sunnah mu'akkadah established through the Prophet's confirmation of a divinely inspired dream, making it a unique and permanent practice of the Muslim ummah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Virtues of the Adhan - The Mu'adhdhin's Lofty Rank
Lists hadiths highlighting the excellence and rewards of the adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least three hadith-based virtues of the adhan and explain the high rank of the mu'adhdhin in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The adhan is a supreme act of worship with immense eschatological rewards, elevating the mu'adhdhin beside prophets and martyrs.

The adhan is not merely a call to prayer; it is a powerful dhikr that manifests Islam's glory. The Prophet (peace be upon him) repeatedly emphasized its virtues, from protection from Hell to special honor on the Day of Judgment. This lesson explores ten hadiths that demonstrate why the mu'adhdhin holds such a lofty station.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Nature
Recognize that the adhan is a form of dhikr (remembrance) that includes the testimony of tawhid and risalah. It is a communal sunnah (sunnah kifayah) in the Hanafi school.
The adhan is not obligatory on every individual, but its performance brings immense reward.
2
List the Virtues from Each Hadith
Go through each of the ten hadith summaries in the passage. For each, extract the specific reward or benefit promised to the mu'adhdhin, e.g., testimony of hearers, entry after prophets, safety from Hell, etc.
The hadiths are from authentic sources like Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Classify the Hadith Sources
Note the compilers mentioned (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah). This establishes the authenticity and reliability of the virtues.
All these are from the major hadith collections, giving strength to the proofs.
4
Analyze the Common Theme
Observe that the virtues consistently elevate the mu'adhdhin to a high status in the Hereafter: intercession, exemption from fear, and proximity to prophets and martyrs.
The theme is that adhan is not just a worldly announcement but a cause of salvation.
5
Apply to Hanafi Fiqh
Understand that these virtues encourage the practice of adhan. In the Hanafi school, the adhan is a sunnah mu'akkadah for congregations, and the mu'adhdhin should be chosen for piety and trustworthiness.
The reward is tied to sincere intention (niyyah), as highlighted in the hadith about seven years.

اذان کی اہمیت و عظمت اذان اللہ تعالیٰ کے اذکار میں ایک بہت بڑے رتبہ کا ذکر ہے۔ اس میں توحید و رسالت کی شہادت اعلان کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اس سے اسلام کی شوکت ظاہر ہوتی ہے۔ بہت سی احادیث میں اذان کی فضیلت مذکور ہے۔
1 اذان کی آواز جہاں تک پہنچتی ہے اور جو لوگ اس کو سنتے ہیں جن ہوں یا انسان ، وہ سب قیامت کے دن اذان دینے والے کے ایمان کی گواہی دیں گے۔ (بخاری ، نسائی ، ابن ماجہ )
( اللہ کے بچے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ انبیاء اور شہداء کے بعد اذان دینے والے جنت میں داخل ہوں گے بعض احادیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ مؤذن کا مرتبہ شہید کے برابر ہے۔ ۳) یتیم عبداللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کہا کہ جو شخص سات برس تک برابر اذان دے اور اس سے اس کا مقصود محض ثواب ہو تو اس کے لئے دوزخ سے آزادی لکھ دی جاتی ہے۔ (ابو داؤد، ترمندی)
نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اگر لوگوں کو معلوم ہو جائے کہ اذان کہنے میں کس قدر ثواب ہے اور پھر ان کو یہ منصب بغیر قرعہ ڈالنے نہ ملے تو بے شک وہ اس کے لئے قرعہ ڈالیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس منصب کے لئے سخت کوشش کریں۔ ( بخاری، مسلم، ترمذی ، نسائی ) صحابہ کے زمانے میں ایسا ہوا ہے کہ اذان کے لئے لوگوں میں اختلاف ہوا، ہر شخص چاہتا تھا کہ یہ مبارک منصب مجھے ملے یہاں تک کہ قرعہ ڈالنے کی نوبت آئی۔ (تاریخ بخاری ) (۵ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے: ” بروز قیامت تین لوگ معطر مشک کے نیلے پر ہوں گے نہ حساب دیں گے، نہ حیران و پریشان ہوں گے۔ ایک وہ جس نے رضائے خداوندی کے لئے قرآن پڑھا، دوسرا وہ جو غلامی میں مبتلا ہوتے ہوئے آخرت کے اعمال سے غافل نہ رہا، تیسرا مؤذن۔ (المرشد الامین ) (1) قیامت کے دن مؤذنوں کو بھی شفاعت کی اجازت دی جائے گی کہ وہ اپنے اعزاء واحباب یا جس کے لئے چاہیں خداوند عالم سے سفارش کریں۔
۷) اذان دیتے وقت شیطان پر بہت خوف اور ہیبت طاری ہوتی ہے اور بہت بے حواسی سے بھاگتا ہے جہاں تک اذان کی آواز جاتی ہے وہاں نہیں ٹھہرتا۔ ( بخاری ، مسلم ) (۸) قیامت کے دن مؤذنوں کی گرد میں بلند ہوں گی یعنی وہ نہایت معزز اور لوگوں میں ممتاز ہوں گے اور قیامت کے خوف اور مصیبت سے محفوظ رہیں گے۔ (۹) جس مقام پر اذان دی جاتی ہے وہاں اللہ تعالیٰ کی رحمت نازل ہوتی ہے ، عذاب اور بلاؤں سے وہ مقام محفوظ رہتا ہے۔ (10) نبی نے مؤذنوں کے لئے دعائے مغفرت فرمائی ہے۔
The importance and greatness of the adhan: the adhan is a very great remembrance among the remembrances of Allah. In it, testimony of tawhid and risalah is made with proclamation; it manifests the glory of Islam. Many hadiths mention the virtue of adhan. (1) The voice of the adhan reaches wherever it reaches, and whoever hears it, whether jinn or humans, they will all testify to the faith of the caller on the Day of Judgment. (Bukhari, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah). (2) The Messenger of Allah said that after prophets and martyrs, the callers to prayer will enter Paradise. Some hadiths also mention that the rank of the mu'adhdhin is equal to that of a martyr. (3) [Abdullah?] said that whoever calls the adhan continuously for seven years with the sole intention of reward, freedom from Hellfire is recorded for him. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). (4) The Prophet said: 'If people knew the reward in calling the adhan, and then they could not get this office without casting lots, they would definitely cast lots for it.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i). In the time of the Companions, people disputed over the adhan, each wanting this blessed office, until it came to casting lots. (Tarikh Bukhari). (5) The Messenger of Allah said: 'On the Day of Resurrection, three persons will be on a hill of fragrant musk; they will not be held to account, nor will they be confused and distressed: one who recited the Qur'an for the pleasure of Allah, one who while in slavery did not neglect the deeds of the Hereafter, and the mu'adhdhin.' (Al-Murshid al-Amin) (6) On the Day of Judgment, the mu'adhdhins will be permitted to intercede; they may intercede with Allah for their relatives and friends or whomever they wish. (7) At the time of calling the adhan, great fear and awe falls upon Satan, and he flees in great confusion; wherever the sound of the adhan reaches, he does not stay. (Bukhari, Muslim). (8) On the Day of Judgment, the necks of mu'adhdhins will be raised high, meaning they will be highly honored and distinguished among people, and they will be safe from the fear and hardship of that Day. (9) Wherever the adhan is called, Allah's mercy descends, and that place is protected from punishment and calamities. (10) The Prophet has prayed for forgiveness for the mu'adhdhins.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths expounding on the virtues (fada'il) of the adhan. The commentary highlights that the adhan is a great dhikr that includes the testimony of tawhid and risalah, showcasing the grandeur of Islam. The author then lists ten specific virtues from reliable hadith sources: (1) All beings that hear the adhan will testify for the caller on Judgment Day. (2) The caller enters Paradise after prophets and martyrs, and his rank is equal to a martyr. (3) Calling adhan for seven years with sincere intention guarantees freedom from Hell. (4) The reward is so great that people would cast lots for the opportunity. (5) On the Day of Resurrection, three categories of people (including the mu'adhdhin) will be on a hill of musk, exempt from accounting. (6) Mu'adhdhins are granted permission to intercede. (7) Satan flees in fear when he hears the adhan. (8) Mu'adhdhins will have their heads raised high, honored and safe from terror. (9) Mercy descends and protection is granted to the place where adhan is called. (10) The Prophet supplicated for forgiveness for mu'adhdhins. These hadiths encourage the practice and emphasize its spiritual significance.

Key Terms
مؤذن (mu'adhdhin): The person who calls the adhan; the office of the caller to prayer.
فضیلت (fadilat): Virtue, excellence, or superior reward as mentioned in the hadiths regarding the adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted in the passage, which three persons will be on a hill of fragrant musk on the Day of Judgment?
A) The Prophet, the mu'adhdhin, and the martyr.
B) One who recited Qur'an for Allah's pleasure, a slave mindful of the Hereafter, and the mu'adhdhin.
C) The mu'adhdhin, the scholar, and the just ruler.
D) The one who prayed all night, the one who fasted all year, and the mu'adhdhin.

Key Takeaway
The adhan is a highly virtuous act; the mu'adhdhin holds a special rank in the Hereafter, next to prophets and martyrs, with the power to intercede and be safe from the terror of that Day.

The Virtues and Excellence of Adhan
Lists hadith-based virtues of the call to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five hadith-based virtues of the adhan and explain their significance in encouraging the practice.

Core Idea
The adhan carries immense reward, including forgiveness, intercession, and protection from Hellfire.

This passage presents a collection of hadith that highlight the extraordinary virtues of the call to prayer (adhan). These narrations serve as motivation for Muslims to appreciate and uphold this sunnah. While not a legal ruling, the virtues demonstrate the high status of the mu'adhdhin and the blessings associated with the adhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify Each Virtue
Read through the passage and list each distinct virtue mentioned (there are ten numbered points). Note the key reward or blessing described.
Some virtues are stated explicitly, others are implied; capture the essence.
2
Note the Hadith Sources
For each virtue, check which hadith collections are cited (e.g., Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This helps assess the reliability and context.
The passage often groups multiple sources for one virtue.
3
Recognize the Common Theme
Identify the overarching themes: forgiveness, honor, intercession, protection from Hell, and the high rank of the mu'adhdhin.
These themes encourage Muslims to value the adhan.
4
Reflect on Practical Implications
Consider how these virtues should influence a Muslim's attitude toward the adhan. Should one rush to respond, respect the mu'adhdhin, or desire to give the call?
The Companions drew lots to gain this role, showing its desirability.
5
Summarize the Overall Lesson
Condense the main takeaway: the adhan is a highly rewarding act that brings worldly and hereafter blessings.
This is not a legal ruling but a motivational foundation.

The Book of Salah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume One. The importance and greatness of Adhan. Adhan is a remembrance of Allah of a very high rank. In it, the testimony of tawhid and risalah is announced, showing the might of Islam. Many hadith mention the virtue of Adhan. 1) The sound of Adhan reaches wherever it goes, and those who hear it, jinn or humans, will all testify to the faith of the one who gave the call on the Day of Judgment. (Bukhari, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah) 2) The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said that after the prophets and martyrs, those who give the call to prayer will enter Paradise. In some hadith, it is also said that the rank of the mu'adhdhin is equal to that of a martyr. 3) 'Abdullah (the orphan?) said that whoever gives the call to prayer regularly for seven years with the sole intention of reward, freedom from Hell is written for him. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) 4) The Prophet, peace be upon him, said that if people knew how much reward there is in giving the call to prayer, and if they could not obtain this position without drawing lots, they would surely draw lots for it. The conclusion is that they should strive hard for this position. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) During the time of the Companions, people differed over who would give the call to prayer; everyone wanted this blessed position until it came to drawing lots. (Tarikh al-Bukhari) 5) The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'On the Day of Judgment, three people will be on a mound of fragrant musk; they will not be held to account, nor will they be bewildered and troubled. One is the one who recited the Qur'an for the pleasure of Allah, the second is the one who was afflicted with slavery but did not neglect acts of the Hereafter, and the third is the mu'adhdhin.' (Al-Murshid al-Amin) 6) On the Day of Judgment, the mu'adhdhins will be allowed to intercede; they may intercede with Allah for their relatives and friends or whomever they wish. 7) When the call to prayer is given, Satan is overcome with great fear and terror and flees in panic; he does not stay where the sound of the call reaches. (Bukhari, Muslim) 8) On the Day of Judgment, the necks of the mu'adhdhins will be raised high, meaning they will be greatly honored and distinguished among people, and they will be safe from the fear and calamity of that Day. 9) Wherever the call to prayer is given, the mercy of Allah descends, and that place is protected from punishment and afflictions. 10) The Prophet prayed for forgiveness for the mu'adhdhins.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith-based virtues of the Adhan (call to prayer) taken from various sources. It serves as an introduction to the legal discussion that follows, highlighting the high status of the Adhan and the reward for those who perform it. The author lists ten distinct points: (1) the testimony of creation on the Day of Judgment, (2) entering Paradise after prophets and martyrs, (3) freedom from Hell for seven years of consistent Adhan, (4) the eagerness of the Companions to obtain this position, (5) the honor of being among three types of people on a mound of musk, (6) permission for intercession, (7) causing Satan to flee, (8) raised status on the Day of Judgment, (9) descent of mercy and protection from calamity, and (10) the Prophet's prayer for forgiveness. These virtues are meant to encourage the practice of Adhan and establish its importance in the Islamic tradition.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, a worship involving specific phrases.
مؤذن (mu'adhdhin): The person who gives the call to prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He will not be allowed to intercede for anyone.
B) He will be allowed to intercede for his relatives and friends.
C) He will be the first to enter Paradise.
D) He will be questioned about his intention.

Key Takeaway
The adhan is a highly rewarded act that brings forgiveness, intercession, and divine mercy, encouraging Muslims to uphold it diligently.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Legal Status of Adhan: Sunnah or Wajib?
State the ruling that Adhan is sunnah and address the wajib view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the legal status of Adhan, explain the evidence from mutawatir practice and hadith, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi wajib argument.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib — the Prophet's practice proves it, and fighting for abandonment is about disdain, not obligation.

This lesson examines a key ruling in salah: the legal status of the call to prayer (Adhan). The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, but some earlier scholars argued it is wajib. By analyzing the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the response to the wajib argument, you will understand why the sunnah position is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (Adhan) and the hukm level stated: sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, not for other prayers.
The ruling is explicitly stated in the matn of al-Hidayah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is the mutawatir practice of the Prophet — he consistently had Adhan called for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, but never for other prayers like Eid or eclipse.
Mutawatir practice yields certain knowledge.
3
Examine the supporting hadith
Two hadith are cited: Jabir ibn Samurah testifies that Eid prayers were without Adhan or Iqamah; Aisha reports that for solar eclipse, only 'al-salat jami'ah' was called, not the full Adhan.
These ahadith are ahad but their meaning is decisive (dalala qati).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi wajib argument
Some mashayikh argue that Adhan is wajib based on Imam Muhammad's report: if a whole city abandons Adhan, they should be fought. Fighting is normally for abandoning a wajib, not a sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The commentator refutes the wajib argument by explaining that the fighting is not for abandoning a sunnah per se, but for the disdain (istikhfaf) of religion that results from persistent abandonment. Thus, Adhan remains sunnah.
The tarjih is that the sunnah position is mufta bihi.

اذان کے مسنون ہونے پر نقل متواتر دلیل ہے یعنی توتر کے ساتھ یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پانچوں نمازوں اور جمعہ کے لئے اذان دلوائی ہے ان کے علاوہ وتر ، عیدین، کسوف، خسوف، استسقاء، نماز جنازہ اور سنن و نوافل کے لئے اذان نہیں دلوائی ہے۔ چنانچہ مسلم میں جابر بن سمرہ کی روایت ہے صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ الْعِيدَ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ وَلَا مَرَّتَيْنِ بِغَيْرِ أَذَانٍ وَلَا إِقَامَةٍ یعنی میں نے متعدد بار حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ عید کی نماز بغیر اذان اور بغیر اقامت کے پڑھی۔

صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اذان کی کیفیت معلوم ہے اور وہ اسی طرح ہے جیسے آسمان سے نازل شدہ فرشتہ نے اذان دی تھی ۔ اس کی تفصیل عبد اللہ بن زید کی حدیث میں گذر چکی۔ حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں: عَنْ مُعَاذِ بْنِ جَبَلٍ قَالَ قَامَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ يَعْنِى إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ فِي النَّوْمِ كَانَ رَجُلًا نَزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ عَلَيْهِ بُرْدَانِ أَخْضَرَانِ أَنْزَلَ عَلَى جَزْمِ حَائِطٍ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ فَأَذَّنَ مَثْنَى مَثْنَى ثُمَّ جَلَسَ ، قَالَ أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنِ عَيَّاشٍ عَلَى نَحْوِ أَذَانِنَا الْيَوْمَ قَالَ عَلِّمُهَا بِلاَلاً فَقَالَ عُمَرُ رَأَيْتُ مِثْلَ الَّذِي رَأَى وَلَكِنَّهُ سَبَقَنِي ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ یہ کون سا فرشتہ تھا تو علامہ بدر الدین عینی نے کہا کہ اظہر یہ ہے کہ یہ جبریل امین تھے اور بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ یہ کوئی دوسرا فرشتہ تھا۔
Their legal status. The Adhan is a sunnah for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, not for others, due to the mutawatir practice. And the description of Adhan is well-known, and it is as the angel descending from heaven gave the call. Translation: Adhan is sunnah for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, not for others, due to mutawatir practice. And the method of Adhan is known, and it is as the angel descending from heaven gave the call. Commentary: Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah for the five prayers and Jumu'ah. Some mashayikh said it is wajib because it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if all the people of a city agree to abandon the Adhan, they will be fought. And it is apparent that fighting is for abandoning a wajib, not a sunnah. So it shows Adhan is wajib. The answer is that Adhan is sunnah, but insistence on abandoning it leads to disdain of the religion, and in case of disdain, fighting is necessary. Therefore Imam Muhammad ordered fighting. The proof that Adhan is sunnah is the mutawatir practice, meaning it is established with tawatur that the Prophet, peace be upon him, had the call given for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, and he did not have it given for other prayers such as Witr, the two Eids, eclipse prayers, prayer for rain, funeral prayer, and supererogatory prayers. Thus, in Muslim, the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah: 'I prayed with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, the Eid prayer many times without Adhan and without Iqamah.' And from Aisha: 'The sun was eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah, so he sent a caller to call 'Prayer in congregation.' From these two hadith, it is understood that there was no Adhan for the Eids and the eclipse prayer. And as for Witr, even though it is wajib, the Adhan of Isha is sufficient for it because its time is the same as Isha. As for supererogatory prayers, they are dependent on the obligatory prayers, so there is no need for a separate Adhan. Regarding Jumu'ah, the hadith of Sa'ib ibn Yazid is in the Sahihain. The author of Hidayah said that the manner of Adhan is known, and it is as the descending angel gave the call. Its detail has passed in the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid. The words of the hadith are: From Mu'adh ibn Jabal, he said: A man from the Ansar, Abdullah ibn Zaid, stood up to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I saw in a dream a man descending from heaven wearing two green garments; he descended on the wall of Madinah and gave the Adhan in pairs, then sat down.' Abu Bakr ibn 'Ayyash said: 'Similar to our Adhan today.' He said: 'Teach them to Bilal.' 'Umar said: 'I saw similar to what he saw, but he preceded me.' As for which angel it was, 'Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni said that the most apparent is that it was Jibril Amin, and some scholars opined that it was another angel.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the legal status of Adhan. It begins with the matn of al-Hidayah stating that Adhan is a sunnah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah only, due to the mutawatir practice (i.e., the continuous practice of the Prophet). The Urdu commentary then clarifies that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The commentator introduces an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some mashayikh (scholars) consider it wajib based on a report from Imam Muhammad that if an entire city abandons Adhan, they should be fought. Since fighting is only for abandoning a wajib, this suggests Adhan is wajib. The commentator refutes this by explaining that the fighting is not for abandoning a sunnah per se, but for the disdain (istikhfaf) of the religion that results from persistent abandonment. The proof for sunniyyah is the mutawatir practice, supported by specific hadith: Jabir ibn Samurah testifies to the absence of Adhan for Eid prayers, and Aisha describes the practice for solar eclipse where only 'al-salat jami'ah' was called. The passage also addresses why Witr does not have its own Adhan (the Isha Adhan covers it) and why supererogatory prayers do not need one. Finally, it recounts the dream of Abdullah ibn Zaid which established the wording of Adhan, confirming its divine origin, with a note on the identity of the angel.

Key Terms
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah, regularly practiced by the Prophet and recommended to be performed.
متواتر (mutawatir): A narration transmitted by so many chains that collusion on a lie is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which of the following prayers is Adhan prescribed according to the Hanafi school?
A) The five daily prayers and Jumu'ah
B) The five daily prayers, Jumu'ah, and Eid prayers
C) All obligatory prayers including Witr and Eid
D) Only the five daily prayers

Key Takeaway
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, and the evidence from mutawatir practice and hadith supports this, while the wajib argument is refuted by distinguishing between the act itself and disdain for religion.

Ruling on Tarjīʿ in Adhān: A Hanafi-Shāfiʿī Dispute
Hanafi denial of tarjīʿ and rebuttal of Shāfiʿī view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tarjīʿ in adhān, evaluate the Shāfiʿī proof, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Tarjīʿ in adhān is not from the sunnah; the well-known hadiths override the incident of Abū Mahdhūrah.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shāfiʿī schools regarding the adhān: whether the two testimonies should be repeated softly then loudly (tarjīʿ). The Hanafi school holds that tarjīʿ is not part of the adhān, while the Shāfiʿīs consider it prescribed. We will analyse the proofs on both sides and understand why the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Define tarjīʿ and the Hanafi position
Tarjīʿ means repeating the shahādatayn twice softly then twice loudly. The Hanafi ruling is that this is not part of the prescribed adhān.
2
Examine the Shāfiʿī proof
Imam al-Shāfiʿī relies on the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah, where the Prophet apparently taught him to repeat the testimonies. Understand the wording and its apparent meaning.
Hadith narrated by Muslim.
3
Analyse the Hanafi textual evidence
The well-known (mashhūr) hadiths on adhān, such as those of Ibn ʿUmar and ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd, contain no tarjīʿ. These are more authoritative because they are widely transmitted.
Ibn ʿUmar's hadith: adhān was two by two without repetition of shahādatayn.
4
Interpret the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah
Hanafis argue the repetition was a teaching incident, not legislation. Abū Mahdhūrah was shy and lowered his voice; the Prophet made him repeat loudly. It was not meant to be a general practice.
Also, a contradictory narration in Ṭabarānī omits tarjīʿ, causing both to be dropped per Ibn al-Humām.
5
Apply the rational argument
The core purpose of adhān is the phrases Hayya ʿalā al-ṣalāh and Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ, which have no repetition. A fortiori, other phrases should not have repetition.
This is a qiyas argument: if the most important parts have no tarjīʿ, less important ones also should not.
6
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafis, the shahādatayn are said twice audibly; according to Shāfiʿīs, they are said four times (two softly, two loudly).
This difference affects how the adhān is performed in each school.
