(رواه مسلم) اس حدیث سے جہاں شہادتین کا چار بار کہنا ثابت ہوتا ہے اسی کے ساتھ یہ بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ تکبیر یعنی اللہ اکبر شروع میں دو مرتبہ ہے۔ حضرت امام مالک شروع میں اللہ اکبر دو بار کہنے پر اسی حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ لیکن ابوداؤ داور نسائی نے اللہ اکبر کا چار بار کہنا روایت کیا ہے جو ہمارا مستدل ہے اور مسلم کی روایت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اللہ اکبر دو مرتبہ ایک سانس میں کہنا کلمہ واحدہ کے مانند ہے پس مسلم کی روایت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابو محذورہ کو اذان کی تعلیم دی اور دو مرتبہ اللہ اکبر کہا یعنی دو سانس میں چار مرتبہ اللہ اکبر کہا۔ اس تاویل کے بعد دونوں روایتوں میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں رہا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اذان کے بیان میں جو احادیث مشہور ہیں ان میں ترجیع نہیں ہے منجملہ ان میں سے عبد اللہ بن زید بن عبد ربہ اور عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیثیں ہیں ان میں ترجیع نہیں ہے چنانچہ ابن عمر کی حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں قَالَ إِنَّمَا كَانَ الْأَذَانُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ مرتين مرتين وَالْإِقَامَةُ مَرَّةً مَرَّة - مَرَّتَينِ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اذان حی علی الصلوۃ اورجی علی الفلاح ہے اور ان دو کلموں میں ترجمیع نہیں لہذا ان دونوں کے علاوہ میں بدرجہ اولیٰ ترجیع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور ابو محذورہ کی حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابو محذورہ سے ان کلمات کو بار بار کہلوانا بطور تعلیم کے تھا۔ ابومحذورہ نے اس کو تر جمیع خیال کیا یعنی ابومحذورہ نے شہادتین کے ساتھ اس قدر آواز بلند نہیں کی تھی جس قدر اللہ کا رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم چاہتا تھا اس لئے دوبارہ لوٹا دیا تا کہ بلند آواز سے کہے اس کو ابو محذورہ نے گمان کیا کہ مجھے ہمیشہ پست آواز کے ساتھ کہنے کے بعد بلند آواز سے کہنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے یہیں تاویل کی ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابومحذورہ کو ایک حکمت کی وجہ سے ترجیع کا حکم دیا تھا۔ حکمت یہ تھی کہ ابومحذورہ مسلمان ہو گئے تو اللہ کے سچے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابو محذورہ کو اذان کا حکم دیا۔ ابو محذورہ جب کلمات شہادت پر پہنچے تو اپنی قوم سے حیا اور شرم کے پیش نظر اپنی آواز کو پست کیا۔ پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابو محذورہ کو بلایا اور ان کی گوش مالی کی اور ان سے فرمایا کہ ان کلمات کو لوٹاؤ اور ان کے ساتھ اپنی آواز کو بلند کرو۔ اب اس اعادہ سے یا تو اس بات کی تعلیم دینی مقصور تھی کہ حق بات کہنے میں کوئی حیا اور شرم نہیں، یا یہ مقصود تھا کہ کلمات شہادت کے تکرار سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ ابو محذورہ کی محبت میں مزید اضافہ ہو جائے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ طبرانی میں ابو محذورہ نے ایک روایت کی ہے جس میں ترجیع نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ابو محذورہ کی دونوں روایتیں متعارض ہوں گی۔ پس تعارض کی وجہ سے دونوں روایتیں ساقط ہو جائیں گی۔ اور ابن عمر اور عبد اللہ بن زید کی حدیث جو معارض سے سلامت ہے وہ قابل عمل ہوگی۔ نیز عدم ترجمیع کا قول اس لئے بھی رائج ہو گا کہ اذان کے باب میں عبداللہ بن زید بن عبدربہ کی حدیث اصل ہے اور اس میں ترجیع نہیں ہے۔
And there is no tarjīʿ in it, and it is that you repeat and raise your voice with the two testimonies after lowering them. And al-Shāfiʿī said that there is tarjīʿ in it because of the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah that the Prophet ordered him with tarjīʿ. And our evidence is that there is no tarjīʿ in the well-known (hadiths), and what he (Abū Mahdhūrah) narrated was teaching, so he thought it was tarjīʿ. Commentary: The form of tarjīʿ in adhān is to pronounce the two testimonies four times: first twice softly, then twice loudly. According to us, there is no tarjīʿ in adhān. Imam al-Shāfiʿī is of the view of tarjīʿ, deducing from the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah: that the Prophet taught him the adhān: Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar, Ashhadu an lā ilāha illallāh, Ashhadu an lā ilāha illallāh, Ashhadu anna Muḥammadan Rasūlullāh, Ashhadu anna Muḥammadan Rasūlullāh, then he returns and says Ashhadu an lā ilāha illallāh twice, Ashhadu anna Muḥammadan Rasūlullāh twice, Hayya ʿalā al-ṣalāh... (narrated by Muslim). From this hadith, besides the four-time testimony, it is also established that the takbīr (Allahu Akbar) is twice at the beginning. Imam Mālik deduces from this hadith for saying Allahu Akbar twice at the beginning. But Abū Dāwūd and al-Nasā’ī narrated four times for Allahu Akbar, which is our proof. And the response to Muslim’s narration is that saying Allahu Akbar twice in one breath is like a single word, so the meaning of Muslim’s narration is that the Prophet taught Abū Mahdhūrah the adhān and said Allahu Akbar twice — meaning four times in two breaths. After this interpretation, there is no contradiction between the two narrations. Our evidence is that the hadiths well-known concerning adhān do not have tarjīʿ; among them are the hadith of ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd ibn ʿAbd Rabbih and ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿUmar, in which there is no tarjīʿ. Indeed, the wording of Ibn ʿUmar’s hadith is: He said: The adhān was only on the time of the Messenger of Allah two by two, and the iqāmah once each. And the rational evidence is that the purpose of adhān is Hayya ʿalā al-ṣalāh and Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ, and there is no tarjīʿ in these two phrases; so a fortiori there is no tarjīʿ in other than them. And the response to the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah is that causing him to repeat those words was by way of teaching; Abū Mahdhūrah thought it was tarjīʿ — meaning Abū Mahdhūrah did not raise his voice with the two testimonies as much as the Messenger of Allah wanted, so he repeated them back so that he would say them loudly. Abū Mahdhūrah thought he had been ordered to always say them softly then loudly. Imam al-Ṭaḥāwī gave this interpretation. The author of al-ʿInāyah wrote that the Prophet ordered Abū Mahdhūrah with tarjīʿ for a wisdom: the wisdom was that when Abū Mahdhūrah became Muslim, the true Messenger of Allah ordered him with adhān. When Abū Mahdhūrah reached the words of testimony, he lowered his voice out of shame and modesty before his people. So the Prophet called Abū Mahdhūrah, pinched his ear, and told him: Repeat these words and raise your voice with them. So this repetition was either to teach that there is no shame in speaking the truth, or to increase Abū Mahdhūrah’s love for the Messenger of Allah through repetition of the words of testimony. ʿAllāmah Ibn al-Humām said that al-Ṭabarānī has a narration from Abū Mahdhūrah without tarjīʿ, so his two narrations are contradictory; due to contradiction, both narrations are dropped. And the hadith of Ibn ʿUmar and ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd, which is safe from contradiction, is operative. Also, the view of no tarjīʿ becomes prevalent because in the chapter of adhān, the hadith of ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd ibn ʿAbd Rabbih is the foundation, and it has no tarjīʿ.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning tarjīʿ in the adhān. The author clarifies that Hanafis hold there is no tarjīʿ, while Shāfiʿīs maintain it. The term tarjīʿ is defined: repeating the two testimonies (shahādatayn) twice softly and then twice loudly. The Shāfiʿī proof is the hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah, where the Prophet apparently taught him tarjīʿ. The Hanafi response is twofold: naqlī (textual) and ʿaqlī (rational). Textually, the well-known aḥādīth on adhān (like those of Ibn ʿUmar and ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd) do not contain tarjīʿ. The hadith of Abū Mahdhūrah is interpreted as teaching, not as a prescribed sunnah — the repetition was to correct his voice out of shyness. Rationally, the core purpose of adhān is the phrases Hayya ʿalā al-ṣalāh and Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ, which have no repetition; therefore other phrases should not have it. The author also notes that Ibn al-Humām points to a contradiction in Abū Mahdhūrah's own narrations (via al-Ṭabarānī), which causes both to be dropped. Thus the non-tarjīʿ position stands, supported by the foundational hadith of ʿAbdullāh ibn Zayd.

Key Terms
ترجیع (tarjīʿ): In adhān, repeating the two testimonies (shahādatayn) twice in a lowered voice and then twice in a raised voice.
شہادتین (shahādatayn): The two testimonies: 'Ashhadu an lā ilāha illā Llāh' and 'Ashhadu anna Muḥammadan Rasūlullāh'.
مشہور (mashhūr): Well-known and widely transmitted hadiths that are relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on tarjīʿ in the adhān?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is mubah.
C) It is not part of the adhān.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tarjīʿ is not part of the adhān, based on well-known hadiths and rational analogy; the Shāfiʿī proof is interpreted as a teaching incident and is overridden.

beginner

Addition in Fajr Adhān: al-Ṣalātu Khayrun min al-Nawm
Ruling and proof for the phrase in Fajr adhān

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhān, identify its evidence from the Sunnah, and explain why it is specific to Fajr.

Core Idea
The phrase 'Prayer is better than sleep' is recommended only in Fajr adhān, based on the Prophet's approval of Bilāl's wording.

This lesson examines a distinctive feature of the Fajr adhān: the addition of 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' (Prayer is better than sleep). According to the Hanafi school, this inclusion is mustaḥabb (recommended), not obligatory. We will explore the hadith of Bilāl that serves as the primary evidence and understand why this phrase is uniquely prescribed for the pre-dawn prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The passage states that in the Fajr adhān, after 'Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ', the phrase 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' is added twice. The Hanafi school rules this addition as mustaḥabb (recommended).
2
Identify the evidence
The proof is the hadith of Bilāl: when Bilāl said this phrase upon finding the Prophet sleeping, the Prophet approved and instructed him to include it in his adhān.
The hadith is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Analyse the command
The Prophet's statement 'Make it part of your adhān' (ijʿalhu fī adhānika) is an imperative. In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarina indicating recommendation. Here, the context of praise shows it is mustaḥabb, not wajib.
This usul principle explains why the addition is not obligatory.
4
Understand the specificity
The addition is specific to Fajr because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so the extra reminder is prescribed to wake people for prayer.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In practice, the mu'adhdhin says the standard adhān, and after 'Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ', says 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' twice, then continues with the final tahlīl. This phrase is not included in other adhāns.

وَيَزِيدُ فِي آذَانِ الْفَجْرِ بَعْدَ الْفَلَاحِ اَلصَّلوةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ مَرَّتَينِ لِأَنَّ بِلَالاً قَالَ الصَّلوةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ حِينَ وَجَدَ النبى عَلَيْهِ السَّلام راقدًا فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلام مَا اَحْسَنَ هَذَا يَابِلَالُ اجْعَلْهُ فِى أَذَانِكَ وَخُصَّ الفَجُرُ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ وَقْتُ نَوْم وَ غَفْلَةٍ ترجمہ اور فجر کی اذان میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد دوبار الصلوۃ خیر من النوم بڑھائے کیونکہ بلال نے جس وقت حضور کو سونا پایا تو کہا تھا الصلواة خير من النوم ۔ پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اے بلال یہ بہت خوب ہے اس کو اپنی اذان میں داخل کر اور فجر اس کے ساتھ مخصوص ہوئی کیونکہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے۔ تشریح فرمایا کہ فجر کی اذان میں حتَّى عَلَى الفلاح کے بعد دوبار الصلوةُ خَيْرٌ مِّنَ النَّوْمِ کا اضافہ کرے اور یہ اضافہ مستحب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک روز حضرت بلال نے نماز فجر کے لئے اذان دی۔ پھر حضرات عائشہ کے حجرے کے دروازے پر آکر کہا الصَّلوةُ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ ( ) حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا کہ اَلرَّسُولُ نَائِمٌ رسول اللہ سور ہے ہیں ۔ پھر بلال نے کہا: الصَّلوةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ ۔ پس جب آپ بیدار ہو گئے تو ام المؤمنین حضرت عائشہ نے آپ کو مطلع کیا آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کلمہ کو پسند فرمایا اور کہا کہ بلال اس کو اپنی اذان میں داخل کر لو۔ رہی یہ بات کہ یہ زیادتی فجر کی اذان کے ساتھ کیوں خاص ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے اس لئے یہ زیادتی فجر کی اذان کے ساتھ خاص کی گئی۔
And he adds in the adhān of Fajr after al-falāh: al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm twice, because Bilāl said al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm when he found the Prophet sleeping. So the Prophet said: How excellent this is, O Bilāl! Make it part of your adhān. And Fajr is specified with it because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness. Translation: And in the adhān of Fajr, after Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ, he adds twice 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' because Bilāl said 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' when he found the Prophet sleeping. So the Prophet said: O Bilāl, this is very good; include it in your adhān. And Fajr is specified with it because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness. Commentary: He says that in the Fajr adhān, after Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ, one adds 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' twice, and this addition is mustaḥabb. The evidence is that one day Bilāl gave the adhān for Fajr prayer, then came to the door of ʿĀ’ishah’s room and said: al-ṣalātu yā Rasūlallāh. ʿĀ’ishah said: al-Rasūlu nā’im (the Messenger is sleeping). Then Bilāl said: al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm. When the Prophet awoke, ʿĀ’ishah informed him, and the Prophet liked this phrase and told Bilāl to include it in his adhān. As for why this addition is specific to Fajr, the answer is that it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so this addition is specified for the Fajr adhān.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the unique phrase in the Fajr adhān. The author states that in the Fajr adhān, after the phrase 'Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ', one adds 'al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm' twice. This addition is mustaḥabb (recommended). The proof is the hadith of Bilāl: when he gave the Fajr adhān and saw the Prophet sleeping, he said the phrase, and the Prophet approved and instructed him to include it in his adhān. The reason Fajr is singled out is that it is a time when people are sleeping and heedless, so the reminder is especially needed. The Hanafi school considers this addition specific to Fajr and does not apply it to other adhāns.

Key Terms
الصلوۃ خير من النوم (al-ṣalātu khayrun min al-nawm): The phrase 'Prayer is better than sleep' added specifically in the Fajr adhān after 'Hayya ʿalā al-falāḥ'.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate the adhān.

Iqamah is Like Adhan: The Hanafi Position and Refutation of the Shafi'i View
States the Hanafi ruling on iqamah and refutes the Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqamah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of the angel.

Core Idea
Iqamah is recited like adhan — all phrases twice — as taught by the angel, and the Shafi'i view is refuted by interpreting the Anas hadith differently.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the iqamah, the second call to prayer. Both schools agree on the adhan's repetition, but they differ on the iqamah. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the angel who descended to teach the iqamah to a companion. We will analyze the proof and the refutation of the Shafi'i view that iqamah is recited singly except for 'qad qamat al-salah'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that iqamah is identical to adhan in repetition: all phrases are recited twice, with the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' after 'hayya ala al-falah'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that iqamah phrases are recited singly except for 'qad qamat al-salah' which is recited twice.
Opponent: Imam al-Shafi'i
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet commanded Bilal to make adhan in pairs and iqamah in odd numbers.
Hadith of Anas
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets the hadith of Anas to mean a difference in delivery (tarassul vs hadr), not in number. The number remains twice for all phrases.
The angel hadith overrides the literal reading of Anas hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis recite all phrases twice; Shafi'is recite only 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. The prayer is valid in both schools, but the sunnah manner differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْإِقَامَةُ مِثْلُ الْأَذَانِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَزِيدُ فِيهَا بَعْدَ الْفَلَاح قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوةُ مَرَّتَيْنِ هَكَذَا فَعَلَ الْمَلَكُ النَّازِلُ مِنَ السَّلَمَاء وَهُوَ المَشْهُورُ ثُمَّ هُوَ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِى قَوْلِهِ إِنَّهَا فَرَادَىٰ فُرَادَى إِلَّا قَوْلُهُ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوةِ ترجمہ اور اقامت اذان کے مثل ہے مگر اقامت میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد دو مرتبہ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة بڑھائے ایساہی اس فرشتہ نے کیا جو آسمان سے نازل ہوا تھا اور یہی مشہور ہے۔ پھر یہ حجت ہے امام شافعی کے خلاف ان کے اس قول میں کہ اقامت فرادی فرادی ہے سوائے کلمہ قد قامت الصلواة کے۔ تشریح شیخ قدوری نے کہا کہ اقامت بھی اذان کے مانند ہے لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ اقامت میں جی علی الفلاح کے بعد دوبار قـــد قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کا اضافہ کرے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کے علاوہ تمام کلمات ایک ایک مرتبہ کہے اور قد قَامَتِ الصَّلوةُ دوبار کہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت انس کی حدیث ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت بلال کو حکم دیا کہ اذان جفت کہے اورا قامت سوائے قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کے طاق ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو فرشتہ آسمان سے نازل ہوا تھا اس نے اذان کی طرح اقامت بھی دو، دو مرتبہ کہی۔ چنانچہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے عثمان بن ابی لیلیٰ سے روایت کی کہ ہم سے اصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیان کیا کہ عثمان بن زید انصاری نے آکر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے عرض کیا کہ گویا ایک شخص جس پر دوسبز چادر ہیں ایک دیوار پر کھڑا ہوا اور اس نے اذان دو دو مرتبہ اور اقامت دو دو مرتبہ کہی۔ اور حدیث انس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اذان میں دو کلمے دو آواز کے ساتھ کہے جائیں اور اقامت میں دو کلمے ایک آواز کے ساتھ کہے جائیں۔
And the iqamah is like the adhan except that he adds in it after al-falah: 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. Thus did the angel who descended from the heaven do, and this is the well-known (position). Then this is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his statement that it is individually (recited) except for his statement 'qad qamat al-salah'. Translation: And the iqamah is like the adhan, except that in iqamah after 'hayya ala al-falah' he adds 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. This is what the angel who descended from heaven did, and this is the well-known. Then this is a proof against Imam al-Shafi'i in his statement that the iqamah is recited singly except for the phrase 'qad qamat al-salah'. Explanation: Shaykh al-Quduri said that iqamah is like adhan with the difference that in iqamah after 'hayya ala al-falah' he adds 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. Imam al-Shafi'i says that all phrases are recited singly except 'qad qamat al-salah' which is recited twice. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded Bilal to recite the adhan in pairs and the iqamah in odd numbers except for 'qad qamat al-salah'. Our evidence is that the angel who descended from heaven recited both adhan and iqamah in pairs (two by two). Thus Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Uthman ibn Abi Layla that the companions of Muhammad (peace be upon him) told us that Uthman ibn Zayd al-Ansari came to the Messenger of Allah and said, 'It was as if a man with two green garments stood on a wall and called adhan in pairs and iqamah in pairs.' And the meaning of the hadith of Anas is that in adhan the two phrases are said with two voices, and in iqamah the two phrases are said with one voice.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling on iqamah. The Hanafi school holds that iqamah is recited in the same manner as adhan, with all phrases repeated twice, with the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' twice after 'hayya ala al-falah'. The proof is the hadith of the angel who taught the adhan and iqamah to a companion. The author also refutes Imam al-Shafi'i who holds that iqamah phrases are recited singly except for 'qad qamat al-salah'. The Hanafi response interprets the hadith of Anas differently: the difference between adhan and iqamah is not in the number of repetitions but in the manner of delivery — adhan with pauses (tarassul) and iqamah with speed (hadr).

Key Terms
اقامة (iqamah): the second call to prayer immediately before the prayer begins
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qamat al-salah): the phrase indicating the prayer has begun
فرادیٰ (furaada): singly, one by one

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Four times
D) Not recited at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that iqamah is recited exactly like adhan — all phrases twice — based on the angel's practice, and the Shafi'i view is refuted by interpreting the Anas hadith as referring to delivery style, not number.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Iqamah Similar to Adhan with Addition of 'Qad Qamat al-Salah' Twice
Inter-madhhab dispute on the number of phrase repetitions in the iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the repetition of iqamah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The iqamah repeats each phrase twice like the adhan, with the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' twice — established by the angel's practice.

The iqamah, the second call to prayer, is closely modeled on the adhan. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling that all phrases of the iqamah are repeated twice, identical to the adhan, with the sole addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' said twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. It then addresses the Shafi'i position that argues for single repetitions, and provides the Hanafi proof from the hadith of the angel who descended from the sky. Understanding this dispute is essential for grasping how different schools derive practices from varying interpretations of the same prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on iqamah repetition
Identify the core ruling: iqamah is like adhan with all phrases twice, plus the additional phrase 'qad qamat al-salah' twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Note that this is the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all iqamah phrases are said singly except 'qad qamat al-salah' which is repeated. His proof is the hadith of Anas where the Prophet commanded Bilal to say adhan in pairs (jift) and iqamah singly (taq).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith of Anas differently: 'pairs' (jift) means each phrase is said with two distinct voices (tarsil) in adhan, while 'single' (taq) in iqamah means the two repetitions are said with one voice (hadr), not that the phrases are said once. The number of repetitions remains two.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi proof from the angel hadith
The Hanafis rely on the explicit narration that the angel who descended from the sky said both adhan and iqamah twice. This is considered more explicit and thus preferred over the Shafi'i interpretation.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis say iqamah with more phrases (e.g., 17 total) while Shafi'is say fewer (e.g., 11). The difference matters for the actual performance of the prayer call in the mosque.

Source Text

وَالْإِقَامَةُ مِثْلُ الْأَذَانِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَزِيدُ فِيهَا بَعْدَ الْفَلَاح قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوةُ مَرَّتَيْنِ هَكَذَا فَعَلَ الْمَلَكُ النَّازِلُ مِنَ السَّلَمَاء وَهُوَ المَشْهُورُ ثُمَّ هُوَ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِى قَوْلِهِ إِنَّهَا فَرَادَىٰ فُرَادَى إِلَّا قَوْلُهُ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوةِ ترجمہ اور اقامت اذان کے مثل ہے مگر اقامت میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد دو مرتبہ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة بڑھائے ایساہی اس فرشتہ نے کیا جو آسمان سے نازل ہوا تھا اور یہی مشہور ہے۔ پھر یہ حجت ہے امام شافعی کے خلاف ان کے اس قول میں کہ اقامت فرادی فرادی ہے سوائے کلمہ قد قامت الصلواة کے۔ تشریح شیخ قدوری نے کہا کہ اقامت بھی اذان کے مانند ہے لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ اقامت میں جی علی الفلاح کے بعد دوبار قـــد قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کا اضافہ کرے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کے علاوہ تمام کلمات ایک ایک مرتبہ کہے اور قد قَامَتِ الصَّلوةُ دوبار کہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت انس کی حدیث ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت بلال کو حکم دیا کہ اذان جفت کہے اورا قامت سوائے قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلوة کے طاق ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو فرشتہ آسمان سے نازل ہوا تھا اس نے اذان کی طرح اقامت بھی دو، دو مرتبہ کہی۔ چنانچہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے عثمان بن ابی لیلیٰ سے روایت کی کہ ہم سے اصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیان کیا کہ عثمان بن زید انصاری نے آکر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے عرض کیا کہ گویا ایک شخص جس پر دوسبز چادر ہیں ایک دیوار پر کھڑا ہوا اور اس نے اذان دو دو مرتبہ اور اقامت دو دو مرتبہ کہی۔ اور حدیث انس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اذان میں دو کلمے دو آواز کے ساتھ کہے جائیں اور اقامت میں دو کلمے ایک آواز کے ساتھ کہے جائیں۔
And the iqamah is like the adhan except that he adds in it after al-falah 'qad qamat al-salah' twice. Thus did the angel descending from the sky, and it is the well-known. Then it is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his statement that it is singular except for his statement 'qad qamat al-salah'. Translation: And iqamah is like adhan, but in iqamah after hayya 'ala al-falah he adds qad qamat al-salah twice. Similarly did the angel who descended from the sky, and this is the well-known. Then this is a proof against Imam Shafi'i in his statement that iqamah is singular except for the word qad qamat al-salah. Explanation: Sheikh Quduri said that iqamah is like adhan except that in iqamah after hayya 'ala al-falah he adds qad qamat al-salah twice. Imam Shafi'i says that all words except qad qamat al-salah are said once and qad qamat al-salah is said twice. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet ﷺ commanded Bilal to say adhan in pairs and iqamah singular except qad qamat al-salah. Our proof is that the angel who descended from the sky said iqamah twice like adhan. Thus Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Uthman ibn Abi Layla that the companions of Muhammad ﷺ said that Uthman ibn Zaid al-Ansari came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and said: 'A person with two green garments stood on a wall and said adhan twice and iqamah twice.' And the meaning of the hadith of Anas is that in adhan the two words are said with two voices and in iqamah the two words are said with one voice.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of repetitions in the iqamah. The Hanafi position, stated by al-Quduri, is that the iqamah is exactly like the adhan in that each phrase is repeated twice, with the sole addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' said twice after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The evidence for this is the report of the angel who descended from the sky and performed both adhan and iqamah with double repetitions, as narrated by the companions. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that all phrases of the iqamah are said singly except 'qad qamat al-salah', relying on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet ordered Bilal to say adhan in pairs (jift) and iqamah singly (taq). The Hanafi response reconciles this by interpreting the hadith of Anas to mean that in adhan each phrase is pronounced with two distinct voices (i.e., with pauses), while in iqamah the two repetitions are run together with one voice (hadr), but the number of repetitions remains two. Thus the Hanafi school maintains the practice of the angel as the stronger evidence, and this is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
الْإِقَامَةُ (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, pronounced just before the obligatory prayer begins.
الْأَذَانُ (al-adhan): The call to prayer announcing the time of prayer.
قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلَاةُ (qad qamat al-salah): Words added in the iqamah after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' meaning 'The prayer has indeed been established.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times is 'qad qamat al-salah' said in the iqamah?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the iqamah repeats each phrase twice like the adhan, adding 'qad qamat al-salah' twice, based on the explicit practice of the angel.

Tarsil in Adhan and Hadr in Iqamah: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling on slow recitation in adhan and quick recitation in iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah, identify the dalil, and explain why the imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah are recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory.

The adhan and iqamah are not just words; they have a prescribed manner. The Prophet ﷺ instructed Bilal to recite the adhan slowly and the iqamah quickly. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the Hanafi ruling, addressing the subtle difference between a command that indicates obligation versus recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the two acts mentioned? Tarsil (slow recitation) in adhan and hadr (quick recitation) in iqamah. The passage states they are mustahabb (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's command to Bilal: 'When you give the adhan, be slow; when you give the iqamah, be quick.' This is a hadith (Sunnah ahad).
The hadith is transmitted via a single chain, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative (فَتَرَسَل فَاحْدِر) prove recommendation? In Hanafi usul, the default for amr is wujub unless there is a qarina (context) indicating nadb. Here, the context of adhan/iqamah practice shows it is not obligatory.
The commentary mentions that the author of Hidayah calls it a 'clarification of recommendation'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars consider doing tarsil in iqamah makruh because it goes against the sunnah. However, the primary position in Hidayah is that it is not makruh because only a mustahabb act is left.
Ibn al-Humam confirms that the recommended view is that both are sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah are mustahabb, and leaving them is not makruh. The authoritative weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَتَرَسَّلُ فِي الْأَذَانِ وَيَحْدِرُ فِي الْإِقَامَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام إِذَا أَذَنْتَ فَتَرَسَل وَإِذَا أَقَمْتَ فَاحْدِرُ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ الاستحباب ترجمہ اور اذان میں ترسل کرے اور اقامت میں صدر کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جب تو اذان دے تو ترسل کر اور جب اقامت کہے تو حد کر ۔ اور یہ استہاب کا بیان ہے۔ تشریح ترسل یہ ہے کہ دو کلموں کے درمیان فصل کرے سکتہ کے ساتھ اور حد یہ ہے کہ فصل نہ کرے۔ فرمایا کہ اذان میں ترسل مستحب ہے اور اقامت میں حدد مستحب ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت بلال کو اسی کا امر فرمایا ہے۔ پس اگر اقامت میں ترسل کیا تو بعض حضرات کا قول یہ ہے کہ خلاف سنت ہونے کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہے لیکن ہدایہ کی عبارت سے عدم کراہت ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ولهذا بيان الاستحباب اور ظاہر ہے کہ ترک مستحب سے کراہت پیدا نہیں ہوتی ۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا کہ قول اول حق ہے یعنی اذان میں ترسل اور اقامت میں صدر کا مسنون ہونا حق ہے۔۔
And he should be slow (tarsil) in the adhan and quick (hadr) in the iqamah because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'When you give the adhan, be slow, and when you give the iqamah, be quick.' And this is a clarification of recommendation. Translation: And in adhan he should do tarsil and in iqamah he should do hadr because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When you give adhan, be slow, and when you give iqamah, be quick.' And this is a statement of recommendation. Explanation: Tarsil is to separate between two words with a pause, and hadr is not to separate. He said that tarsil in adhan is mustahabb and hadr in iqamah is mustahabb. The evidence is that the Prophet ﷺ commanded Bilal to do so. So if one does tarsil in iqamah, some scholars say it is makruh because it is against the sunnah, but the text of Hidayah indicates no karahah because the author said 'this is a clarification of recommendation' and it is apparent that leaving a mustahabb does not cause karahah. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said that the first saying is correct, i.e., that tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah are sunnah.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the manner of recitation in the calls to prayer. 'Tarsil' means to recite slowly with pauses between phrases, while 'hadr' means to recite quickly without interruption. The Prophet's command to Bilal establishes that tarsil is mustahabb (recommended) in adhan and hadr is mustahabb in iqamah. There is a minor ikhtilaf about whether doing tarsil in iqamah is makruh; the text of Al-Hidayah suggests it is not makruh since only a mustahabb act is left, but some scholars hold it is makruh tanzihan. Ibn al-Humam confirms the first opinion that both are sunnah (i.e., mustahabb).

Key Terms
التَّرَسُّلُ (al-tarsil): Reciting slowly with pauses between phrases, specifically in adhan.
الْحَدْرُ (al-hadr): Reciting quickly without pauses between phrases, specifically in iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing tarsil (slow recitation) in the iqamah according to the primary position in Al-Hidayah?
A) It is wajib
B) It is mustahabb
C) It is makruh
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah are recommended (mustahabb), not required; reversing them does not invalidate the adhan or iqamah but leaves the preferred practice.

Facing Qibla in Adhan and Turning Face for Hayya 'ala al-Salah
Ruling on facing qibla during adhan/iqamah and turning face during specific phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla during adhan and iqamah, and explain the sunnah of turning the face for 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is sunnah, not wajib; turning face right and left is also sunnah.

In the Hanafi school, the mu'adhdhin should face the qibla during adhan and iqamah, based on the practice of the angel. However, if he omits facing, the adhan is valid but disliked. At the phrases calling the congregation, he should turn his face to the right and left without moving his feet. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains these rulings and the concession for a spacious minaret.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The passage states that the mu'adhdhin should face the qibla during adhan and iqamah. Determine the hukm level: is it wajib, sunnah, or mubah?
The text says 'يستقبل' which indicates recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the practice of the angel who descended from the sky and gave adhan facing the qibla. Identify the type of proof (Sunnah ahad) and its strength (zanni al-thubut).
The angel's action is cited as a precedent for sunnah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the angel's action prove the ruling? Explain why it indicates sunnah, not obligation, based on Hanafi usul: the angel's action is not a command but a practice that implies recommendation.
If it were wajib, omitting it would invalidate the adhan; but the text says it is permissible but makruh.
4
Examine the exception for turning face
The text prescribes turning the face right and left for 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Understand the wisdom: it is an address to the people, so facing them symbolically. Why not turn to the back? Explain the answer in the commentary: turning back would be turning away from the qibla.
The sunnah is to keep feet fixed and only turn the face.
5
Apply the minaret concession
If the minaret is spacious and turning the face while keeping feet fixed is not possible, the mu'adhdhin may turn his whole body to face the openings. Identify the condition: only when necessary (i.e., the purpose of conveying the voice is not achieved otherwise).
Without need, moving feet is not good.

الْوَجْهَ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا مَعَ ثُبَاتِ قَدَمَيْهِ مَكَانَهُمَا كَمَا هُوَ السُّنَّةُ بِأَنْ كَانَتِ الصَّوْمَعَةُ مُتَّسِعَةً فَأَمَّا مِنْ غَيْرِ حَاجَةٍ فَلَا ترجمہ اور اذان اور اقامت میں قبلہ عَلَى الصَّلوة اور حَيَّ عَلَى الفلاح کے وقت اپنا چہرہ دائیں اور بائیں طرف پھیرے کیونکہ یہ تو قوم کو خطاب ہے۔ پس ان کے روبرو ہوگا اور اگر موذن اپنے صومعہ میں گھوم گیا تو اچھا ہے۔ اور امام محمد کی مراد یہ ہے کہ اپنے قدم اس جگہ جمائے رکھنے کے ساتھ جو کہ سنت طریقہ ہے دائیں بائیں منہ پھیرناممکن نہ ہو ۔ بایں طور کہ صومعہ کشادہ ہے، رہا بغیر ضرورت کے تو اپنی جگہ سے قدم ہٹانا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب عنایہ تھی اور اگر اذان میں استقبال قبلہ چھوڑ دیا تو جائز ہے لیکن خلاف سنت ہونے کی وجہ سے مکروہ تنزیہی ہوگا اور حَتی عَلَى الصَّلوة اور حَى عَلَى الفلاح کہتے وقت صرف اپنا چہرہ دائیں اور بائیں جانب گھومائے کیونکہ ان دونوں کلموں کے ساتھ قوم کو خطاب کیا گیا ہے لہذا یہ خطاب ان کے روبرو ہوگا کہ نماز کی طرف وار فلاح دارین کی طرف آؤ۔ یہاں یہ اشکال ہو سکتا ہے کہ قوم جس طرح دائیں اور بائیں جانب ہے اس طرح پیچھے معینی نے شرح ہدایہ میں لکھا کہ صومعہ مسجدمیں وہ بلند جگہ ہے جہاں مؤذن کھڑا ہو کر اذان دے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر موذن صومعہ میں گھوم گیا تو اچھا ہے بشرطیکہ صومعہ کشادہ ہو پس دائیں موکھلے سے سر نکال کر دو ہے جبکہ اس کو دونوں قدم جمائے رکھنے کے ساتھ دائیں بائیں منہ پھیرنا جو کہ سنت طریقہ ہے ممکن نہ ہو بایں طور کہ صومعہ کشادہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ اپنی جگہ پر جھے ہونے کے ساتھ اذان کا پورا اعلام جو مقصود ہے حاصل نہ ہو تب موکھلے پر جانے کی ضرورت ہوگی۔ اس میں کچھ مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ اور بغیر ضرورت اپنی جگہ سے قدم ہٹانا اچھا نہیں ہے۔
And he should face the qibla with both (adhan and iqamah) because the angel descending from the sky gave adhan facing the qibla. And if he leaves facing, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked (makruh) due to opposing the sunnah. And he should turn his face for 'al-salah' and 'al-falah' to the right and left because it is an address to the people, so he faces them. And if he turns around in his minaret (sawma'ah), it is good. And his (Imam Muhammad's) intent is when he cannot turn his face right and left while keeping his feet fixed in their place as is the sunnah, such as when the minaret is spacious. As for without need, then no. Translation: And in adhan and iqamah he should face the qibla because the angel who descended from the sky gave adhan facing the qibla. And if he leaves facing, it is permissible because the purpose of adhan is achieved, but it will be makruh due to opposing the sunnah. And at the time of 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' he should turn his face to the right and left because this is an address to the people, so he faces them. And if the mu'adhdhin turns around in his minaret, it is good. And Imam Muhammad's intent is when it is not possible to turn the face right and left while keeping his feet fixed in their place, which is the sunnah way, such as when the minaret is spacious. As for without need, moving his feet from his place is not good. Explanation: Sahib al-'Inayah stated that one should stand facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah, except for 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. The evidence is that the angel who descended from the sky gave adhan facing the qibla. And if facing the qibla is left in adhan, it is permissible but makruh tanzihan due to opposing the sunnah. When saying 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', he should only turn his face to the right and left because these two phrases address the people, so the address should be towards them: 'Come to prayer and success in both worlds.' Here an objection may arise: the people are behind as well as right and left, so why not turn to the back? The answer is that turning to the back would mean turning away from the qibla, while the mu'adhdhin is inviting people to face the qibla, so only turning to the sides suffices because the purpose of conveying the voice is achieved. In Bahr al-Ra'iq, sawma'ah means minaret. Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni wrote in Sharh al-Hidayah that sawma'ah is a high place in the mosque where the mu'adhdhin stands to give adhan. The conclusion is that if the mu'adhdhin turns around in the minaret, it is good provided the minaret is spacious, so he puts his head out of the right opening and says 'hayya 'ala al-salah' twice, and out of the left opening and says 'hayya 'ala al-falah' twice. Sahib al-Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad's statement in the text means that turning in the minaret is when it is not possible to turn the face right and left while keeping both feet fixed, which is the sunnah way, such as when the minaret is spacious. The conclusion is that if the complete announcement of adhan, which is the purpose, is not achieved while standing in one place, then going to the openings is necessary. There is no harm in that. And without need, moving feet from one's place is not good.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof on facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah, and the specific action during the 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' phrases. The Hanafi position is that the mu'adhdhin must face the qibla throughout the adhan and iqamah, based on the practice of the angel who descended from the sky. If one omits facing the qibla, the adhan is valid but makruh tanzihan. At the phrases calling the people to prayer and success, the mu'adhdhin should turn his face to the right and left, as this is an address to the congregation. The text also discusses the case of a spacious minaret (sawma'ah): if turning the face while keeping the feet fixed is not possible, the mu'adhdhin may turn his whole body to face the right opening for 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and the left for 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Without need, moving the feet is discouraged. The wisdom behind not turning to the back is that it would involve turning away from the qibla, which would contradict the invitation to face the qibla.

Key Terms
الصَّوْمَعَةُ (al-sawma'ah): A high place in the mosque or a minaret where the mu'adhdhin stands to give adhan.
الاِسْتِقْبَالُ (al-istiqbal): Facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a mu'adhdhin gives adhan without facing the qibla?
A) The adhan is invalid and must be repeated
B) The adhan is valid but makruh tanzihi
C) The adhan is valid and not disliked
D) The adhan is invalid and the mu'adhdhin sins

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla is sunnah for adhan; turning face right and left for the call is also sunnah; omission is permissible but disliked.

Salah — Prayer

Facing the Qibla and Turning During Adhan: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on facing qibla during adhan/iqamah, with turning for hayya alas-salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah, explain the proof, and identify when turning is required.

Core Idea
Facing Qibla during adhan is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib; omitting it is makruh tanzihi.

The adhan is a call to prayer, and its sunan enhance its completeness. One such sunnah is facing the qibla. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the angel's practice, and the specific turning for hayya alas-salah. Understanding these details ensures that we perform the adhan in the best manner while knowing when deviation is excusable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act: facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah; leaving it is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of the angel who descended from heaven giving adhan while facing the qibla.
This is a hadith, but its transmission is ahad, so it indicates sunnah, not wujub.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The angel's action is a precedent. However, the purpose of adhan (i'lam, informing people) is achieved even without facing qibla. Therefore, it is not obligatory but a sunnah.
4
Apply to turning for hayya alas-salah
The mu'adhdhin turns his face right and left for hayya alas-salah and hayya alal-falah because it is a call to the people. If the minaret is spacious and he cannot turn his face while feet remain fixed, he may turn his whole body. This is good (hasan). Without need, turning the whole body is not preferred.
The turning is also a sunnah, tied to the address to the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ بِهِمَا الْقِبْلَةَ لأنَّ النَّازِلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ اذَنَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةَ وَلَوْ تَرَكَ الإِسْتِقْبَالَ جَازَ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَيُكْرَهُ لِمُخَالَفَةِ السُّنَّةِ وَيُحَوِّلُ وَجْهَهُ لِلصَّلَاةِ وَالْفَلَاحِ يَمْنَةً وَيُسْرَةً لِأَنَّهُ خِطَابٌ لِلْقَوْمِ فَيُوَاجِهُهُمْ وَإِنِ اسْتَدارَ فِي صَوْمَعَتِهِ فَحَسَنٌ وَ مُرَادُهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ تَحْوِيلَ الْوَجْهِ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا مَعَ ثَبَاتِ قَدَمَيْهِ مَكَانَهُمَا كَمَا هُوَ السُّنَّةُ بِأَنْ كَانَتِ الصَّوْمَعَةُ مُتَّسِعَةً فَأَمَّا مِنْ غَيْرِ حَاجَةٍ فَلَا
And he faces the qibla with both (adhan and iqamah) because the one who descended from heaven gave adhan facing the qibla. And if he leaves facing the qibla, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked because it contradicts the sunnah. And he turns his face for as-salah and al-falah to the right and left because it is a call to the people, so he faces them. And if he turns around in his minaret, it is good. And his meaning is: when he cannot turn his face right and left while keeping his feet fixed in their place as is the sunnah, because the minaret is spacious. As for without need, then no.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on facing the qibla during adhan and iqamah. The author explains that it is sunnah to face the qibla, based on the practice of the angel who descended from heaven. If one omits it, the adhan is valid but makruh tanzihi (disliked) because it contradicts the sunnah. At the words hayya alas-salah and hayya alal-falah, the mu'adhdhin should turn his face to the right and left respectively, as these are addresses to the people. If the minaret is spacious and turning the face while keeping feet fixed is impossible, he may turn his whole body to face the right and left openings—this is good. But without need, moving feet is not good. The commentary elaborates that the proof is the hadith of the angel Jibril (or the caller from heaven) facing the qibla. The turning for hayya alas-salah is specific to right and left, not back, because that would turn away from the qibla, and the mu'adhdhin is calling people to the qibla.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qibla): Facing the qibla direction during adhan and iqamah.
صومعة (sawma'ah): The elevated place in a mosque where the mu'adhdhin stands to give adhan, often a minaret or platform.
مخالفة السنة (mukhalafat al-sunnah): Acting contrary to the established prophetic practice; here it makes the action makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on facing the qibla during the entire adhan according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is fard; without it adhan is invalid.
B) It is sunnah; leaving it makes adhan valid but makruh tanzihi.
C) It is wajib; leaving it requires repeating the adhan.
D) It is mustahab; leaving it is not disliked.

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla during adhan is sunnah muakkadah; omitting it does not invalidate the adhan but is disliked.

Placing Fingers in Ears During Adhan
Ruling with proof on a recommended adhan practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing fingers in ears during adhan and explain the evidence from the Prophet's command to Bilal.

Core Idea
Placing fingers in ears during adhan is afdal (better), not wajib, because it is a sunnah zā'idah, not a sunnah asliyyah.

When the mu'adhdhin calls the adhan, there is a recommended practice to place his index fingers in his ears. This lesson examines the Hanafi stance on this action, its proof from the Sunnah, and why it is considered merely better (afdal) rather than an integral part of the adhan. Understanding this distinction helps you appreciate the different levels of sunnah in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the mu'adhdhin placing his fingers in his ears. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or merely recommended?
The text uses 'afdal' (better) and 'hasan' (good) for omitting it.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ commanded Bilal to do this. Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah ahad) and its strength of transmission (zanni) and indication (zanni).
The command is a specific action, not a general obligation.
3
Analyze the wording and rationale
The text also gives a rational reason: 'because it is more effective in proclaiming.' This shows the action is recommended for a practical benefit, not required for validity.
The combination of a prophetic command and a rational benefit reinforces the recommendation.
4
Understand the classification as sunan zā'idah
The passage states it is not a sunnah asliyyah (primary sunnah) but a sunnah zā'idah (additional). This explains why omitting it is still 'hasan' (good or acceptable).
Hanafis categorize sunnan into asliyyah (foundational, like facing qibla) and zā'idah (supplementary, like this action).
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In a real adhan, the mu'adhdhin should place his fingers in his ears to follow the Sunnah optimally. If he forgets or chooses not to, his adhan remains valid and good, but doing it is better.
This ruling is mufta bihi and widely practiced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْاَفْضَلُ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ إِصْبَعَيْهِ فِي اذْنَيْهِ بِذَلِكَ أَمَرَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِلَالًا وَلِأَنَّهُ ابْلَغُ فِي الْأَعْلَامِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ فَحَسَنْ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتَ بِسُنَّةٍ أَصْلِيَّةٍ
And the better for the mu'adhdhin is that he places his two fingers in his ears; with that the Prophet ﷺ commanded Bilal, and because it is more effective in proclaiming. And if he does not do it, then it is good because it is not an original sunnah.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage states that it is afdal (better) for the mu'adhdhin to place his index fingers in his ears when giving adhan. The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ commanded Bilal to do so, and it helps raise the voice. However, if he omits it, the adhan is still good (hasan) because this action is not from the original sunnah (sunan asliyyah) but rather from the sunan zawā'id (additional recommended acts). The commentary explains that 'hasan' here means acceptable, not that omitting it is itself good. The author clarifies that while it is not a primary sunnah, it is still a recommended act due to the Prophet's command. Thus, doing it makes the adhan ahsan (better), and omitting it makes it hasan. The passage also lists the qualities of a preferred mu'adhdhin: male, sane, adult, healthy, pious, knowledgeable of sunnah and prayer times, loud voice, and regular in five daily adhans. He should not take wages for adhan; if he does, his adhan is makruh and he is fasiq.

Key Terms
سنن أصلية (sunan asliyyah): Original or primary sunnah actions that are part of the established practice; placing fingers in ears is not from these, so it is not a sunnah muakkadah.
أفضل (afdal): Better; a recommended action that is not wajib or sunnah muakkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is placing fingers in ears during adhan considered afdal rather than wajib according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the command was only for Bilal and not for others.
B) Because it is classified as a sunnah zā'idah, not a sunnah asliyyah, and the evidence is zanni.
C) Because the Prophet never did it himself.
D) Because it is a bid'ah (innovation) but tolerated.

Key Takeaway
Placing fingers in ears during adhan is a recommended practice (mustahab) based on the Prophet's command to Bilal, but its omission does not affect the validity of the adhan.

Ruling on Tathwib (Calling After Adhan)
Ruling on tathwib in Fajr and other prayers with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwib for Fajr and other prayers, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding addressing the amir, and apply the later istihsan to modern contexts.

Core Idea
Tathwib was originally for Fajr only; later scholars extended it to all prayers due to widespread laziness.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines the practice of tathwib—calling out between adhan and iqamah. It distinguishes between the original ruling (hasan for Fajr, makruh for others) and the later istihsan that made it mustahsan for all prayers. It also addresses an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding whether the mu'adhdhin may specifically greet and call the amir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what tathwib is and the original ruling for Fajr vs other prayers.
The text says 'hasan' for Fajr and 'makruh' for others.
2
Trace the reasoning (talil)
Understand why Kufan scholars introduced it and why later scholars extended it.
Reason for Fajr: time of sleep; later istihsan due to laziness.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions on addressing the amir.
Abu Yusuf permits; Muhammad opposes based on equality.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical impact of each view.
Whether the mu'adhdhin may specifically call the amir.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling for fatwa.
Later scholars preferred Abu Yusuf's view and extended it to qadi and mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّنْوِيبُ فِي الْفَجْرِ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ مَرَّتَيْنِ بَيْنَ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ حَسَنٌ لِأَنَّهُ وَقْتُ نَوْمٍ وَغَفْلَةٍ وَكُرِهَ فِي سَائِرِ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَمَعْنَاهُ الْعَوْدُ إِلَى الْإِعْلَامِ وَهُوَ عَلَى حَسَبِ مَا تَعَارَفُوهُ وَهَذَا تَنْوِيبُ أَحْدَثَهُ عُلَمَاءُ الْكُوفَةِ بَعْدَ عَهْدِ الصَّحَابَةِ لِتَغَيُّرِ أَحْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَخَصُّوا الْفَجْرَ بِهِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ وَالْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ اسْتَحْسَنُوهُ فِي الصَّلَوَاتِ كُلِّهَا لِظُهُورِ التَّوَانِي فِي الْأُمُورِ الدِّينِيَّةِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا أَرَى بَأْسًا أَنْ يَقُولَ الْمُؤَذِّنُ لِلْأَمِيرِ فِي الصَّلَوَاتِ كُلِّهَا السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ وَاسْتَبْعَدَهُ مُحَمَّدٌ لِأَنَّ النَّاسَ سَوَاسِيَةٌ فِي أَمْرِ الْجَمَاعَةِ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ خَصَّهُمْ بِذَلِكَ لِزِيَادَةِ اشْتِغَالِهِمْ بِأُمُورِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَيْ لَا تَفُوتَهُمُ الْجَمَاعَةُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْقَاضِي وَالْمُفْتِي
And tathwib in Fajr: saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between the adhan and iqamah is good (hasan) because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, and it is disliked (makruh) in other prayers. Its meaning is returning to notification, and it is according to what they are accustomed. This tathwib was introduced by the scholars of Kufa after the era of the Companions due to the change in people's conditions, and they specified it for Fajr for the reason we mentioned. The later scholars considered it good (mustahsan) in all prayers due to the appearance of laziness in religious matters. Abu Yusuf said: I see no harm if the mu'adhdhin says to the amir in all prayers: 'al-Salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-amir wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah, yarhamuka Allah.' Muhammad considered it far-fetched because people are equal in the matter of jama'ah. Abu Yusuf specified them with that due to their increased preoccupation with the affairs of the Muslims so that they do not miss the jama'ah. The same applies to the qadi and the mufti.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses tathwib (sometimes spelled tathwib), which means returning to notification after the adhan. Linguistically, it denotes returning; in Shar'iah, it refers to calling out between the adhan and iqamah. There are two types: al-tathwib al-qadim (the original, which is 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' for Fajr, considered sunnah) and al-tathwib al-muhdath (the newly introduced one). This passage deals with the latter: saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between adhan and iqamah. The original ruling in the Hidayah is that this is 'hasan' (good, recommended) specifically for Fajr because it is a time of sleep, and disliked (makruh) for other prayers. This practice was initiated by the Kufan scholars after the Companion era due to changing circumstances. However, later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirun) deemed it mustahsan (preferred) for all prayers because people became lazy in religious duties. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: Abu Yusuf allows the mu'adhdhin to address the amir specifically in all prayers with a greeting and the tathwib phrases, to remind the ruler due to his busy schedule. Imam Muhammad considers this far-fetched because all people are equal in the obligation of jama'ah. Abu Yusuf's view extends also to the qadi and mufti. The comment concludes that the mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that tathwib in all prayers is permissible due to the later scholars' istihsan.

Key Terms
تَنْوِيب/تَّثْوِيب (tathwib/tanwib): Literally 'returning'; in fiqh, calling out between adhan and iqamah to remind people of prayer, especially for Fajr.
مُسْتَحْسَن (mustahsan): Deemed good by istihsan (juristic preference); a ruling preferred over qiyas due to necessity or custom.
أَمِير (amir): The ruler or governor; a person in authority over Muslims' affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the original ruling for tathwib in prayers other than Fajr?
A) It is mustahsan (preferred).
B) It is makruh (disliked).
C) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Tathwib in all prayers is now considered mustahsan due to later istihsan, and addressing the amir is permissible following Abu Yusuf's view.

Ruling on Tathwīb in Fajr and the Dispute of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Ruling on tathwīb with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwīb in Fajr and other prayers, explain the evolution of the ruling, and compare the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding tathwīb for rulers.

Core Idea
Tathwīb in Fajr is commendable; later scholars extended it to all prayers due to negligence.

Tathwīb—the extra call between adhan and iqama—is a practice introduced after the Companions' era. This lesson clarifies its ruling in Fajr (commendable) and other prayers (disliked), the later shift to mustahsan for all prayers, and a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether rulers deserve a special tathwīb. Understanding this evolution shows how Hanafi fiqh adapts to changing circumstances while preserving the core principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
Tathwīb in Fajr: saying 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between adhan and iqama. The ruling is hasan (commendable) because Fajr is a time of sleep and heedlessness. For all other prayers, it is makruh (disliked).
The text clearly states 'hasan' for Fajr and 'makruh' for others.
2
Understand the rationale and origin
Tathwīb was innovated by Kufan scholars after the Sahaba due to changing conditions. They confined it to Fajr because people needed extra reminder at that time.
It is not a sunna from the Prophet; it is a later practice based on istihsan.
3
Track the later development
Later scholars (muta'akhkhirūn) considered tathwīb mustahsan (recommended) in all prayers because of general negligence in religious duties. This is a shift from the earlier narrower ruling.
Mustahsan here is a level above hasan, reflecting a stronger recommendation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on rulers
Abu Yusuf permits a special tathwīb for rulers in all prayers using additional words of greeting. Muhammad al-Shaybani rejects this, arguing all people are equal in congregation. The passage extends the ruling to judges and muftis.
This dispute is within the Hanafi school; both imams have valid arguments.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to Abu Yusuf, the special tathwīb for rulers is allowed; according to Muhammad, it is disapproved. Later practice often follows Abu Yusuf for rulers and those in authority.
No explicit tarjih in the text, but the extension to judges/muftis suggests acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتَّنْوِيبُ فِي الْفَجْرِ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ مَرَّتَيْنِ بَيْنَ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ حَسَنٌ لِأَنَّهُ وَقْتُ نَوْمٍ وَغَفْلَةٍ وَكُرِهَ فِي سَائِرِ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَمَعْنَاهُ الْعَوْدُ إِلَى الْإِعْلَامِ وَهُوَ عَلَى حَسَبِ مَا تَعَارَفُوهُ وَهَذَا تَنْوِيبٌ أَحْدَثَهُ عُلَمَاءُ الْكُوفَةِ بَعْدَ عَهْدِ الصَّحَابَةِ لِتَغَيُّرِ أَحْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَخَصُّوا الْفَجْرَ بِهِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ وَالْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ اسْتَحْسَنُوهُ فِي الصَّلَوَاتِ كُلِّهَا لِظُهُورِ التَّوَانِي فِي الْأُمُورِ الدِّينِيَّةِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا أَرَى بَأْسًا أَنْ يَقُولَ الْمُؤَذِّنُ لِلْأَمِيرِ فِي الصَّلَوَاتِ كُلِّهَا السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ يَرْحَمُكَ الله وَاسْتَبْعَدَهُ مُحَمَّدٌ لِأَنَّ النَّاسَ سَوَاسِيَةٌ فِي أَمْرِ الْجَمَاعَةِ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ خَصَّهُمْ بِذَلِكَ لِزِيَادَةِ اشْتِغَالِهِمْ بِأُمُورِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَيْلَا تَفُوتَهُمُ الْجَمَاعَةُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْقَاضِي وَالْمُفْتِي

ترجمہ: اور فجر میں تصویب کرنا دو بار حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ کے ساتھ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان بہتر ہے کیونکہ وہ خواب اور غفلت کا وقت ہے۔ اور باقی نمازوں میں تحویب مکروہ ہے۔ اور تحویب کے معنی ہیں باخبر کرنے کی طرف عود کرنا۔ اور یہ لوگوں کے عرف کے موافق ہے۔ اور یہ تحویب ایسی ہے جسے عہد صحابہ کے بعد لوگوں کی حالتوں کے بدل جانے کی وجہ سے علمائے کوفہ نے ایجاد کیا ہے اور انہوں نے اس تحویب کے ساتھ فجر کو خاص کیا ہے جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے۔ اور متاخرین فقہاء نے تمام نمازوں میں تصویب کو مستحسن قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ امور دینیہ میں سستی ظاہر ہوگئی ہے۔ ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میں اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں سمجھتا کہ مؤذن تمام نمازوں میں امیر کو کہے: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، الصَّلَاةُ يَرْحَمُكَ الله۔ اور امام محمد نے اس کو مستبعد سمجھا کیونکہ جماعت کے معاملہ میں سب برابر ہیں۔ ابو یوسف نے حکام کو اس تحویب کے ساتھ اس لئے خاص کیا کہ مسلمانوں کے امور میں ان کی مشغولیت زیادہ ہے تاکہ ان کی جماعت فوت نہ ہو جائے۔ اور اسی حکم قاضی اور مفتی ہے۔
Tathwīb in the Fajr (prayer): saying 'Come to prayer, come to success' twice between the adhan and iqama is good (hasan) because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, and it is disliked (makruh) in other prayers. Its meaning is returning to the announcement, and it is according to their custom. This tathwīb was innovated by the scholars of Kufa after the era of the Companions due to the change in people's conditions, and they specified it for Fajr for the reason we mentioned. The later scholars considered it good (mustahsan) in all prayers due to the appearance of negligence in religious matters. Abu Yusuf said: I do not see any harm if the mu'adhdhin says to the ruler in all prayers: 'Peace be upon you, O ruler, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings; come to prayer, come to success; may Allah have mercy on you.' Muhammad considered it far-fetched because people are equal in the matter of congregation. Abu Yusuf specified them (rulers) for this due to their increased engagement in the affairs of the Muslims so that they would not miss the congregation. And similarly for the judge and the mufti.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (hukm) along with an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by stating the ruling on tathwīb (also called tanwīb or tashwīb) during the Fajr prayer: it is hasan (commendable) to say 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between the adhan and iqama. The reason given is that Fajr is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so this extra reminder is beneficial. For all other prayers, it is makruh (disliked). The text then clarifies that tathwīb means returning to the announcement—i.e., repeating the call—and its form follows local custom. Importantly, this practice was not from the time of the Prophet or the Companions; it was innovated by the scholars of Kufa after the Sahaba due to changing circumstances. They specifically confined it to Fajr. However, later scholars (muta'akhkhirūn) regarded it as mustahsan (recommended) in all prayers because people became negligent in religious duties. Then the passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf permits tathwīb for rulers in all prayers, using specific words of greeting. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, arguing that all people are equal regarding congregation. Abu Yusuf's justification is that rulers are busy with public affairs and might miss the congregation, so a special tathwīb helps them. The ruling is extended to judges and muftis as well. This lesson establishes the basic ruling and the key ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التَّنْوِيبُ / التَّثْوِيبُ (al-tanwīb / al-tathwīb): In Hanafi fiqh, tathwīb is an extra call between adhan and iqama to alert people to prayer, especially in Fajr. Here it refers to saying 'hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah' twice.
حَسَنٌ (hasan): A legal category meaning commendable or recommended, but not obligatory or sunnah mu'akkadah. It is a level above mubah.
مُسْتَحْسَنٌ (mustahsan): A ruling that is considered good by later scholars (muta'akhkhirūn), often based on istihsan or changing circumstances. It indicates a preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling (hukm) of tathwīb in the Fajr prayer?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah Mu'akkadah
C) Hasan (commendable)
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Tathwīb is a commendable practice in Fajr, later extended to all prayers, and a legitimate intra-Hanafi dispute exists regarding its use for rulers.

Definition and Types of Tathwīb
Definition and types of tathwīb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tathwīb in Hanafi terminology and distinguish between qadim and muhdath tathwīb.

Core Idea
Tathwīb is an additional call between adhan and iqama; its wording is flexible and follows local custom.

Tathwīb is a practice that has evolved in the Hanafi school. Understanding its lexical and technical meaning, as well as its two types, is essential before exploring the intra-school dispute on its scope. This lesson introduces the foundational definitions and characteristics of tathwīb as presented in Ashraf al-Hidaya.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwīb linguistically and technically
Identify the lexical meaning (returning) and the technical meaning (informing after informing) as defined by Mulla Ali Qari.
The benefit of action returns to the person.
2
Distinguish between qadim and muhdath tathwīb
Qadim is the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' originally after adhan; muhdath is the repetition of hayya 'ala al-salah etc. created by Kufan scholars.
Qadim has prophetic origin; muhdath is a bid'ah hasanah.
3
Identify the flexible nature of muhdath tathwīb
The text states that there is no fixed wording or language; even a cough suffices if understood. It follows local custom.
This is a key Hanafi principle of flexibility in custom-based practices.
4
Understand why muhdath tathwīb is considered a bid'ah hasanah
It was not present in the time of the Prophet or Companions, but later scholars collectively considered it good, and the hadith 'what Muslims consider good is good with Allah' supports it.
This illustrates the Hanafi concept of bid'ah hasanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح: تحویب کے لغوی معنی رجوع اور عود کرنے کے ہیں۔ اس سے ثواب آتا ہے کیونکہ آدمی کے عمل کی منفعت اسی کی طرف عود کرتی ہے اور اسی سے مشابہت ہے کیونکہ لوگ اس کی طرف لوٹ لوٹ کر آتے ہیں۔ اور شریعت کی اصطلاح میں تحویب اعلام بعد الاعلام کو کہتے ہیں۔ ملا علی قاری نے لکھا ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان نماز کے اعلان کا نام تحویب ہے۔

تحویب کی اقسام: تحویب کی دو قسمیں ہیں: اول تحویب قدیم اور وہ الصَّلَاةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ ہے۔ فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ یہ اذان کے بعد تھی اور کتاب الآثار میں امام محمد کا قول بھی اس پر صریح دلالت کرتا ہے۔ لیکن لوگوں نے اس تحویب کو اذان میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل کر لیا۔ مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ وہ حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل اذان تھی جیسا کہ متن میں مذکور ہے اور معمول ہے۔ اور حدیث: "بِلالُ اجْعَلْهُ فِي أَذَانِكَ" اس پر کھلی دلیل ہے۔

دوسری قسم تحویب محدث: تحویب محدث یہ ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو بار حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ یا اس کے ہم معنی اپنے یہاں کے عرف کے مطابق کہے۔ تحویب میں نہ الفاظ مخصوص ہیں اور نہ زبان کا عربی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر الصَّلَاةُ الصَّلَاةُ کہہ دیا، یا قَامَتْ قَامَتْ کہا تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی شخص یوں کہہ دے کہ نماز تیار ہے یا نماز ہوتی ہے یا اور کوئی لفظ تو بھی درست ہے۔ اور اگر صرف کھانسنے سے لوگ سمجھ جائیں تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جیسا جہاں دستور ہو اسی کے مطابق وہاں تحویب کی جائے۔

اس تحویب کو محدث اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ نہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں تھی اور نہ عہد صحابہ میں، بلکہ تابعین کے دور میں جب لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو گئے اور لوگ دینی امور میں سستی کرنے لگے تو علمائے کوفہ نے اس کو ایجاد کیا تو گویا یہ بدعت حسنہ ہے۔ حسنہ اس لئے ہے کہ فقہاء متقدمین و متاخرین نے اس کو مستحسن قرار دیا، اور مسلمان جس چیز کو حسن قرار دیں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی حسن ہے۔ اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے: "مَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَسَنًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ حَسَنٌ، وَمَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ قَبِيحًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ قَبِيحٌ"

رہی یہ بات کہ تحویب محدث صرف فجر کی نماز میں جائز ہے یا تمام نمازوں میں۔ سو اس بارے میں فقہاء متقدمین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ صرف فجر میں جائز ہے، اس کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے۔ اس کی تائید ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے: عَنْ بِلالٍ قَالَ: أَمَرَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ أَنْ لَا أُثَوِّبَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَّا فِي الْفَجْرِ۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت علی نے ایک مؤذن کو عشاء میں تحویب کرتے دیکھا تو فرمایا: "أَخْرِجُوا هَذَا الْمُبْتَدِعَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ"۔

فقہاء متاخرین نے کہا کہ تحویب محدث تمام نمازوں میں جائز ہے۔ عین البدایہ میں شرح نقایہ کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ متاخرین کے نزدیک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں تحویب مستحسن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لوگ دینی امور میں تساہل اور سستی کرنے لگے، لہٰذا جب فجر میں نیند کی غفلت میں تحویب جائز ہوئی تو سستی اور کام کاج کی غفلتوں کے ساتھ تو بدرجہ اولیٰ جائز ہوگی۔

لیکن متاخرین کا یہ خیال درست نہیں کیونکہ نیند کی غفلت تو غیر اختیاری ہے اور اس میں کوئی کوتاہی و سرکشی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ لیلۃ العریس کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب صبح کی نماز میں سو گئے تھے تو صحابہ کو بڑی تشویش ہوئی کہ ہم نے بڑی کوتاہی کی، تو رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا: "لَا تَفْرِيطَ فِي النَّوْمِ" یعنی نیند میں اپنی طرف سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارواح قبضۂ قدرت میں ہیں، اس نے جب چاہا ان کو چھوڑا۔

تفریط امر کن ہے اور صرف بیداری کی حالت میں ہوتی ہے۔ پس فجر میں تحویب بغیر تفریط کے غیر اختیاری حالت میں تھی تو اب اس کو دوسرے اوقات کی نمازوں میں جو صورت تفریط اور اختیاری حالت ہے قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک قاضیوں اور حاکموں کے لئے فجر کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی تحویب جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ مؤذن مسلمانوں کے حاکم کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ تحویب کرے: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، الصَّلَاةُ يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ۔
Explanation: The lexical meaning of tathwīb is returning and coming back. Reward comes from it because the benefit of a person's action returns to him, and it is similar to him because people come back to it repeatedly. In Shari'ah terminology, tathwīb is informing after informing. Mulla 'Ali al-Qari wrote that the announcement of prayer between the adhan and iqama is called tathwīb.

Types of tathwīb: There are two types. First: qadim (ancient) tathwīb, which is 'al-salat khayr min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). According to Fakhr al-Islam, the correct view is that this was after the adhan, and the statement of Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar also clearly indicates this. But people inserted this tathwīb into the adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah.' However, the correct view is that it was after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' as mentioned in the matn and as is the practice. The hadith 'O Bilal, include it in your adhan' is clear evidence.

Second type: muhdath (innovated) tathwīb. This is to say 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between the adhan and iqama, or something equivalent according to local custom. In tathwīb, there is no specific wording, nor is it necessary to be in Arabic. Thus, if one says 'al-salah, al-salah' or 'qamat, qamat,' that is also tathwīb. Similarly, if someone says 'prayer is ready' or 'prayer is happening' or any other word, it is valid. And if people understand just from a cough, that is also tathwīb. The conclusion is that tathwīb should be done according to the custom of the place.

This tathwīb is called muhdath (innovated) because it was not present in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) nor in the era of the Companions, but in the time of the Tabi'in, when people's conditions changed and they became lazy in religious matters, the scholars of Kufa invented it. So it is a bid'ah hasanah (good innovation). It is hasan because the early and later jurists considered it good, and what the Muslims consider good is good with Allah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'What the believers consider good is good with Allah, and what they consider bad is bad with Allah.'

As for whether muhdath tathwīb is permissible only in Fajr or in all prayers, the school of the early jurists (mutaqaddimin) is that it is permissible only in Fajr, and not in other prayers, because that is the time of sleep and heedlessness. This is supported by the hadith of Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah: from Bilal who said: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded me not to do tathwīb in any prayer except Fajr.' In one narration, 'Ali saw a mu'adhdhin doing tathwīb in 'Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque.'

The later jurists (muta'akhkhirin) said that muhdath tathwīb is permissible in all prayers. In 'Ayn al-Bidayah, quoting Sharh al-Niqayah, it is written that according to the later scholars, tathwīb is recommended (mustahsan) in all prayers except Maghrib. The evidence is that people have become negligent and lazy in religious matters. So when tathwīb was allowed in Fajr due to the heedlessness of sleep, then it should be allowed even more so for the heedlessness of laziness and work.

But this opinion of the later scholars is not correct, because the heedlessness of sleep is involuntary and involves no shortcoming or disobedience. As in the hadith of Laylat al-'Arus, when they slept through the morning prayer, the Companions were very worried that they had committed a great shortcoming, but the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no shortcoming in sleep' meaning that there is no shortcoming on one's part in sleep, because souls are in the control of Allah; He releases them when He wills.

Shortcoming (tafrit) is a command and occurs only in the state of wakefulness. So tathwīb in Fajr was without shortcoming, in an involuntary state. Now to analogize it to other prayers, which involve shortcoming and voluntary state, is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Imam Abu Yusuf said: In my view, for judges and rulers, tathwīb is permissible in prayers other than Fajr. So the mu'adhdhin should do tathwīb for the Muslim ruler with these words: 'Peace be upon you, O ruler, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings; come to prayer, come to success; prayer, may Allah have mercy on you.'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn's ruling. It begins by defining tathwīb linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it means returning; technically, it is an announcement after an announcement, specifically the call made between adhan and iqama. The author then distinguishes two types of tathwīb. The first is qadim (ancient): the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' which, according to Fakhr al-Islam and Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Athar, was originally said after the adhan (specifically after 'hayya 'ala al-falah') before being integrated into the adhan itself by later practice. The hadith 'Bilal, include it in your adhan' supports this. The second is muhdath (innovated): repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar phrases between adhan and iqama. This innovation was introduced by the Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in due to growing religious negligence. The author notes that for muhdath tathwīb, the wording is not fixed—anything that alerts people suffices, even a cough, as long as it follows local custom. The author then presents a major dispute: early jurists (mutaqaddimun) restrict muhdath tathwīb to Fajr, citing the hadith of Bilal and the incident of 'Ali expelling a mu'adhdhin who did tathwīb in 'Isha. Later jurists (muta'akhkhirun) extend it to all prayers except Maghrib, using qiyas (analogy): if Fajr's sleep-related heedlessness justifies tathwīb, then work-related negligence (which is voluntary) should justify it even more. However, the author sides with the early jurists, arguing that sleep is involuntary while work-related negligence is a choice, making the analogy invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The passage concludes with Abu Yusuf's view allowing tathwīb specifically for rulers and judges in all prayers due to their heavy responsibilities—a compromise position rooted in practical necessity.

Key Terms
تَحْوِيبٌ قَدِيمٌ (tahwīb qadīm): The ancient tathwīb consisting of the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). The author clarifies it was originally said after the adhan, not as part of it.
تَحْوِيبٌ مُحْدَثٌ (tahwīb muḥdath): The innovated tathwīb of repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar words between adhan and iqama. It was introduced by Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in.
بِدْعَةٌ حَسَنَةٌ (bid'ah hasanah): An innovation in religious practice that is considered good because it serves a beneficial purpose and has been accepted by the community of scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, tathwīb can be performed with:
A) Only Arabic phrases
B) Any phrase that alerts people, even a cough
C) The exact words 'hayya 'ala al-salah' only
D) Only the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm'

Key Takeaway
Tathwīb in Hanafi fiqh is a flexible alert after the adhan; its wording is not fixed and may follow local custom.
