The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Tathwīb in All Prayers or Only Fajr?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of muhdath tathwīb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the mutaqaddimun and muta'akhkhirun regarding tathwīb and evaluate the author's refutation of the later view.

Core Idea
Sleep is involuntary; work-related negligence is voluntary — the later scholars' analogy for tathwīb in all prayers is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

After defining tathwīb and its types, the author turns to a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: whether muhdath tathwīb is permissible only in Fajr (as the early jurists held) or in all prayers except Maghrib (as the later jurists argued). The dispute turns on the nature of the heedlessness that tathwīb addresses and the validity of analogical reasoning. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the author's decisive refutation.

Guided Path
1
State the early Hanafi view
Mutaqaddimun: tathwīb only in Fajr, because that is the time of sleep and heedlessness. They cite the hadith of Bilal and the incident of 'Ali.
2
State the later Hanafi view
Muta'akhkhirun: tathwīb in all prayers except Maghrib. They use qiyas: if allowed for involuntary sleep, it should be more so for voluntary negligence.
The later view is widely practiced.
3
Examine the early evidence
The hadith 'Amarani an la uthawwiba illa fi al-fajr' is a clear command. The expulsion of the mu'adhdhin in 'Isha by 'Ali reinforces it.
Dalil is explicit.
4
Analyse the later evidence and the author's refutation
The later scholars' qiyas is refuted because sleep is involuntary (no shortcoming) while work negligence is voluntary (shortcoming). The hadith 'La tafrita fi al-nawm' shows there is no shortcoming in sleep.
The author calls this qiyas ma'a al-fariq (false analogy).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, some Hanafis restrict tathwīb to Fajr, others extend it. The author sides with the early view.
The mufta bihi may vary by region.

Source Text

تشریح: تحویب کے لغوی معنی رجوع اور عود کرنے کے ہیں۔ اس سے ثواب آتا ہے کیونکہ آدمی کے عمل کی منفعت اسی کی طرف عود کرتی ہے اور اسی سے مشابہت ہے کیونکہ لوگ اس کی طرف لوٹ لوٹ کر آتے ہیں۔ اور شریعت کی اصطلاح میں تحویب اعلام بعد الاعلام کو کہتے ہیں۔ ملا علی قاری نے لکھا ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان نماز کے اعلان کا نام تحویب ہے۔

تحویب کی اقسام: تحویب کی دو قسمیں ہیں: اول تحویب قدیم اور وہ الصَّلَاةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ ہے۔ فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ یہ اذان کے بعد تھی اور کتاب الآثار میں امام محمد کا قول بھی اس پر صریح دلالت کرتا ہے۔ لیکن لوگوں نے اس تحویب کو اذان میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل کر لیا۔ مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ وہ حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل اذان تھی جیسا کہ متن میں مذکور ہے اور معمول ہے۔ اور حدیث: "بِلالُ اجْعَلْهُ فِي أَذَانِكَ" اس پر کھلی دلیل ہے۔

دوسری قسم تحویب محدث: تحویب محدث یہ ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو بار حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ یا اس کے ہم معنی اپنے یہاں کے عرف کے مطابق کہے۔ تحویب میں نہ الفاظ مخصوص ہیں اور نہ زبان کا عربی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر الصَّلَاةُ الصَّلَاةُ کہہ دیا، یا قَامَتْ قَامَتْ کہا تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی شخص یوں کہہ دے کہ نماز تیار ہے یا نماز ہوتی ہے یا اور کوئی لفظ تو بھی درست ہے۔ اور اگر صرف کھانسنے سے لوگ سمجھ جائیں تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جیسا جہاں دستور ہو اسی کے مطابق وہاں تحویب کی جائے۔

اس تحویب کو محدث اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ نہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں تھی اور نہ عہد صحابہ میں، بلکہ تابعین کے دور میں جب لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو گئے اور لوگ دینی امور میں سستی کرنے لگے تو علمائے کوفہ نے اس کو ایجاد کیا تو گویا یہ بدعت حسنہ ہے۔ حسنہ اس لئے ہے کہ فقہاء متقدمین و متاخرین نے اس کو مستحسن قرار دیا، اور مسلمان جس چیز کو حسن قرار دیں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی حسن ہے۔ اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے: "مَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَسَنًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ حَسَنٌ، وَمَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ قَبِيحًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ قَبِيحٌ"

رہی یہ بات کہ تحویب محدث صرف فجر کی نماز میں جائز ہے یا تمام نمازوں میں۔ سو اس بارے میں فقہاء متقدمین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ صرف فجر میں جائز ہے، اس کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے۔ اس کی تائید ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے: عَنْ بِلالٍ قَالَ: أَمَرَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ أَنْ لَا أُثَوِّبَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَّا فِي الْفَجْرِ۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت علی نے ایک مؤذن کو عشاء میں تحویب کرتے دیکھا تو فرمایا: "أَخْرِجُوا هَذَا الْمُبْتَدِعَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ"۔

فقہاء متاخرین نے کہا کہ تحویب محدث تمام نمازوں میں جائز ہے۔ عین البدایہ میں شرح نقایہ کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ متاخرین کے نزدیک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں تحویب مستحسن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لوگ دینی امور میں تساہل اور سستی کرنے لگے، لہٰذا جب فجر میں نیند کی غفلت میں تحویب جائز ہوئی تو سستی اور کام کاج کی غفلتوں کے ساتھ تو بدرجہ اولیٰ جائز ہوگی۔

لیکن متاخرین کا یہ خیال درست نہیں کیونکہ نیند کی غفلت تو غیر اختیاری ہے اور اس میں کوئی کوتاہی و سرکشی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ لیلۃ العریس کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب صبح کی نماز میں سو گئے تھے تو صحابہ کو بڑی تشویش ہوئی کہ ہم نے بڑی کوتاہی کی، تو رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا: "لَا تَفْرِيطَ فِي النَّوْمِ" یعنی نیند میں اپنی طرف سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارواح قبضۂ قدرت میں ہیں، اس نے جب چاہا ان کو چھوڑا۔

تفریط امر کن ہے اور صرف بیداری کی حالت میں ہوتی ہے۔ پس فجر میں تحویب بغیر تفریط کے غیر اختیاری حالت میں تھی تو اب اس کو دوسرے اوقات کی نمازوں میں جو صورت تفریط اور اختیاری حالت ہے قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک قاضیوں اور حاکموں کے لئے فجر کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی تحویب جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ مؤذن مسلمانوں کے حاکم کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ تحویب کرے: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، الصَّلَاةُ يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ۔
Explanation: The lexical meaning of tathwīb is returning and coming back. Reward comes from it because the benefit of a person's action returns to him, and it is similar to him because people come back to it repeatedly. In Shari'ah terminology, tathwīb is informing after informing. Mulla 'Ali al-Qari wrote that the announcement of prayer between the adhan and iqama is called tathwīb.

Types of tathwīb: There are two types. First: qadim (ancient) tathwīb, which is 'al-salat khayr min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). According to Fakhr al-Islam, the correct view is that this was after the adhan, and the statement of Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar also clearly indicates this. But people inserted this tathwīb into the adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah.' However, the correct view is that it was after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' as mentioned in the matn and as is the practice. The hadith 'O Bilal, include it in your adhan' is clear evidence.

Second type: muhdath (innovated) tathwīb. This is to say 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between the adhan and iqama, or something equivalent according to local custom. In tathwīb, there is no specific wording, nor is it necessary to be in Arabic. Thus, if one says 'al-salah, al-salah' or 'qamat, qamat,' that is also tathwīb. Similarly, if someone says 'prayer is ready' or 'prayer is happening' or any other word, it is valid. And if people understand just from a cough, that is also tathwīb. The conclusion is that tathwīb should be done according to the custom of the place.

This tathwīb is called muhdath (innovated) because it was not present in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) nor in the era of the Companions, but in the time of the Tabi'in, when people's conditions changed and they became lazy in religious matters, the scholars of Kufa invented it. So it is a bid'ah hasanah (good innovation). It is hasan because the early and later jurists considered it good, and what the Muslims consider good is good with Allah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'What the believers consider good is good with Allah, and what they consider bad is bad with Allah.'

As for whether muhdath tathwīb is permissible only in Fajr or in all prayers, the school of the early jurists (mutaqaddimin) is that it is permissible only in Fajr, and not in other prayers, because that is the time of sleep and heedlessness. This is supported by the hadith of Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah: from Bilal who said: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded me not to do tathwīb in any prayer except Fajr.' In one narration, 'Ali saw a mu'adhdhin doing tathwīb in 'Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque.'

The later jurists (muta'akhkhirin) said that muhdath tathwīb is permissible in all prayers. In 'Ayn al-Bidayah, quoting Sharh al-Niqayah, it is written that according to the later scholars, tathwīb is recommended (mustahsan) in all prayers except Maghrib. The evidence is that people have become negligent and lazy in religious matters. So when tathwīb was allowed in Fajr due to the heedlessness of sleep, then it should be allowed even more so for the heedlessness of laziness and work.

But this opinion of the later scholars is not correct, because the heedlessness of sleep is involuntary and involves no shortcoming or disobedience. As in the hadith of Laylat al-'Arus, when they slept through the morning prayer, the Companions were very worried that they had committed a great shortcoming, but the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no shortcoming in sleep' meaning that there is no shortcoming on one's part in sleep, because souls are in the control of Allah; He releases them when He wills.

Shortcoming (tafrit) is a command and occurs only in the state of wakefulness. So tathwīb in Fajr was without shortcoming, in an involuntary state. Now to analogize it to other prayers, which involve shortcoming and voluntary state, is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Imam Abu Yusuf said: In my view, for judges and rulers, tathwīb is permissible in prayers other than Fajr. So the mu'adhdhin should do tathwīb for the Muslim ruler with these words: 'Peace be upon you, O ruler, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings; come to prayer, come to success; prayer, may Allah have mercy on you.'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn's ruling. It begins by defining tathwīb linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it means returning; technically, it is an announcement after an announcement, specifically the call made between adhan and iqama. The author then distinguishes two types of tathwīb. The first is qadim (ancient): the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' which, according to Fakhr al-Islam and Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Athar, was originally said after the adhan (specifically after 'hayya 'ala al-falah') before being integrated into the adhan itself by later practice. The hadith 'Bilal, include it in your adhan' supports this. The second is muhdath (innovated): repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar phrases between adhan and iqama. This innovation was introduced by the Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in due to growing religious negligence. The author notes that for muhdath tathwīb, the wording is not fixed—anything that alerts people suffices, even a cough, as long as it follows local custom. The author then presents a major dispute: early jurists (mutaqaddimun) restrict muhdath tathwīb to Fajr, citing the hadith of Bilal and the incident of 'Ali expelling a mu'adhdhin who did tathwīb in 'Isha. Later jurists (muta'akhkhirun) extend it to all prayers except Maghrib, using qiyas (analogy): if Fajr's sleep-related heedlessness justifies tathwīb, then work-related negligence (which is voluntary) should justify it even more. However, the author sides with the early jurists, arguing that sleep is involuntary while work-related negligence is a choice, making the analogy invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The passage concludes with Abu Yusuf's view allowing tathwīb specifically for rulers and judges in all prayers due to their heavy responsibilities—a compromise position rooted in practical necessity.

Key Terms
تَحْوِيبٌ قَدِيمٌ (tahwīb qadīm): The ancient tathwīb consisting of the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). The author clarifies it was originally said after the adhan, not as part of it.
تَحْوِيبٌ مُحْدَثٌ (tahwīb muḥdath): The innovated tathwīb of repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar words between adhan and iqama. It was introduced by Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in.
بِدْعَةٌ حَسَنَةٌ (bid'ah hasanah): An innovation in religious practice that is considered good because it serves a beneficial purpose and has been accepted by the community of scholars.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the later scholars' analogy allowing tathwīb in all prayers?
A) Because there is no hadith supporting it
B) Because the heedlessness of sleep is involuntary while work-related negligence is voluntary
C) Because only the Prophet can permit tathwīb
D) Because tathwīb is only for Fajr

Key Takeaway
The early Hanafi view restricts muhdath tathwīb to Fajr, and the author's critique of the qiyas used by later scholars is based on the distinction between involuntary sleep and voluntary shortcoming.

Abu Yusuf's Special Permission and the Ruling for Rulers
Abu Yusuf's exception for rulers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's exceptional ruling on tathwīb for rulers and identify the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Yusuf permitted tathwīb for rulers in all prayers due to their responsibility, but the mufta bihi today often follows the later scholars.

After presenting the dispute between early and later scholars, the text records a unique position from Imam Abu Yusuf, one of the founding authorities of the Hanafi school. He allowed tathwīb in prayers other than Fajr specifically for rulers and judges, acknowledging their heavy engagement in state affairs. This lesson examines that exceptional view and its place in the school's hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Yusuf's exceptional ruling
He permitted tathwīb for rulers and judges in prayers other than Fajr, due to their engagement in state affairs.
2
Describe the prescribed wording
The mu'adhdhin addresses the ruler with 'Peace be upon you, O ruler...' etc. This is a special formula.
It shows respect and urgency.
3
Compare with the earlier and later views
This is a middle position: not as restrictive as the early view (only Fajr) but not as broad as the later view (all prayers for everyone).
It is specific to rulers.
4
Determine the mufta bihi today
Many Hanafi communities have adopted the later view for all prayers, but Abu Yusuf's view is sometimes invoked for leaders.
The author of the sharh does not explicitly endorse Abu Yusuf's view.

تشریح: تحویب کے لغوی معنی رجوع اور عود کرنے کے ہیں۔ اس سے ثواب آتا ہے کیونکہ آدمی کے عمل کی منفعت اسی کی طرف عود کرتی ہے اور اسی سے مشابہت ہے کیونکہ لوگ اس کی طرف لوٹ لوٹ کر آتے ہیں۔ اور شریعت کی اصطلاح میں تحویب اعلام بعد الاعلام کو کہتے ہیں۔ ملا علی قاری نے لکھا ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان نماز کے اعلان کا نام تحویب ہے۔

تحویب کی اقسام: تحویب کی دو قسمیں ہیں: اول تحویب قدیم اور وہ الصَّلَاةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ ہے۔ فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ یہ اذان کے بعد تھی اور کتاب الآثار میں امام محمد کا قول بھی اس پر صریح دلالت کرتا ہے۔ لیکن لوگوں نے اس تحویب کو اذان میں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل کر لیا۔ مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ وہ حی علی الفلاح کے بعد داخل اذان تھی جیسا کہ متن میں مذکور ہے اور معمول ہے۔ اور حدیث: "بِلالُ اجْعَلْهُ فِي أَذَانِكَ" اس پر کھلی دلیل ہے۔

دوسری قسم تحویب محدث: تحویب محدث یہ ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو بار حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ یا اس کے ہم معنی اپنے یہاں کے عرف کے مطابق کہے۔ تحویب میں نہ الفاظ مخصوص ہیں اور نہ زبان کا عربی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر الصَّلَاةُ الصَّلَاةُ کہہ دیا، یا قَامَتْ قَامَتْ کہا تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی شخص یوں کہہ دے کہ نماز تیار ہے یا نماز ہوتی ہے یا اور کوئی لفظ تو بھی درست ہے۔ اور اگر صرف کھانسنے سے لوگ سمجھ جائیں تو یہ بھی تحویب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جیسا جہاں دستور ہو اسی کے مطابق وہاں تحویب کی جائے۔

اس تحویب کو محدث اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ نہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں تھی اور نہ عہد صحابہ میں، بلکہ تابعین کے دور میں جب لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو گئے اور لوگ دینی امور میں سستی کرنے لگے تو علمائے کوفہ نے اس کو ایجاد کیا تو گویا یہ بدعت حسنہ ہے۔ حسنہ اس لئے ہے کہ فقہاء متقدمین و متاخرین نے اس کو مستحسن قرار دیا، اور مسلمان جس چیز کو حسن قرار دیں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی حسن ہے۔ اللہ کے رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے: "مَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَسَنًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ حَسَنٌ، وَمَا رَآهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ قَبِيحًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ قَبِيحٌ"

رہی یہ بات کہ تحویب محدث صرف فجر کی نماز میں جائز ہے یا تمام نمازوں میں۔ سو اس بارے میں فقہاء متقدمین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ صرف فجر میں جائز ہے، اس کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے۔ اس کی تائید ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے: عَنْ بِلالٍ قَالَ: أَمَرَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ أَنْ لَا أُثَوِّبَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَّا فِي الْفَجْرِ۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت علی نے ایک مؤذن کو عشاء میں تحویب کرتے دیکھا تو فرمایا: "أَخْرِجُوا هَذَا الْمُبْتَدِعَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ"۔

فقہاء متاخرین نے کہا کہ تحویب محدث تمام نمازوں میں جائز ہے۔ عین البدایہ میں شرح نقایہ کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ متاخرین کے نزدیک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں تحویب مستحسن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لوگ دینی امور میں تساہل اور سستی کرنے لگے، لہٰذا جب فجر میں نیند کی غفلت میں تحویب جائز ہوئی تو سستی اور کام کاج کی غفلتوں کے ساتھ تو بدرجہ اولیٰ جائز ہوگی۔

لیکن متاخرین کا یہ خیال درست نہیں کیونکہ نیند کی غفلت تو غیر اختیاری ہے اور اس میں کوئی کوتاہی و سرکشی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ لیلۃ العریس کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب صبح کی نماز میں سو گئے تھے تو صحابہ کو بڑی تشویش ہوئی کہ ہم نے بڑی کوتاہی کی، تو رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا: "لَا تَفْرِيطَ فِي النَّوْمِ" یعنی نیند میں اپنی طرف سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارواح قبضۂ قدرت میں ہیں، اس نے جب چاہا ان کو چھوڑا۔

تفریط امر کن ہے اور صرف بیداری کی حالت میں ہوتی ہے۔ پس فجر میں تحویب بغیر تفریط کے غیر اختیاری حالت میں تھی تو اب اس کو دوسرے اوقات کی نمازوں میں جو صورت تفریط اور اختیاری حالت ہے قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک قاضیوں اور حاکموں کے لئے فجر کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی تحویب جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ مؤذن مسلمانوں کے حاکم کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ تحویب کرے: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الْأَمِيرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ، الصَّلَاةُ يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ۔
Explanation: The lexical meaning of tathwīb is returning and coming back. Reward comes from it because the benefit of a person's action returns to him, and it is similar to him because people come back to it repeatedly. In Shari'ah terminology, tathwīb is informing after informing. Mulla 'Ali al-Qari wrote that the announcement of prayer between the adhan and iqama is called tathwīb.

Types of tathwīb: There are two types. First: qadim (ancient) tathwīb, which is 'al-salat khayr min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). According to Fakhr al-Islam, the correct view is that this was after the adhan, and the statement of Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar also clearly indicates this. But people inserted this tathwīb into the adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah.' However, the correct view is that it was after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' as mentioned in the matn and as is the practice. The hadith 'O Bilal, include it in your adhan' is clear evidence.

Second type: muhdath (innovated) tathwīb. This is to say 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice between the adhan and iqama, or something equivalent according to local custom. In tathwīb, there is no specific wording, nor is it necessary to be in Arabic. Thus, if one says 'al-salah, al-salah' or 'qamat, qamat,' that is also tathwīb. Similarly, if someone says 'prayer is ready' or 'prayer is happening' or any other word, it is valid. And if people understand just from a cough, that is also tathwīb. The conclusion is that tathwīb should be done according to the custom of the place.

This tathwīb is called muhdath (innovated) because it was not present in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) nor in the era of the Companions, but in the time of the Tabi'in, when people's conditions changed and they became lazy in religious matters, the scholars of Kufa invented it. So it is a bid'ah hasanah (good innovation). It is hasan because the early and later jurists considered it good, and what the Muslims consider good is good with Allah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'What the believers consider good is good with Allah, and what they consider bad is bad with Allah.'

As for whether muhdath tathwīb is permissible only in Fajr or in all prayers, the school of the early jurists (mutaqaddimin) is that it is permissible only in Fajr, and not in other prayers, because that is the time of sleep and heedlessness. This is supported by the hadith of Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah: from Bilal who said: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded me not to do tathwīb in any prayer except Fajr.' In one narration, 'Ali saw a mu'adhdhin doing tathwīb in 'Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque.'

The later jurists (muta'akhkhirin) said that muhdath tathwīb is permissible in all prayers. In 'Ayn al-Bidayah, quoting Sharh al-Niqayah, it is written that according to the later scholars, tathwīb is recommended (mustahsan) in all prayers except Maghrib. The evidence is that people have become negligent and lazy in religious matters. So when tathwīb was allowed in Fajr due to the heedlessness of sleep, then it should be allowed even more so for the heedlessness of laziness and work.

But this opinion of the later scholars is not correct, because the heedlessness of sleep is involuntary and involves no shortcoming or disobedience. As in the hadith of Laylat al-'Arus, when they slept through the morning prayer, the Companions were very worried that they had committed a great shortcoming, but the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no shortcoming in sleep' meaning that there is no shortcoming on one's part in sleep, because souls are in the control of Allah; He releases them when He wills.

Shortcoming (tafrit) is a command and occurs only in the state of wakefulness. So tathwīb in Fajr was without shortcoming, in an involuntary state. Now to analogize it to other prayers, which involve shortcoming and voluntary state, is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Imam Abu Yusuf said: In my view, for judges and rulers, tathwīb is permissible in prayers other than Fajr. So the mu'adhdhin should do tathwīb for the Muslim ruler with these words: 'Peace be upon you, O ruler, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings; come to prayer, come to success; prayer, may Allah have mercy on you.'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn's ruling. It begins by defining tathwīb linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it means returning; technically, it is an announcement after an announcement, specifically the call made between adhan and iqama. The author then distinguishes two types of tathwīb. The first is qadim (ancient): the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' which, according to Fakhr al-Islam and Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Athar, was originally said after the adhan (specifically after 'hayya 'ala al-falah') before being integrated into the adhan itself by later practice. The hadith 'Bilal, include it in your adhan' supports this. The second is muhdath (innovated): repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar phrases between adhan and iqama. This innovation was introduced by the Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in due to growing religious negligence. The author notes that for muhdath tathwīb, the wording is not fixed—anything that alerts people suffices, even a cough, as long as it follows local custom. The author then presents a major dispute: early jurists (mutaqaddimun) restrict muhdath tathwīb to Fajr, citing the hadith of Bilal and the incident of 'Ali expelling a mu'adhdhin who did tathwīb in 'Isha. Later jurists (muta'akhkhirun) extend it to all prayers except Maghrib, using qiyas (analogy): if Fajr's sleep-related heedlessness justifies tathwīb, then work-related negligence (which is voluntary) should justify it even more. However, the author sides with the early jurists, arguing that sleep is involuntary while work-related negligence is a choice, making the analogy invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The passage concludes with Abu Yusuf's view allowing tathwīb specifically for rulers and judges in all prayers due to their heavy responsibilities—a compromise position rooted in practical necessity.

Key Terms
تَحْوِيبٌ قَدِيمٌ (tahwīb qadīm): The ancient tathwīb consisting of the phrase 'al-salatu khayru min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep). The author clarifies it was originally said after the adhan, not as part of it.
تَحْوِيبٌ مُحْدَثٌ (tahwīb muḥdath): The innovated tathwīb of repeating 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' or similar words between adhan and iqama. It was introduced by Kufan scholars after the Tabi'in.
بِدْعَةٌ حَسَنَةٌ (bid'ah hasanah): An innovation in religious practice that is considered good because it serves a beneficial purpose and has been accepted by the community of scholars.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, tathwīb in prayers other than Fajr is permissible specifically for:
A) All Muslims
B) Only rulers and judges
C) Only the elderly
D) Only the mu'adhdhin

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Yusuf allowed tathwīb for rulers in all prayers, but this is an exception, not a general ruling.

The Scope of Taswib Muhdath: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discussion of the permissibility of taswib as a bid'ah hasanah and disagreement on its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the early and later Hanafi positions on taswib muhdath, identify the dalil for the early view, and evaluate the later Hanafis' qiyas as invalid due to qiyas ma' al-fariq.

Core Idea
Taswib muhdath is a good innovation restricted to Fajr; analogizing it to other prayers is invalid due to the involuntary nature of sleep.

In this lesson, we examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on taswib muhdath – the practice of adding a call after the adhan. While early Hanafis limited it to Fajr, later scholars extended it to all prayers via analogy. The passage critically refutes that analogy, defending the early position based on clear textual evidence and sound legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the early Hanafi position
Early Hanafis (mutqaddimin) hold that taswib muhdath is permissible only in Fajr prayer. Their evidence: the hadith from Bilal that the Prophet ﷺ ordered him not to make taswib except in Fajr, and the action of 'Ali who expelled a mu'adhdhin for making taswib in Isha.
This position is anchored in a clear, specific textual proof.
2
Identify the later Hanafi position
Later Hanafis (muta'akhkhirin) permit taswib in all prayers except Maghrib. They base this on qiyas (analogy) from Fajr: since taswib is allowed due to heedlessness of sleep, it should also be allowed due to heedlessness from laziness and work.
This extension relies on reasoning rather than direct textual evidence.
3
Examine the later Hanafis' dalil
Their proof is a qiyas: the ʿilla (effective cause) in Fajr is heedlessness (ghaflah). They argue this ʿilla is present in other prayers as well, so taswib should be permissible. They consider the ʿilla as jaliyyah (manifest).
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) from the perspective of the later scholars.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author refutes this qiyas as qiyas ma' al-fariq (analogy with a critical difference). Sleep is involuntary (ghayr ikhtiyari) and not blameworthy, whereas laziness and work are voluntary (ikhtiyari) and involve negligence (tafrīṭ). The hadith of Laylat al-ʿArus emphasizes that negligence does not occur in sleep. Therefore the ʿilla is not truly shared.
This refutation uses a nuanced understanding of the underlying cause.
5
Note additional positions
Imam Abu Yusuf permits taswib for rulers and judges in all prayers, addressing them with specific salutations. Imam Muhammad rejects this entirely, citing the equality of all before the Shari'ah. The author sides with the early Hanafi view as the mufta bihi.
These views show further internal variation within the Hanafi school.

الصلوة کہہ دیا، یا قامت قامت کہ تو یہ بھی تھو یب ہے اسی طرح اگر کوئی شخص یوں کہہ دے کہ نماز تیار ہے یا نماز ہوتی ہے یا اور کوئی لفظ ،تب بھی درست ہے اور اگر صرف کھانسنے سے لوگ سمجھ جائیں تو یہ بھی تقویب ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جیسا جہاں دستور ہو اسی کے مطابق وہاں تھو یب کی جائے ۔
اس تصویب کو محدث اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ نہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں تھی اور نہ عہد صحابہ میں ۔ بلکہ تابعین کے دور میں جب لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو گئے اور لوگ دینی امور میں سستی کرنے لگے تو علماء کو فہ نے اس کو ایجاد کیا تو گویا یہ بدعت حسنہ ہے۔ حسنہ اس لئے ہے کہ فقہاء متقدمین و متاخرین نے اس کو مستحسن قرار دیا اور مسلمان جس چیز کو حسن قرار دیں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی حسن ہے، اللہ کے بچے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے مَارَاهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَسَنًا فَهُوَ عِندَ اللهِ حَسَنَّ وَمَا رَاهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ فَبِيحًا فَهُوَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ قَبِيحٌ
یعنی مسلمان جس کو اچھا تصور کریں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی حسن ہے اور جس کو قبیح خیال کریں وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بھی قبیح ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ تصویب محدث صرف فجر کی نماز میں جائز ہے یا تمام نمازوں میں جائز ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں فقہاء متقدمین کابذہب یہ ہے کہ صرف فجر میں جائز ہے اس کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ وقت نیند اور غفلت کا ہے اس کی تائید ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے عَنْ بِلال قَالَ أَمَرَنِي رَسُولُ الله أَنْ لَا أَتُوبَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنَ الصَّلَوَةِ إِلَّا فِي الْفَجْرِ - بال کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مجھ کو حکم کیا کہ میں سوائے فجر کے کسی نماز میں تھویب نہ کروں۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت علی نے ایک مؤذن کو عشاء میں تخریب کرتے ہوئے دیکھا تو فرمایا اَخْرِجُوا هَذَا المُبْتَدُوعَ مِنَ المَسْجِدِ اس بدعتی کو مسجد سے نکالو۔
فقہا ء متاخرین نے کہا کہ تصویب محدث تمام نمازوں میں جائز ہے۔ عین البدایہ میں شرح نقایہ کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ متاخرین کے نزد یک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں تصویب مستحسن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لوگ دینی امور میں تساہل اور سستی کرنے لگے۔ لہذا جب فجر میں نیند کی غفلت میں تحویب جائز ہوئی تو سستی اور کام کاج کی غفلتوں کے ساتھ تو بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگی۔
لیکن متأخرین کا یہ خیال درست نہیں کیونکہ نیند کی غفلت تو غیر اختیاری ہے اور اس میں کوئی کوتاہی و سرکشی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ لیلتہ العریس کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب صبح کی نماز میں سب و گئے تھے تو صحابہ کو بڑی تشویش ہوئی کہ ہم نے بڑی کوتاہی کی تو رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم رمایا لَا تَفْرِيطُ فِی النُّومِ یعنی نیند میں اپنی طرف سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارواح قبضہ قدرت میں ہیں اس نے جب چاہا ان کو چھوڑا۔ تفریط امر کن، می صرف بیداری کی حالت میں ہوتی ہے پس فجر میں تصویب بغیر تفریط کے غیر اختیاری حالت میں تھی تو اب اس کو دوسرے اوقات کی نمازوں میں جو صورت تفریط اور اختیاری حالت ہے قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک قاضیوں اور حاکموں کے لئے فجر کے علاوہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی تجویب جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ مؤذن مسلمانوں کے حاکم کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ تصویب کرے السّلامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّها الأميرُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُه حتى على الصلوة حَى عَلَى الفَلَاحِ الصَّلوةُ يَرْحَمُكَ الله
امام محمد نے اس کو مستبعد قرار دیا ، وجہ استبعاد یہ ہے کہ شریعت کی نظر میں سب برابر ہیں امیر ہوں یا رعایا کے لوگ ہوں اس وجہ ۔ امیر کی کوئی خصوصیت نہیں ۔
قاضی ابو یوسف نے امراء اور مسلمین کو اس تثویب کے ساتھ اس لئے خاص کیا کہ یہ حضرات مسلمانوں کے کاموں میں زیادہ مشغول رہتے ہیں اس وجہ سے ان کو یہ خاص اعلان کر دیا جائے۔ تاکہ ان کی جماعت فوت نہ ہو جائے ۔ یہی حکم ان تمام حضرات کے لئے ہے جو مسلمانوں کے کاموں میں مشغول رہتے ہیں جیسے مفتی اور قاضی ۔
فوائکہ اذان کے بعد چالیس آیات پڑھنے کی مقدار ٹھہر کر تھو یب کرے ۔ جمیل
Say 'al-salah' or 'qamat' — this is taswib. Similarly if one says 'prayer is ready' or 'prayer happens' or any other word, it is correct. If people understand from coughing alone, that is also taswib. The outcome is that taswib should be done according to local custom. This taswib is called 'muhdath' (innovated) because it was not present in the time of the Prophet ﷺ nor in the era of the Companions. Rather, in the period of the Followers, when people's conditions changed and they became lax in religious matters, the scholars invented it, so it is a good innovation (bid'ah hasanah). It is good because the early and later jurists deemed it commendable, and whatever the Muslims deem good is good before Allah. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good before Allah, and what they consider evil is evil before Allah.' As for whether this taswib is permissible only in Fajr prayer or in all prayers, the early jurists held that it is only permissible in Fajr, not in other prayers, because this time is one of sleep and heedlessness. This is supported by the hadith of Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah from Bilal: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered me not to make taswib in any prayer except Fajr.' In another narration, 'Ali saw a mu'adhdhin making taswib in Isha and said: 'Expel this innovator from the mosque.' The later jurists said that taswib muhdath is permissible in all prayers. In 'Ayn al-Bidayah, quoting Sharh al-Niqayah, it is written that according to the later jurists, taswib is commendable in all prayers except Maghrib. Their proof is that people became negligent and lazy. Thus, when taswib was allowed in Fajr due to the heedlessness of sleep, then it is even more appropriate for the heedlessness of laziness and work. But this opinion of the later jurists is not correct, because the heedlessness of sleep is involuntary and involves no shortcoming or rebellion. In the hadith of Laylat al-'Arus, when the Companions overslept for Fajr prayer, they were greatly distressed that they had committed a lapse, but the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no negligence in sleep,' because souls are in the grasp of the Powerful; He releases them when He wills. Negligence occurs only in a waking state. So taswib in Fajr was in an involuntary state without negligence; now to analogize it to other prayers, which involve negligence and voluntary state, is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma' al-fariq). Imam Abu Yusuf said: In my view, taswib is permissible for judges and rulers in prayers other than Fajr. So the mu'adhdhin should make taswib to the ruler with the words: 'Assalamu 'alayka ayyuha al-amir, wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah, al-salah yarhamuka Allah.' Imam Muhammad rejected this; the reason for rejection is that in the view of the Shari'ah, all are equal, whether ruler or subject; the ruler has no special status. Qadi Abu Yusuf specified the taswib for rulers and Muslims in charge because these persons are more engaged in the affairs of the Muslims, so this special announcement is made for them so that they do not miss the congregation. The same ruling applies to all who are occupied with the affairs of the Muslims, such as the mufti and the judge. Benefit: After the adhan, he should wait the amount of time to recite forty verses, then make taswib.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage discusses the practice known as 'taswib al-muhdath' — the innovation of adding a call after the adhan to alert people to prayer. The author begins by defining taswib: any words or sounds (like coughing) that inform people that prayer is about to begin, done according to local custom. He then explains why it is called 'muhdath' (innovated): it did not exist at the time of the Prophet ﷺ or the Companions, but was introduced during the Tabi'een period when people became negligent in religious duties. The author presents a hadith-quote: 'What the Muslims consider good is good before Allah,' justifying it as a 'bid'ah hasanah'. He then presents the central dispute: whether taswib is limited to Fajr prayer or extends to all prayers. The early Hanafi jurists (mutqaddimin) restrict it to Fajr, citing the hadith of Bilal where the Prophet ﷺ ordered him not to make taswib except in Fajr, and the narration of 'Ali expelling a mu'adhdhin who made taswib in Isha. The later Hanafi jurists (muta'akhkhirin) permit it in all prayers except Maghrib, based on analogy (qiyas) from Fajr: since taswib was allowed in Fajr due to heedlessness (sleep), it should be even more allowed for heedlessness due to laziness and work. The author criticizes this analogy as 'qiyas ma' al-fariq' (analogy with a difference), because sleep is involuntary and not blameworthy, while negligence in other times is voluntary and blameworthy. He then mentions the position of Imam Abu Yusuf, who allowed taswib for rulers and judges in prayers other than Fajr, addressing them with specific words, but Imam Muhammad rejected this, arguing that all are equal in the Shari'ah. The passage concludes by noting that a similar ruling applies to other persons occupied with public duties, and adds a benefit: the mu'adhdhin should wait the time to recite forty verses after the adhan before making taswib.

Key Terms
تصويب محدث (taswīb muḥdath): The innovation of adding a call after the adhan, such as saying 'al-salah' or 'qamat', to alert people that prayer is about to begin.
بدعت حسنة (bidʿah ḥasanah): A good innovation that is not contrary to the Shariah and is deemed beneficial by scholars; here it refers to taswib.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyās maʿa al-fāriq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a significant difference between the original case and the new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the early Hanafi jurists (mutqaddimin), in which prayer is taswib muhdath permissible?
A) In all five daily prayers
B) Only in Fajr prayer
C) In all prayers except Maghrib
D) Only in Isha prayer

Key Takeaway
Taswib muhdath is a bid'ah hasanah restricted to Fajr in the relied-upon Hanafi view; extending it via analogy is invalid due to the unique involuntary nature of sleep negligence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Sitting Between Adhan and Iqamah: Disagreement on Maghrib
Inter-madhhab dispute on sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish and explain the three positions (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and al-Shafi'i) on sitting between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib, and identify the mufta bihi position with its dalil.

Core Idea
In Maghrib, delay is disliked; Abu Hanifa therefore requires no sitting—silence suffices.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical debate: should the mu'adhdhin sit briefly between the adhan and iqamah in Maghrib? All scholars agree that a separation is needed, but they differ on its form. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that silence is enough, while the Sahibayn insist on a brief sitting, and Imam al-Shafi'i recommends two rak'ahs. Understanding the reasoning behind each position deepens your appreciation of how usul principles (like avoiding delay) shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State Abu Hanifa's view: no sitting in Maghrib; silence is sufficient separation. Note the Sahibayn's dissent within the school.
The Sahibayn require a brief sitting by analogy with the two sermons.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's objection
They argue silence is insufficient because it occurs naturally between words of the adhan; a physical sitting is needed to create a distinct separation.
They compare it to the sitting between the two khutbahs.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
Delay in Maghrib is makruh, so the minimal separation (silence) suffices to avoid delay. The place and tone of adhan differ from khutbah, making silence acceptable.
Abu Yusuf observed Abu Hanifa practicing this.
4
Examine al-Shafi'i's position
Al-Shafi'i analogizes to other prayers and recommends two rak'ahs of nafl between adhan and iqamah. The Hanafi response: Maghrib's short time makes delay disliked, breaking the analogy.
The text says 'the difference has been mentioned'.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, supported by Abu Yusuf's testimony and the principle of avoiding delay.
Mufta bihi: no sitting in Maghrib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجْلِسُ بَيْنَ الْآذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ إِلَّا فِي الْمَغْرِبِ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَالَا يَجْلِسُ فِي الْمَغْرِبِ أَيْضًا جَلْسَةٌ خَفِيفَةً لِأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْفَضْلِ اِذِ الوَصْلُ مَكْرُوهُ وَلَا يَقَعُ الْفَصْلُ بِالسَّكْتَةِ لِوُجُودِهَا بَيْنَ كَلِمَاتِ الْأَذَانِ فَيَفْصِلُ بِالْجَلسَةِ كَمَا بَيْنَ الْخُطْبَتَيْنِ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ التَّاخِيرَ مَكْرُوهُ فَيَكْتَفِي بِأَدْنَى الْفَصْلِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْهُ وَالْمَكَانُ فِي مَسْأَلَتِنَا مُخْتَلِفٌ وَكَذَا النَّغْمَةٌ فَيَقَعُ الْفَضْلُ بِالسَّكْتَةِ وَلَا كَذلِكَ الخُطْبَةُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِى يَفْصِلُ بِرَكْعَتَيْنِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِسَائِرِ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَالْفَرْقُ قَدْ ذَكَرُنَاهُ قَالَ يَعْقُوبُ رَأَيْتُ أَبَا حَنِيفَةً يُوَدِّنُ فِى الْمَغْرِبِ وَيُقِيمُ وَلَا يَجُلِسُ بَيْنَ الْآذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ وَهُذَا يَفِيدُ مَا قُلْنَاهُ وَأنَّ الْمُسْتَحَبُّ كَوْنُ المُؤَذِنَ عَالِمًا بِالسُّنَّةِ لِقَوْله عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام وَيُوَدِّنُ لَكُمْ خياركم
ترجمہ اور اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان جلسہ کرے سوائے مغرب کے اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ مغرب میں بھی جلسہ خفیف کرے کیونکہ فصل ضروری ہے اس لئے کہ وصل مکروہ ہے۔ اور فصل سکوت سے نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ سکتہ تو کلمات اذان کے درمیان میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے پس بیٹھ کر فصل کرے جیسے دو خطبوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں ) تاخیر کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ پس تاخیر سے احتراز کرتے ہوئے کم سے کم فصل پر اکتفاء کرے اور ہمارے (اس) مسئلہ میں مکان مختلف ہے اور آواز بھی مختلف ہے لہذا سکتہ کے ساتھ فصل ہو جائے گا۔ اور خطبہ ایسا نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا دو رکعتوں کے ساتھ فصل کرے دوسری نمازوں کے ساتھ کرتے ہوئے اور فرق ہم نے ذکر کر دیا۔ یعقوب (ابو یوسف) نے کہا کہ میں نے ابو حنیفہ کو دیکھا کہ مغرب میں اذان دیتے اور اقامت کرتے اور اذان واقامت کے درمیان نہیں بیٹھتے تھے اور یہ قول ( دو باتوں کا ) فائدہ دیتا ہے (ایک) وہ جو ہم نے کہا ( دوم ) یہ کہ مستحب یہ ہے کہ اذان دینے والا عالم بالن ہو کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تمہارے واسطے وہ اذان دے جو تم میں سے بہتر ہو۔ تشریح اس بات پر تمام علماء کا اتفاق ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان وصل مکروہ ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت بلال سے فرمایا اِجْعَلْ بَيْنَ أَذَانِكَ وَإِقَامَتِكَ قَدْرَ مَا يَفْرَعُ الاكل من اكلم یعنی اے بلال اپنی اذ ان اور اقامت کے درمیان اس قدر فصل کر کہ کھانے والا اپنے کھانے سے فراغت پا جائے۔
He should sit between the adhan and iqamah except in Maghrib. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He should sit even in Maghrib a brief sitting, because separation is necessary since joining (without pause) is disliked, and separation does not occur by silence, because silence occurs between the words of the adhan, so he separates by sitting just as between the two sermons. Abu Hanifa's proof is that delay in Maghrib is disliked, so he suffices with the minimum separation to avoid it. In our issue, the place is different and likewise the tone, so separation occurs by silence; it is not so with the sermon. Al-Shafi'i said: He separates with two rak'ahs by analogy with other prayers. We have mentioned the difference. Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) said: I saw Abu Hanifa give the adhan in Maghrib and say the iqamah, and he did not sit between the adhan and iqamah. This benefits what we said, and that it is mustahabb for the mu'adhdhin to be knowledgeable in the sunnah because of his ﷺ statement: 'Let the best among you give the adhan for you.' Translation: And he should sit between the adhan and iqamah except in Maghrib. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: He should sit even in Maghrib a brief sitting, because separation is necessary since joining is disliked. Separation does not occur by silence, because silence occurs between the words of the adhan, so he sits to separate, as between the two sermons. Abu Hanifa's proof is that delay in Maghrib is disliked, so he suffices with the minimum separation to avoid delay. In our issue, the place varies and the voice varies, so separation occurs by silence; the sermon is not like that. Al-Shafi'i said: He separates with two rak'ahs by analogy with other prayers. We have mentioned the difference. Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) said: I saw Abu Hanifa give the adhan in Maghrib and say the iqamah, and he did not sit between the adhan and iqamah. This benefits what we said, and that it is mustahabb for the mu'adhdhin to be knowledgeable in the sunnah because of his ﷺ statement: 'Let the best among you give the adhan for you.' Explanation: All scholars agree that joining (without pause) between adhan and iqamah is disliked. The Prophet ﷺ said to Bilal: 'Make a gap between your adhan and iqamah such that the eater finishes his meal.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah deals with the ruling of sitting (jalsah) between the adhan and iqamah, specifically for Maghrib prayer. The main ruling: a person should sit between the adhan and iqamah in all prayers except Maghrib, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that even in Maghrib, one should sit briefly. Their reasoning is that there must be a separation (fasl) between adhan and iqamah, because joining them without any pause is makruh. The separation cannot be achieved by mere silence (saktah), because silence naturally occurs between the words of the adhan itself; thus, an intentional pause by sitting is required, just as one sits between the two sermons of Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa's proof is that delay in Maghrib is disliked (makruh), so one should suffice with the minimal separation. In the issue of adhan and iqamah, the place (the mosque) and the vocal tone differ from the khutbah, so silence suffices as separation. The passage then mentions the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who recommends separating with two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer between adhan and iqamah, by analogy with other prayers where it is sunnah to pray two rak'ahs after the adhan. The author notes that the difference has already been explained. Abu Yusuf narrates that he saw Abu Hanifa give adhan and iqamah for Maghrib without sitting between them, which supports Abu Hanifa's position. This also leads to the point that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the mu'adhdhin to be knowledgeable in the sunnah, as the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Let the best among you give the adhan for you.' The commentary adds that all scholars agree that joining the adhan and iqamah without any pause is disliked, and quotes the hadith from Bukhari: the Prophet ﷺ instructed Bilal to leave enough gap for a person to finish his meal.

Key Terms
جلسة (jalsah): Sitting between the adhan and iqamah as a form of separation. In Maghrib, Abu Hanifa omits it.
فصل (fasl): Separation or pause between adhan and iqamah. The dispute is over how to achieve it (silence, sitting, or prayer).
وصل (wasl): Joining the adhan and iqamah without any pause; this is makruh according to all scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is there no sitting between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib?
A) Because Maghrib is a short prayer
B) Because delay in Maghrib is disliked (makruh)
C) Because the Prophet ﷺ never sat in Maghrib
D) Because the Sahibayn disagreed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view that in Maghrib, silence suffices as separation between adhan and iqamah due to the dislike of delay, and this is the operative ruling for fatwa.

The Dispute on Sitting Between Adhan and Iqamah for Maghrib
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For Maghrib, Abu Hanifa avoids sitting to prevent delay; Sahibayn require a light sitting to achieve separation.

This lesson explores a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib prayer. While all schools agree that connecting adhan and iqamah without any interval is disliked (makruh), they differ on how separation is achieved—particularly for Maghrib. We will examine the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and understand the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key act and point of dispute
Determine what the act is (sitting between adhan and iqamah) and for which prayer (Maghrib). Recognize that the dispute is about whether sitting is required for Maghrib or not.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that one does not sit for Maghrib; a brief silence while standing suffices for separation (fasl).
His reasoning: delay in Maghrib is disliked, so minimal separation is preferred.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that even for Maghrib, a light sitting is required because silence alone does not constitute a valid separation.
They analogize to the sitting between the two sermons of Jumu'ah.
4
Analyze the opposing proofs
Compare the proofs: Abu Hanifa cites the dislike of delay and that the place and tone of adhan differ from iqamah, allowing silence to separate. The Sahibayn argue that silence is present within adhan itself, so it cannot effect separation, hence sitting is needed.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and determine the mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa distinguishes adhan/iqamah from the Jumu'ah sermons, pointing out differences in place, voice, and posture. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is to not sit for Maghrib.
The base matn (Hidayah) follows Abu Hanifa's view.

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اذ ان لوگوں کو دخول وقت کی خبر دیتا ہے تا کہ وہ نماز کی تیاری کر کے ادائے نماز کے لئے مسجد میں حاضر ہو جائیں اور چونکہ وصل سے یہ مقصود فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان وصل مکروہ اور فصل ضروری ہے۔ پس اگر نماز ایسی ہے جس سے پہلے تطوعا کوئی نماز مسنون یا مستحب ہو تو اذان واقامت کے درمیان نماز کے ساتھ فصل کرے مثلا فجر کی نماز سے پہلے دو رکعت اور ظہر سے پہلے چار رکعت مسنون ہیں اور عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور عشاء سے پہلے چار رکعت استحباب کے درجہ میں ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بین کل اذانین صلاة یعنی ہر دو اذان واقامت کے درمیان نماز ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ بات تین بار کہی اور تیسری بار فرمایا لِمَنْ شَاءَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يُصَلّ يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمَا تیسری بار فر مایا کہ یہ حکم اس شخص کے فرمایا لئے ہے جو چاہے اگر اس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تو ان دونوں کے درمیان جلسہ خفیفہ کے ساتھ فصل کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان جلسہ کرے اور مؤذن کو اسی درمیان میں سنت یا نفل پڑھنا اولیٰ ہے۔ اور مغرب میں امام ابوحنیفہ سے دور واسیتیں ہیں : ایک یہ کہ مغرب کی اذان واقامت کے درمیان سکوت کے ساتھ کھڑے کھڑے اتنی مقدار فصل کرنا مستحب ہے کہ جس میں چھوٹی تین آیات یا بڑی ایک آیت پڑھ سکے۔ دوم یہ کہ اس قدر فصل کرے کہ تین قدم چلنا ممکن ہو ۔ صاحبین نے کہا کہ مغرب میں بھی جلسہ کرے مگر بہت مختصر جیسے دو خطبوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بات تو طے شدہ ہے کہ اذان واقامت کے درمیان وصل مکروہ اور فصل ضروری ہے جیسا کہ یہ بات تو ہےکہ کے اور تمہید میں مذکور ہوا۔ اور یہ بات بھی تقریبا مسلم ہے کہ سکوت کے ساتھ فصل واقع نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ سکوت تو اذان کے کلمات کے درمیان میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے اس لئے بیٹھ کر فصل کرے اگر چہ مختصر ہی کیوں نہ ہو جیسے جمعہ کے دن دو خطبوں میں بیٹھ کر فصل کیا جاتا ہے۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں تاخیر کرنا مکروہ ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ سابق میں ہم نے کہا تھا کہ غروب کے بعد اور فرض سے پہلے نفل نہ پڑھے۔ پس اونی فصل یعنی سکتہ پر اکتفاء کرے تا کہ تاخیر سے بھی احتراز ہو جائے اور اذان واقامت میں فصل بھی واقع ہو جائے۔ اور صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان فصل کو دو خطبوں کے درمیان فصل پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں زمین و آسمان کا فرق ہے بایں طور کہ اذان واقامت کی جگہ مختلف ہوتی ہے اور دونوں میں آواز مختلف ہوتی ہے اس طور پر کہ اذان میں ترسل ہوتا ہے اور اقامت میں حدر ہوتا ہے نیز دونوں میں مؤذن کی ہیئت مختلف ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اذان کے وقت وہ اپنی دونوں انگلیاں دونوں کانوں میں داخل کرتا ہے اور اقامت میں ہاتھ چھوڑے رکھتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف خطبہ ہے کہ دونوں خطبوں کی جگہ ایک، دونوں خطبوں میں نغمہ اور و آواز متحد اور دو نوں خطبوں میں خطیب کی ہیئت متحد ہے پس اس فرق کی موجودگی میں ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا کیسے درست ہوگا۔
امام شافعی نے کہا کہ مغرب کی اذان اور اقامت میں دور کھتوں سے فصل کرے اور دلیل میں فرمایا کہ مغرب کو باقی نمازوں پر قیاس کیا جائے۔
And he sits between the adhan and iqamah except for Maghrib, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He sits for Maghrib as well, a light sitting, because separation (fasl) is necessary since connecting (wasl) is disliked, and separation does not occur by silence because silence is also found between the words of the adhan. So he separates by sitting, as between the two sermons. And for Abu Hanifa, delay in Maghrib is disliked, so he suffices with the minimum separation to avoid it. And the place in our issue is different, and likewise the tone, so separation occurs by silence, but not so for the sermon. And al-Shafi'i said: He separates by two rak'ahs, analogizing to other prayers, and the difference we have mentioned. Ya'qub said: I saw Abu Hanifa giving adhan for Maghrib and then iqamah, and he did not sit between the adhan and iqamah. And this supports what we said, and that it is recommended for the mu'adhdhin to be knowledgeable in the Sunnah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let the best of you give the adhan for you.'

Commentary: The explanation is that all scholars agree that connecting (wasl) between adhan and iqamah is disliked. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah a measure sufficient for the eater to finish his meal.' Another proof is that the purpose of the adhan is to inform people of the entry of time so they prepare and come to the mosque for prayer. Since connecting defeats this purpose, connecting between adhan and iqamah is disliked and separation is necessary. So if the prayer has a recommended sunnah or nafl prayer before it, one separates by that prayer, e.g., two rak'ahs before Fajr, four before Zuhr, four before Asr, four before Isha. The proof is that the Prophet said: 'Between every two adhans (i.e., adhan and iqamah) there is a prayer.' He said it three times, and the third time said: 'For whoever wishes; and if he does not pray, let him separate between them (by a light sitting).' The conclusion: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one sits between adhan and iqamah for all prayers except Maghrib, and it is better for the mu'adhdhin to pray sunnah or nafl in that interval. For Maghrib, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one is that standing in silence for the duration of three short verses or one long verse is recommended; the second is that one should separate by enough time to take three steps. The two (Sahibayn) said that for Maghrib also one should sit, but very briefly, as between the two sermons. Their proof is that it is established that connecting is disliked and separation necessary, and silence does not effect separation because silence also occurs between the words of adhan. Therefore, one should sit, even if briefly, like the sitting between the two sermons of Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa's proof is that delay in Maghrib is disliked, which is why we said earlier that one should not pray nafl after sunset before the fard. So he suffices with the minimum separation, i.e., silence, to avoid delay while still achieving separation. And the response to the Sahibayn's analogy is that the separation between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib cannot be compared to the separation between the two sermons because there is a world of difference: the place of adhan and iqamah differs, the voice differs (adhan is with slow recitation and iqamah is with haste), and the posture of the mu'adhdhin differs (he puts fingers in ears during adhan but leaves hands during iqamah). In contrast, for the two sermons, the place, voice, and posture of the khatib are the same. So analogy is not valid. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He separates between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib by two rak'ahs, analogizing Maghrib to other prayers.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and also includes an inter-madhhab comparison regarding the ruling on sitting (jalsah) between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib prayer. The base text from Hidayah states the ruling: one sits between adhan and iqamah except for Maghrib, according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that even for Maghrib, a light sitting is required. The commentator explains the reasoning of each side. The Sahibayn argue that separation (fasl) is necessary because connecting (wasl) the adhan directly to iqamah without any interval is disliked (makruh). Silence (saktah) does not count as separation because silence also occurs between the words of the adhan itself, so a distinct action like sitting is needed. They analogize this to the sitting between the two sermons of Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa's argument is that delay in Maghrib is disliked, as Maghrib's time is short. Therefore, one should suffice with the minimum separation, which is a brief silence while standing. He distinguishes this case from the sermons, noting that the place and tone of adhan and iqamah differ, so silence can constitute separation here, whereas the sermons are identical. The passage then mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf that he saw Abu Hanifa practice not sitting for Maghrib. Additionally, it includes the recommendation for the mu'adhdhin to be knowledgeable, citing the hadith 'Let the best of you give the adhan.' The commentary further elaborates on the general ruling that between adhan and iqamah, one should separate either by a prayer (if there is a sunnah/nafl) or by a light sitting. For Maghrib, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one is to stand in silence long enough to recite three short verses or one long verse, the other is to take three steps. The Sahibayn insist on a sitting, even if brief. Finally, Imam al-Shafi'i's view is mentioned: he says separate by two rak'ahs, analogizing Maghrib to other prayers, but the text dismisses this by stating the difference has been explained.

Key Terms
الجلسة بين الأذان والإقامة (al-jalsah bayn al-adhan wa al-iqamah): The sitting between the call to prayer and the commencement of prayer.
الوصل (al-wasl): Connecting the adhan directly to the iqamah without any interval.
الفصل (al-fasl): Separation between adhan and iqamah, either by sitting or by prayer or by silence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib?
A) One must sit for a long time.
B) One does not sit, but separates by silence while standing.
C) One sits briefly, just like for other prayers.
D) One prays two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
For Maghrib prayer, the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) holds that the mu'adhdhin should not sit between adhan and iqamah but should stand silently for a brief interval.

The General Ruling on the Interval Between Adhan and Iqamah
Explaining the general rule on interval between adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that separating between adhan and iqamah is necessary (wajib), identify the evidence from hadith, and apply it to prayers that have preceding sunnah prayers.

Core Idea
Separation between adhan and iqamah is wajib; connecting is makruh.

This lesson explains the fundamental principle that between the adhan and iqamah there must be an interval. The Hanafi school considers this separation necessary to achieve the purpose of the adhan and to follow the Prophet's instruction. We will examine the evidence and how it applies to different prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act in question: the interval (fasl) between adhan and iqamah. State the ruling: connecting (wasl) is makruh (disliked) and separation is necessary (wajib).
The ruling is based on the purpose of the adhan and the hadith.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Identify the hadith: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' and the instruction to separate with a brief sitting if one does not pray. This is the main dalil for the ruling.
The hadith is narrated and considered reliable in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply to prayers with supererogatory prayers
For prayers that have a sunnah or mustahabb prayer before the fard (e.g., Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Isha), that prayer serves as the interval.
If there is no supererogatory prayer, a brief sitting or pause is sufficient.
4
Understand the wisdom
The adhan informs people of the time; they need time to prepare and come to the mosque. Connecting would defeat this purpose.
This is a rationale reinforced by later scholars.

پڑھ سکے۔ دوم یہ کہ اس قدر فصل کرے کہ تین قدم چلنا ممکن ہو ۔ صاحبین نے کہا کہ مغرب میں بھی جلسہ کرے مگر بہت مختصر جیسے دو خطبوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بات تو طے شدہ ہے کہ اذان جواب یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان فصل کو دو خطبوں کے درمیان فصل پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں زمین و آسمان کا فرق ہے بایں طور کہ اذان واقامت کی جگہ مختلف ہوتی ہے اور دونوں میں آواز مختلف ہوتی ہے اس طور پر کہ اذان میں ترسل ہوتا ہے اور اقامت میں حدر ہوتا ہے نیز دونوں میں مؤذن کی ہیئت مختلف ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اذان کے وقت وہ اپنی دونوں انگلیاں دونوں کانوں میں داخل کرتا ہے نمازوں کے درمیان فرق ذکر کیا جا چکا۔ یعنی امام شافعی کا مغرب کو باقی دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مغرب میں تاخیر مکروہ ہے اور دوسری نمازوں میں تاخیر مکروہ نہیں ہے پس مغرب کا دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کیسے صحیح ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ جیسے فاضل پر تعجب ہے کہ باب المواقیت میں، مغرب کے وقت میں امام شافعی کا مذہب نقل کرتے ہوئے لکھا کہ مغرب کا صرف اتناوقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے بعد صرف تین رکعتیں پڑھ سکے اور یہاں لکھا کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو رکعت کے ساتھ فصل کرے پس یہ دونوں مذہب کیسے جمع ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لیکن اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کے مغرب کے وقت میں دو قول ہیں جیسا کہ خادم نے امام غزالی کے حوالہ سے باب المواقیت میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ پس مصنف نے باب المواقیت میں امام شافعی کا ایک قول ذکر کیا ہے اور یہاں دوسرے قول کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مغرب کا اتنا وقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے علاوہ پانچ رکعتیں پڑھ سکے یعنی تین رکعت فرض اور دو رکعت کے ساتھ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان فصل کرے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میں نے ابو حنیفہ کو دیکھا کہ وہ مغرب میں اذان دیتے اور اقامت کرتے اور اذان واقامت کے درمیان نہیں بیٹھتے تھے۔ امام ابو یوسف کا یہ قول دو باتوں کو مفید ہے ایک تو وہی جو ہم ذکر کر چکے یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان جلسہ نہ کرے۔ دوم یہ کہ اذان دینے والا احکام شرع کا عالم ہو۔ رہا یہ کہ یہ کس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا تو جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور نے فرمايا: وَيُؤَدِّنُ لَكُمْ خِيَارُكُمْ وَ ليَؤمَّكُمُ اقْرَاكُم یعنی تمہارے واسطے وہ اذان کہے جو تم میں سے بہتر ہو اور تمہارے واسطے و وامام ہو جو اقر آہوں یعنی کتاب الہی خوب پڑھا ہوا ہو ۔
Second evidence is that the purpose of the adhan is to inform people of the entry of time so that they may prepare and come to the mosque to perform the prayer. And because this purpose is lost by connecting [the adhan and iqamah without interval], therefore connecting between adhan and iqamah is makruh and separating is necessary. So if the prayer has a supererogatory prayer before it that is sunnah or mustahabb, then one should separate between adhan and iqamah with that prayer, e.g., two rak'ahs before Fajr, four before Zuhr are sunnah, and four before Asr and four before Isha are mustahabb. The evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' meaning between adhan and iqamah. He said it three times, and the third time he said: 'For whoever wishes; if he does not pray, then let him separate between them with a brief sitting.' The conclusion is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for all prayers except Maghrib, one should sit between adhan and iqamah, and it is better for the mu'adhdhin to pray sunnah or nafl in that interval. Regarding Maghrib, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: first, that it is mustahabb to stand silently for the duration of reciting three short verses or one long verse; second, that he should separate by the time it takes to take three steps. The Sahibayn said that for Maghrib too, one should sit briefly like the interval between two khutbahs. Their evidence is that it is established that connecting is makruh and separation is necessary, and it is nearly agreed that separation does not occur with silence because silence occurs between the words of the adhan itself, so one should sit to separate, even if briefly, like the separation between two khutbahs on Friday. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that delay in Maghrib is makruh, which is why we previously said that one should not pray nafl after sunset before the fard. So he should suffice with a minimal separation, i.e., silence, to avoid delay and still achieve separation. The response to the Sahibayn's analogy is that comparing the separation between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib to the separation between two khutbahs is incorrect because there is a vast difference between them: the locations of adhan and iqamah differ, the voices differ (adhan with slow recitation, iqamah with speed), and the posture of the mu'adhdhin differs (he puts his fingers in his ears during adhan but leaves his hands loose during iqamah). In contrast, the two khutbahs share the same location, same tone and voice, and the same posture of the khatib. So how can one be analogized to the other given these differences? Imam al-Shafi'i said that for Maghrib, one should separate with two rak'ahs, and his evidence is to analogize Maghrib to the other prayers. The author of Hidayah said that the difference between Maghrib and other prayers has been mentioned. That is, Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy of Maghrib to other prayers is qiyas ma'a al-fariq because delay in Maghrib is makruh while in other prayers it is not, so how can the analogy be valid? One may wonder at a scholar like the author of Hidayah: in Bab al-Mawaqit, he narrated Imam al-Shafi'i's opinion that Maghrib's time is only enough for wudu, adhan, iqamah, and three rak'ahs, but here he says to separate with two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah. How can these two views be reconciled? The answer is that Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions regarding the time of Maghrib, as mentioned by al-Khadim quoting Imam al-Ghazali in Bab al-Mawaqit. So the author mentioned one opinion there and adopted the other opinion here. The second opinion is that Maghrib's time is enough for wudu, adhan, and iqamah, plus five rak'ahs (three fard and two nafl for the interval). Imam Abu Yusuf said: I saw Abu Hanifa giving adhan for Maghrib and then iqamah, and he did not sit between them. This statement of Abu Yusuf indicates two things: first, that according to Abu Hanifa, one should not sit between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib; second, that the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable of Islamic rulings. As for how this is known, the answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let the best among you give adhan for you, and let the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead you in prayer.'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on the interval (fasl) between the adhan and iqamah (the call to prayer and the second call for commencement), specifically for Maghrib prayer. It is an expansion probe (sharh) that explains and debates the issue. The passage begins by stating the general principle: connecting adhan and iqamah without any interval is makruh (disliked), and separation is necessary. For prayers that have a sunnah or mustahabb prayer before the fard, that prayer serves as the separation. This is based on the hadith 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' and the instruction to separate with a brief sitting if one does not pray. For Maghrib, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the interval should be minimal—either by standing silently or taking three steps—because delaying Maghrib is makruh. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, saying that even for Maghrib there should be a short sitting like between the two khutbahs of Jumu'ah. They argue that silence is not a valid separation since it occurs within the adhan itself. Abu Hanifa responds by emphasizing the dislike of delay in Maghrib, so a silent pause suffices. The author then refutes the Sahibayn's analogy to the khutbahs by listing differences: adhan and iqamah occur at different times and with different styles and postures, unlike the two khutbahs which are identical in these aspects. Next, the passage addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's view that for Maghrib one should pray two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah, analogizing Maghrib to other prayers. The author of al-Hidayah rejects this as qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a point of difference) because delay in Maghrib is disliked. Finally, it resolves an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah itself regarding Imam al-Shafi'i's two opinions on the length of Maghrib time, explaining that al-Shafi'i has two valid positions. The passage ends with Imam Abu Yusuf's observation that he saw Abu Hanifa not sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib, and that this also implies the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable. The evidence for the latter is a hadith about choosing the best for adhan and imamah.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): The separation or interval between the adhan and iqamah, which can be a prayer, a sitting, or a pause.
وصل (wasl): Connecting the adhan and iqamah without any interval, which is considered makruh (disliked).
جلسة خفيفة (jalsah khafifah): A brief sitting between adhan and iqamah, as recommended by the Sahibayn for Maghrib, analogous to the sitting between the two khutbahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on connecting the adhan and iqamah without any interval in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is wajib to connect them
B) It is makruh
C) It is sunnah
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Separation between adhan and iqamah is necessary to avoid the disliked act of connecting them.

The Maghrib Exception: Intra-Hanafi and Inter-Madhhab Disputes on the Interval
Explaining the specific rulings and disputes for Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three positions on the Maghrib interval (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, al-Shafi'i), explain the evidence for each, and apply the Hanafi response that qiyas ma'a al-fariq invalidates the Shafi'i analogy.

Core Idea
For Maghrib, the interval is minimal because delay is makruh; analogies to other prayers or khutbahs fail.

Maghrib prayer is unique because delaying it is disliked. This creates a tension with the general principle of separation between adhan and iqamah. In this lesson, we explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, as well as the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. We will see how the authors rebut analogies using qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific issue
The issue is the interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib prayer. Unlike other prayers, Maghrib has a dislike of delay.
This distinction is the basis of all differences.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the interval should be minimal: either standing silently for the duration of three short verses or one long verse, or taking three steps. No sitting or prayer.
His evidence: delay in Maghrib is makruh, so a long interval is disliked.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that even for Maghrib, there should be a brief sitting between adhan and iqamah, like the sitting between two khutbahs.
They argue that silence is not a valid separation because it occurs within the adhan itself.
4
State Imam al-Shafi'i's position
Al-Shafi'i holds that for Maghrib, one should separate by praying two rak'ahs, analogizing to other prayers.
His evidence: the general command 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' applies to all prayers.
5
Analyze the Hanafi responses
The author of Hidayah responds to the Sahibayn by listing many differences between adhan/iqamah and khutbahs (location, voice, posture), making the analogy invalid. To al-Shafi'i, the response is qiyas ma'a al-fariq: Maghrib is different because delay is makruh.
Thus the Hanafi school maintains the minimal interval for Maghrib.

Source Text
