دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اذ ان لوگوں کو دخول وقت کی خبر دیتا ہے تا کہ وہ نماز کی تیاری کر کے ادائے نماز کے لئے مسجد میں حاضر ہو جائیں اور چونکہ وصل سے یہ مقصود فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان وصل مکروہ اور فصل ضروری ہے۔ پس اگر نماز ایسی ہے جس سے پہلے تطوعا کوئی نماز مسنون یا مستحب ہو تو اذان واقامت کے درمیان نماز کے ساتھ فصل کرے مثلا فجر کی نماز سے پہلے دو رکعت اور ظہر سے پہلے چار رکعت مسنون ہیں اور عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور عشاء سے پہلے چار رکعت استحباب کے درجہ میں ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بین کل اذانین صلاة یعنی ہر دو اذان واقامت کے درمیان نماز ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ بات تین بار کہی اور تیسری بار فرمایا لِمَنْ شَاءَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يُصَلّ يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمَا تیسری بار فر مایا کہ یہ حکم اس شخص کے فرمایا لئے ہے جو چاہے اگر اس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تو ان دونوں کے درمیان جلسہ خفیفہ کے ساتھ فصل کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک سوائے مغرب کے تمام نمازوں میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان جلسہ کرے اور مؤذن کو اسی درمیان میں سنت یا نفل پڑھنا اولیٰ ہے۔ اور مغرب میں امام ابوحنیفہ سے دور واسیتیں ہیں : ایک یہ کہ مغرب کی اذان واقامت کے درمیان سکوت کے ساتھ کھڑے کھڑے اتنی مقدار فصل کرنا مستحب ہے کہ جس میں چھوٹی تین آیات یا بڑی ایک آیت پڑھ سکے۔ دوم یہ کہ اس قدر فصل کرے کہ تین قدم چلنا ممکن ہو ۔ صاحبین نے کہا کہ مغرب میں بھی جلسہ کرے مگر بہت مختصر جیسے دو خطبوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بات تو طے شدہ ہے کہ اذان واقامت کے درمیان وصل مکروہ اور فصل ضروری ہے جیسا کہ یہ بات تو ہےکہ کے اور تمہید میں مذکور ہوا۔ اور یہ بات بھی تقریبا مسلم ہے کہ سکوت کے ساتھ فصل واقع نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ سکوت تو اذان کے کلمات کے درمیان میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے اس لئے بیٹھ کر فصل کرے اگر چہ مختصر ہی کیوں نہ ہو جیسے جمعہ کے دن دو خطبوں میں بیٹھ کر فصل کیا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں تاخیر کرنا مکروہ ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ سابق میں ہم نے کہا تھا کہ غروب کے بعد اور فرض سے پہلے نفل نہ پڑھے۔ پس اونی فصل یعنی سکتہ پر اکتفاء کرے تا کہ تاخیر سے بھی احتراز ہو جائے اور اذان واقامت میں فصل بھی واقع ہو جائے۔ اور صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان فصل کو دو خطبوں کے درمیان فصل پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں زمین و آسمان کا فرق ہے بایں طور کہ اذان واقامت کی جگہ مختلف ہوتی ہے اور دونوں میں آواز مختلف ہوتی ہے اس طور پر کہ اذان میں ترسل ہوتا ہے اور اقامت میں حدر ہوتا ہے نیز دونوں میں مؤذن کی ہیئت مختلف ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اذان کے وقت وہ اپنی دونوں انگلیاں دونوں کانوں میں داخل کرتا ہے اور اقامت میں ہاتھ چھوڑے رکھتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف خطبہ ہے کہ دونوں خطبوں کی جگہ ایک، دونوں خطبوں میں نغمہ اور و آواز متحد اور دو نوں خطبوں میں خطیب کی ہیئت متحد ہے پس اس فرق کی موجودگی میں ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا کیسے درست ہوگا۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ مغرب کی اذان اور اقامت میں دور کھتوں سے فصل کرے اور دلیل میں فرمایا کہ مغرب کو باقی نمازوں پر قیاس کیا جائے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مغرب اور دوسری نمازوں کے درمیان فرق ذکر کیا جا چکا۔ یعنی امام شافعی کا مغرب کو باقی دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مغرب میں تاخیر مکروہ ہے اور دوسری نمازوں میں تاخیر مکروہ نہیں ہے پس مغرب کا دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کیسے صحیح ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ جیسے فاضل پر تعجب ہے کہ باب المواقیت میں، مغرب کے وقت میں امام شافعی کا مذہب نقل کرتے ہوئے لکھا کہ مغرب کا صرف اتناوقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے بعد صرف تین رکعتیں پڑھ سکے اور یہاں لکھا کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو رکعت کے ساتھ فصل کرے پس یہ دونوں مذہب کیسے جمع ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لیکن اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کے مغرب کے وقت میں دو قول ہیں جیسا کہ خادم نے امام غزالی کے حوالہ سے باب المواقیت میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ پس مصنف نے باب المواقیت میں امام شافعی کا ایک قول ذکر کیا ہے اور یہاں دوسرے قول کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مغرب کا اتنا وقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے علاوہ پانچ رکعتیں پڑھ سکے یعنی تین رکعت فرض اور دو رکعت کے ساتھ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان فصل کرے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میں نے ابو حنیفہ کو دیکھا کہ وہ مغرب میں اذان دیتے اور اقامت کرتے اور اذان واقامت کے درمیان نہیں بیٹھتے تھے۔ امام ابو یوسف کا یہ قول دو باتوں کو مفید ہے ایک تو وہی جو ہم ذکر کر چکے یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان جلسہ نہ کرے۔ دوم یہ کہ اذان دینے والا احکام شرع کا عالم ہو۔ رہا یہ کہ یہ کس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا تو جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور نے فرمايا: وَيُؤَدِّنُ لَكُمْ خِيَارُكُمْ وَ ليَؤمَّكُمُ اقْرَاكُم یعنی تمہارے واسطے وہ اذان کہے جو تم میں سے بہتر ہو اور تمہارے واسطے و وامام ہو جو اقر آہوں یعنی کتاب الہی خوب پڑھا ہوا ہو ۔
Second evidence is that the purpose of the adhan is to inform people of the entry of time so that they may prepare and come to the mosque to perform the prayer. And because this purpose is lost by connecting [the adhan and iqamah without interval], therefore connecting between adhan and iqamah is makruh and separating is necessary. So if the prayer has a supererogatory prayer before it that is sunnah or mustahabb, then one should separate between adhan and iqamah with that prayer, e.g., two rak'ahs before Fajr, four before Zuhr are sunnah, and four before Asr and four before Isha are mustahabb. The evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' meaning between adhan and iqamah. He said it three times, and the third time he said: 'For whoever wishes; if he does not pray, then let him separate between them with a brief sitting.' The conclusion is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for all prayers except Maghrib, one should sit between adhan and iqamah, and it is better for the mu'adhdhin to pray sunnah or nafl in that interval. Regarding Maghrib, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: first, that it is mustahabb to stand silently for the duration of reciting three short verses or one long verse; second, that he should separate by the time it takes to take three steps. The Sahibayn said that for Maghrib too, one should sit briefly like the interval between two khutbahs. Their evidence is that it is established that connecting is makruh and separation is necessary, and it is nearly agreed that separation does not occur with silence because silence occurs between the words of the adhan itself, so one should sit to separate, even if briefly, like the separation between two khutbahs on Friday. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that delay in Maghrib is makruh, which is why we previously said that one should not pray nafl after sunset before the fard. So he should suffice with a minimal separation, i.e., silence, to avoid delay and still achieve separation. The response to the Sahibayn's analogy is that comparing the separation between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib to the separation between two khutbahs is incorrect because there is a vast difference between them: the locations of adhan and iqamah differ, the voices differ (adhan with slow recitation, iqamah with speed), and the posture of the mu'adhdhin differs (he puts his fingers in his ears during adhan but leaves his hands loose during iqamah). In contrast, the two khutbahs share the same location, same tone and voice, and the same posture of the khatib. So how can one be analogized to the other given these differences? Imam al-Shafi'i said that for Maghrib, one should separate with two rak'ahs, and his evidence is to analogize Maghrib to the other prayers. The author of Hidayah said that the difference between Maghrib and other prayers has been mentioned. That is, Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy of Maghrib to other prayers is qiyas ma'a al-fariq because delay in Maghrib is makruh while in other prayers it is not, so how can the analogy be valid? One may wonder at a scholar like the author of Hidayah: in Bab al-Mawaqit, he narrated Imam al-Shafi'i's opinion that Maghrib's time is only enough for wudu, adhan, iqamah, and three rak'ahs, but here he says to separate with two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah. How can these two views be reconciled? The answer is that Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions regarding the time of Maghrib, as mentioned by al-Khadim quoting Imam al-Ghazali in Bab al-Mawaqit. So the author mentioned one opinion there and adopted the other opinion here. The second opinion is that Maghrib's time is enough for wudu, adhan, and iqamah, plus five rak'ahs (three fard and two nafl for the interval). Imam Abu Yusuf said: I saw Abu Hanifa giving adhan for Maghrib and then iqamah, and he did not sit between them. This statement of Abu Yusuf indicates two things: first, that according to Abu Hanifa, one should not sit between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib; second, that the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable of Islamic rulings. As for how this is known, the answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let the best among you give adhan for you, and let the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead you in prayer.'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on the interval (fasl) between the adhan and iqamah (the call to prayer and the second call for commencement), specifically for Maghrib prayer. It is an expansion probe (sharh) that explains and debates the issue. The passage begins by stating the general principle: connecting adhan and iqamah without any interval is makruh (disliked), and separation is necessary. For prayers that have a sunnah or mustahabb prayer before the fard, that prayer serves as the separation. This is based on the hadith 'Between every two adhans is a prayer' and the instruction to separate with a brief sitting if one does not pray. For Maghrib, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the interval should be minimal—either by standing silently or taking three steps—because delaying Maghrib is makruh. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, saying that even for Maghrib there should be a short sitting like between the two khutbahs of Jumu'ah. They argue that silence is not a valid separation since it occurs within the adhan itself. Abu Hanifa responds by emphasizing the dislike of delay in Maghrib, so a silent pause suffices. The author then refutes the Sahibayn's analogy to the khutbahs by listing differences: adhan and iqamah occur at different times and with different styles and postures, unlike the two khutbahs which are identical in these aspects. Next, the passage addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's view that for Maghrib one should pray two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah, analogizing Maghrib to other prayers. The author of al-Hidayah rejects this as qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a point of difference) because delay in Maghrib is disliked. Finally, it resolves an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah itself regarding Imam al-Shafi'i's two opinions on the length of Maghrib time, explaining that al-Shafi'i has two valid positions. The passage ends with Imam Abu Yusuf's observation that he saw Abu Hanifa not sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib, and that this also implies the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable. The evidence for the latter is a hadith about choosing the best for adhan and imamah.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): The separation or interval between the adhan and iqamah, which can be a prayer, a sitting, or a pause.
جلسة خفيفة (jalsah khafifah): A brief sitting between adhan and iqamah, as recommended by the Sahibayn for Maghrib, analogous to the sitting between the two khutbahs.
قياس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a material difference (fariq) between the original and the new case, making the analogy inapplicable.
وصل (wasl): Connecting the adhan and iqamah without any interval, which is considered makruh (disliked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the recommended interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib?
A) A brief sitting like between two khutbahs
B) Two rak'ahs of prayer
C) Standing silently for the duration of three short verses or taking three steps
D) No interval at all

Key Takeaway
For Maghrib, the interval is minimal due to the dislike of delay; analogies to other prayers or khutbahs are rejected.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Adhan for Missed Prayers (Qada) – The Proof from Laylat al-Ta'ris
Establishing the ruling by prophetic action and refuting the Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for qada prayers and support it with the dalil from the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris.

Core Idea
The Prophet's action at Laylat al-Ta'ris proves adhan is due for missed prayers.

When you miss a prayer, you must make it up. But do you need to call the adhan before doing so? The Hanafi school says yes, based on the Prophet's own practice on the morning after Laylat al-Ta'ris. This lesson unpacks that proof and how it settles a key inter-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the act of giving adhan for a missed (qada) prayer. The Hanafi school holds that it is a sunnah muakkadah to give both adhan and iqamah.
Note that this ruling applies whether one prays alone or in congregation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris: the Prophet ﷺ and his companions overslept and missed Fajr, and upon waking he ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah before making up the prayer.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawood and others.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How does this action prove the ruling? The Prophet’s command to Bilal (أمر بلالاً بالأذان) indicates at least recommendation. In Hanafi usul, a command from the Prophet for a non-obligatory act gives it the status of sunnah muakkadah.
If it were obligatory, the command would be stronger; but here it is at least a confirmed sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only iqamah is needed for qada prayers; adhan is not required. His reasoning is that adhan is meant to announce the time of prayer, which is irrelevant for makeup prayers.
The Hanafi school responds by citing the explicit action of the Prophet.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is preferred because it is based on direct prophetic practice. The hadith provides a clear precedent, and the Shafi'i position lacks a comparable explicit dalil.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوت شدہ نمازوں کے لئے اذان کا حکم وَيُوَدِّنَ لِلْقَانِيَةِ وَيُقِيمُ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ قَضَى الفَجْرَ غَدَاةَ لَيْلَةِ التَّعْرِيسِ بِادَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِي في اكتفائه بالإقامة ترجمہ اور فائنہ نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت بھی کہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لیلتہ العربی کے دن دن نکلنے پر فجر کی نماز کو اذان و اقامت کے ساتھ قضاء کیا اور یہ حدیث امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے ان کے اقامت پر اکتفاء کرنے میں۔ تشریح سئلہ، فوت شدہ (قضاء ) نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے خواہ اکیلا ہو یا جماعت ہو۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ اقامت پر اکتفاء کرنا کافی ہے اذان کی ضرورت نہیں۔ ہماری دلیل لیلتہ العریس کا واقعہ ہے۔ تعریس کہتے ہیں آخری رات میں کسی مقام پر اتر کر آرام کرنا۔ یہ واقعہ حدیث کی کتابوں میں مختلف الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے ۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے ابوداؤد کے حوالہ سے یہ الفاظ نقل کئے ہیں اُنهُ أَمَرَ بِلَالاً بِالاَ ذَانِ
Ruling on adhan for missed prayers: He should give adhan and iqamah for the missed prayer because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'ris with adhan and iqamah. And this hadith is evidence against al-Shafi'i in his sufficing with iqamah alone. Explanation: For a missed (qada) prayer, he should give adhan and iqamah, whether alone or in congregation. Imam al-Shafi'i said that sufficing with iqamah is enough; adhan is not needed. Our evidence is the incident of Laylat al-Ta'ris. Ta'ris means alighting at a place for rest in the last part of the night. This incident is narrated in hadith books with various wording. Allama Ibn al-Humam narrated from Abu Dawood the words: 'that he ordered Bilal to give the adhan...'
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling of giving adhan for missed prayers (qada). The author states that for a missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah should be pronounced, whether one prays alone or in congregation. This is based on the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) after sleeping through the night and missing Fajr, made it up with adhan and iqamah. This hadith is used as a proof against Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that only iqamah is sufficient for a missed prayer; adhan is not required. The term 'Ta'ris' refers to stopping for rest during the last part of a journey. The author references Allama Ibn al-Humam who transmitted the hadith from Abu Dawood that the Prophet ordered Bilal to give the adhan. The text is cut off before completing the hadith, but the ruling is clear: adhan is mandatory for qada prayers according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has passed.
تعریس (ta'ris): Alighting for rest during the last part of the night, often on a journey.
لیلۃ العریس (laylat al-ta'ris): The night when the Prophet and his companions stopped to rest and subsequently missed Fajr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving adhan for a missed prayer?
A) Adhan is not required; iqamah alone is sufficient.
B) Both adhan and iqamah should be given, whether alone or in congregation.
C) Adhan is only required if praying in congregation.
D) Adhan is allowed but not recommended.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates adhan and iqamah for every missed obligatory prayer, following the explicit practice of the Prophet ﷺ at Laylat al-Ta'ris.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

No Interval Between Adhan and Iqamah for Maghrib: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Refuting Shafi'i analogy by distinguishing Maghrib's unique time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits an interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of qiyas ma' al-fariq.

Core Idea
Maghrib's short time makes delay makruh, so no sunnah between adhan and iqamah.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author refutes the Shafi'i practice of praying two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib. The Hanafi school argues that Maghrib's time is uniquely short, making any delay disliked (makruh). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the critique of the Shafi'i analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is whether there should be an interval (e.g., two rak'ahs of sunnah) between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib prayer.
This interval is recommended for other prayers but contested for Maghrib.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi school holds that no interval should occur because delay is makruh due to Maghrib's very short time. Evidence includes the practice of Abu Hanifa witnessed by Abu Yusuf and a hadith implying the mu'adhdhin should be knowledgeable.
The hadith: 'Let the best among you give adhan...' suggests the mu'adhdhin knows the rulings.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes Maghrib to other prayers, allowing two rak'ahs between adhan and iqamah. He has two sayings on Maghrib's time: one that it suffices for only three rak'ahs, another that it suffices for five.
The second saying supports his allowance of the interval.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rejects the analogy as qiyas ma' al-fariq (invalid analogy) because Maghrib's time is short—delay is makruh, unlike other prayers where it is not.
The term 'qiyas ma' al-fariq' is a key usul concept: the difference between the cases invalidates the analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الصلوة
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مغرب اور دوسری نمازوں کے درمیان فرق ذکر کیا جا چکا۔ یعنی امام شافعی کا مغرب کو باقی دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مغرب میں تاخیر مکروہ ہے اور دوسری نمازوں میں تاخیر مکروہ نہیں ہے پس مغرب کا دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کیسے صحیح ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ جیسے فاضل پر تعجب ہے کہ باب المواقیت میں، مغرب کے وقت میں امام شافعی کا مذہب نقل کرتے ہوئے لکھا کہ مغرب کا صرف اتنا وقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے بعد صرف تین رکعتیں پڑھ سکے اور یہاں لکھا کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان دو رکعت کے ساتھ فصل کرے پس یہ دونوں مذہب کیسے جمع ہو سکتے ہیں۔
لیکن اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کے مغرب کے وقت میں دو قول ہیں جیسا کہ خادم نے امام غزالی کے حوالہ سے باب المواقیت میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ پس مصنف نے باب المواقیت میں امام شافعی کا ایک قول ذکر کیا ہے اور یہاں دوسرے قول کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مغرب کا اتنا وقت ہے جس میں وضو، اذان اور اقامت کے علاوہ پانچ رکعتیں پڑھ سکے یعنی تین رکعت فرض اور دو رکعت کے ساتھ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان فصل کرے۔
امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ میں نے ابو حنیفہ کو دیکھا کہ وہ مغرب میں اذان دیتے اور اقامت کرتے اور اذان واقامت کے درمیان نہیں بیٹھتے تھے۔ امام ابو یوسف کا یہ قول دو باتوں کو مفید ہے ایک تو وہی جو ہم ذکر کر چکے یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مغرب میں اذان واقامت کے درمیان جلسہ نہ کرے۔ دوم یہ کہ اذان دینے والا احکام شرع کا عالم ہو۔ رہا یہ کہ یہ کس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا تو جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور نے فرمایا: وَيُؤَدِّنُ لَكُمْ خِيَارُكُمْ وَ ليَؤمَّكُمُ اقْرَاكُم یعنی تمہارے واسطے وہ اذان کہے جو تم میں سے بہتر ہو اور تمہارے واسطے وہ امام ہو جو کتاب الہی خوب پڑھا ہوا ہو۔
The Book of Prayer. The author of al-Hidayah said that the difference between Maghrib and other prayers has been mentioned. That is, Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy of Maghrib to other prayers is an analogy with a difference. Because delay in Maghrib is disliked (makruh) and delay in other prayers is not disliked. So how can the analogy of Maghrib to other prayers be correct? It is surprising that a scholar like the author of al-Hidayah, in the chapter on times (Bab al-Mawaqit), when narrating Imam al-Shafi'i's madhhab regarding the time of Maghrib, wrote that Maghrib has only enough time in which, after ablution, adhan, and iqamah, only three rak'ahs can be prayed. And here he wrote that one should separate between adhan and iqamah with two rak'ahs. How can these two madhhabs be reconciled? But the answer is that Imam al-Shafi'i has two sayings regarding the time of Maghrib, as al-Khadim mentioned from Imam al-Ghazali in Bab al-Mawaqit. So the author mentioned one saying in Bab al-Mawaqit and relied on the other saying here. The second saying is that Maghrib has enough time in which, besides ablution, adhan, and iqamah, five rak'ahs can be prayed: three fard and two rak'ahs to separate between adhan and iqamah. Imam Abu Yusuf said: I saw Abu Hanifa that he would give adhan for Maghrib and say iqamah, and he would not sit between adhan and iqamah. This statement of Imam Abu Yusuf benefits two things: first, that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, one should not sit between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib; second, that the one giving adhan should be knowledgeable of the rulings of Shari'ah. As for how this is known from evidence, the answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Let the best among you give adhan for you, and let those who are most recitative of the Book of Allah lead you in prayer."
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib prayer. The Hanafi position is that there is no interval (jalsah) between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib because its time is very short, and any delay is disliked (makruh). Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes Maghrib to other prayers, allowing an interval. The text clarifies that the author of al-Hidayah was criticized for inconsistency in narrating Shafi'i's position, but it resolves by noting that Shafi'i has two sayings: one that Maghrib time is only sufficient for three rak'ahs, and another that it is sufficient for five rak'ahs, allowing two rak'ahs of sunnah between adhan and iqamah. The Hanafi position is supported by the practice of Imam Abu Hanifa as witnessed by Imam Abu Yusuf, and by the hadith that the adhan should be given by the best among the people, implying knowledge of the rulings.

Key Terms
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma' al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a material difference (fariq) between the original case and the new case that prevents transferring the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is there no interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib?
A) Because it is makruh to delay Maghrib due to its short time
B) Because Maghrib has no sunnah prayers
C) Because the Prophet never prayed sunnah before Maghrib
D) Because adhan and iqamah must be consecutive for all prayers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school forbids an interval between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib because its short time makes delay disliked, distinguishing it from other prayers.

Adhan for Missed (Qada) Prayers
Proving adhan for qada prayers with dalil and rebutting Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for qada prayers, explain the proof from Laylat al-Ta'ris, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
For qada prayers, adhan is wajib — the Prophet's practice proves it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that adhan is required for make-up prayers, based on authentic hadiths. We'll also see why Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed and how the Hanafi school responds, including the case of multiple missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on adhan for qada
Identify the ruling for a single missed prayer: the Hanafi school holds that both adhan and iqamah are wajib. Note that this applies whether praying alone or in congregation.
2
Identify the primary dalil
Locate the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris (the night the Prophet and companions overslept Fajr). The Prophet commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah before making up the prayer. This is the core proof.
Also the Battle of the Trench hadith supports the same.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove wujub? The Prophet's command (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The adhan was given specifically for the qada prayer, establishing it as a required element.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (ahad), so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Present the Shafi'i counter-proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on a narration in Sahih Muslim from Abu Hurairah that only mentions iqamah, omitting adhan. He concludes that iqamah alone is sufficient.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response: other authentic narrations include adhan. Acting on the additional detail (ziyadat) is preferable. The hadith with adhan is more complete and corroborated by the Battle of the Trench incident. Therefore, the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
For multiple missed prayers: first gets both adhan and iqamah; the rest have choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوت شدہ نمازوں کے لئے اذان کا حکم
لِلْفَائِتَةِ وَيُقِيمُ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَضَى الْفَجْرَ غَدَاةَ لَيْلَةِ التَّعْرِيسِ بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي اكْتِفَائِهِ بِالْإِقَامَةِ
ترجمہ: فوت شدہ نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت بھی کہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لیلۃ التعریس کے دن صبح کو فجر کی نماز کو اذان و اقامت کے ساتھ قضاء کیا اور یہ حدیث امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے جو اقامت پر اکتفاء کرتے ہیں۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ فوت شدہ (قضاء) نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے خواہ اکیلا ہو یا جماعت ہو۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ اقامت پر اکتفاء کرنا کافی ہے، اذان کی ضرورت نہیں۔ ہماری دلیل لیلۃ التعریس کا واقعہ ہے۔ تعریس کہتے ہیں آخری رات میں کسی مقام پر اتر کر آرام کرنا۔ یہ واقعہ حدیث کی کتابوں میں مختلف الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے ابوداؤد کے حوالہ سے یہ الفاظ نقل کئے ہیں: أَنَّهُ أَمَرَ بِلَالًا بِالْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ حِينَ نَامُوا عَنِ الصُّبْحِ وَصَلُّوهَا بَعْدَ ارْتِفَاعِ الشَّمْسِ یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بلال کو اذان و اقامت کا حکم دیا جس وقت صحابہ صبح کی نماز سے سو گئے اور سورج نکلنے کے بعد اسے ادا کیا۔ شیخین نے اس واقعہ کو اس طرح نقل کیا ہے: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: سِرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ لَيْلَةً فَقَالَ بَعْضُ الْقَوْمِ لَوْ عَرَّسْتَ بِنَا يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ قَالَ أَخَافُ أَنْ تَنَامُوا عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ قَالَ بِلَالٌ أَنَا أُوقِظُكُمْ فَاضْطَجَعُوا وَاسْتَنَدَ بِلَالٌ ظَهْرَهُ إِلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ فَغَلَبَتْهُ عَيْنَاهُ فَنَامَ فَاسْتَيْقَظَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَدْ طَلَعَ حَاجِبُ الشَّمْسِ فَقَالَ يَا بِلَالُ أَيْنَ مَا قُلْتَ قَالَ مَا أُلْقِيَتْ عَلَيَّ نَوْمَةٌ مِثْلُهَا قَطُّ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَبَضَ أَرْوَاحَكُمْ حِينَ شَاءَ يَا بِلَالُ قُمْ فَأَذِّنْ بِالصَّلَاةِ فَتَوَضَّأَ فَلَمَّا ارْتَفَعَتِ الشَّمْسُ وَابْيَضَّتْ قَامَ فَصَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ جَمَاعَةً. دونوں روایتوں سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لیلۃ التعریس کی صبح کو دن نکلنے کے بعد اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ فجر کی نماز کی قضا فرمائی ہے۔ امام شافعی نے اس روایت سے استدلال کیا ہے جو مسلم میں حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے مروی ہے یعنی أَمَرَ بِلَالًا فَأَقَامَ الصَّلَاةَ فَصَلَّى بِهِمُ الصُّبْحَ یعنی آپ نے بلال کو حکم کیا پھر آپ نے صحابہ کو اقامت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائی۔ اس حدیث میں اذان کا ذکر نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قضا نماز کے لئے اقامت پر اکتفاء کرنا کافی ہے۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ دوسری صحیح روایتوں میں اذان کا ذکر موجود ہے لہذا زیادت پر عمل کرنا اولیٰ ہے۔ ہمارے مسلک کی تائید اس روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ غزوہ خندق کے موقع پر جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی چار نمازیں فوت ہو گئیں تو آپ نے اذان و اقامت کے ساتھ ان کی قضا فرمائی۔ پس اتنی احادیث صحیحہ کے ہوتے ہوئے امام شافعی کا اختلاف کرنا مناسب معلوم نہیں ہوتا۔
کثیر فوائت میں اول کے لئے اذان و اقامت ہے اور بقیہ کے لئے صرف اقامت پر اکتفاء کافی ہے فَإِنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَوَاتٌ أَذَّنَ لِلْأُولَى وَأَقَامَ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَكَانَ مُخَيَّرًا فِي الْبَاقِي إِنْ شَاءَ أَذَّنَ وَأَقَامَ لِيَكُونَ الْقَضَاءُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْأَدَاءِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى الْإِقَامَةِ لِأَنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلِاسْتِحْضَارِ وَهُمْ حُضُورٌ. قَالَ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ يُقَامُ لِمَا بَعْدَهُمَا قَالُوا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَذَا قَوْلُهُم.
ترجمہ: پھر اگر اس کی چند نمازیں فوت ہو گئیں تو پہلی نماز کے واسطے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی، اور اس کو باقی نمازوں کے حق میں اختیار ہے چاہے تو (ہر ایک کے لئے) اذان دے اور اقامت کہے تاکہ قضا ادا کے موافق ہو جائے اور چاہے تو اقامت پر اکتفاء کرے کیونکہ اذان تو حاضری طلب کرنے کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور یہاں سب حاضر ہیں۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ اول کے بعد والی نمازوں کے لئے صرف اقامت کہی جائے گی۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ سب کا قول ہو۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کی چند نمازیں فوت ہو گئی ہوں تو پہلی نماز کے لئے اذان بھی دے اور اقامت بھی کہے۔
The ruling on adhan for missed prayers: He should give adhan and iqamah for the missed prayer because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'ris with adhan and iqamah, and this is a proof against al-Shafi'i who considers iqamah sufficient. Translation: For a missed prayer, give adhan and also iqamah, because the Prophet made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'ris with adhan and iqamah, and this hadith is evidence against Imam al-Shafi'i who deems iqamah sufficient. Explanation: The issue is that for a missed (qada) prayer, one should give adhan and iqamah, whether alone or in congregation. Imam al-Shafi'i said that relying on iqamah is sufficient, adhan is not needed. Our evidence is the incident of Laylat al-Ta'ris. Ta'ris means to alight and rest at a place in the last part of the night. This incident is narrated in various wordings in hadith books. Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated from Abu Dawud these words: that he commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah when they overslept the morning prayer, and they prayed it after sunrise. The Two Shaykhs narrated it as follows: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah from his father: We traveled with the Messenger of Allah one night, and some people said, 'O Messenger of Allah, would you camp with us?' He said, 'I fear you might oversleep the prayer.' Bilal said, 'I will wake you.' They lay down, and Bilal leaned against his mount, and sleep overcame him. The Prophet woke up when the sun had risen a little, and said, 'O Bilal, where is what you said?' He said, 'Sleep never overcame me like this before.' The Prophet said, 'Indeed, Allah took your souls when He willed. O Bilal, get up and call the adhan for prayer.' He performed ablution, and when the sun had risen high and become white, he stood and led the people in congregation. From both narrations it is known that the Prophet made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'ris after sunrise with adhan and iqamah. Imam al-Shafi'i used the narration in Muslim from Abu Hurairah: 'He commanded Bilal, so he said the iqamah for prayer, and he led them in the morning prayer.' In this hadith, adhan is not mentioned, so it is proven that for qada prayer, relying on iqamah is sufficient. The answer to this is that other authentic narrations mention adhan, so acting on the additional information is preferable. Our school is also supported by the narration that during the Battle of the Trench, when the Prophet missed four prayers, he made them up with adhan and iqamah. With so many authentic hadiths, it is not appropriate for Imam al-Shafi'i to differ. When multiple prayers are missed: for the first, adhan and iqamah; for the rest, just iqamah is sufficient. If he missed several prayers, he should give adhan for the first and say iqamah due to the hadith we narrated, and he has the choice for the remaining: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah so that the qada is like the original performance, and if he wishes, he restricts to iqamah because adhan is for summoning, and they are present. The author said: From Muhammad, it is narrated that iqamah should be said for what follows the first two. They (the mashayikh) said: It is possible that this is their (all scholars') saying. Translation: Then if several prayers are missed, for the first prayer he gives adhan and says iqamah due to the hadith we narrated, and for the remaining he has the choice: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah so that the qada matches the ada, and if he wishes, he restricts to iqamah because adhan is for summoning, and they are present. The author said: From Muhammad, it is narrated that iqamah should be said for what follows the first two. The mashayikh said: It is possible that this is their (all scholars') saying. Explanation: The issue is that if a person has missed several prayers, for the first prayer he should give adhan and also iqamah.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that for a missed (qada) prayer, one must give both adhan and iqamah, whether praying alone or in congregation. It presents the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that only iqamah is sufficient. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris (the night the Prophet and companions overslept Fajr), where the Prophet commanded Bilal to give both adhan and iqamah before making up the prayer. The text responds to Shafi'i's counter-proof from a narration in Sahih Muslim that mentions only iqamah, arguing that other authentic narrations include adhan, and the version with additional detail is preferred. The Hanafi position is further supported by the hadith of the Battle of the Trench. The passage also covers the case of multiple missed prayers: the first prayer gets both adhan and iqamah, and for the remaining prayers, one has the choice to give both or just iqamah, since the people are already present. Imam Muhammad is reported to hold that just iqamah is said for the subsequent prayers, and the mashayikh consider this possibly the consensus.

Key Terms
لیلۃ التعریس (laylat al-ta'ris): The night when the Prophet and companions alighted for rest and overslept the Fajr prayer
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has expired
فوائت (fawā'it): Multiple missed (qada) prayers

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on adhan for a single missed prayer?
A) Both adhan and iqamah are required
B) Only iqamah is required
C) Neither adhan nor iqamah is required
D) Adhan is required only if praying in congregation

Key Takeaway
For qada prayers, the Hanafi school requires adhan and iqamah for the first missed prayer, with choice for subsequent ones.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Adhan and Iqamah for Qada: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with narrative proof and rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on adhan and iqamah for qada prayers, cite the primary proof, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of accepting a reliable addition (ziyadah).

Core Idea
For a missed prayer, the Prophet gave both adhan and iqamah – the addition is binding.

When you miss a prayer and need to make it up (qada), should you call the adhan again? The Hanafi school says yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only iqamah suffices. This lesson analyzes the key incident of Laylat al-Ta'ris (the night the Prophet and companions slept through Fajr) and the subsequent response to the Shafi'i proof. You will learn how the Hanafi school prioritizes a complete narration over an abridged one, and why this matters when performing qada today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What exactly is disputed: whether adhan is part of the qada prayer ritual. The Hanafi school says both adhan and iqamah, Shafi'i says only iqamah.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Read the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris from Ibn Abi Faddada. Note how the Prophet (SAW) commanded Bilal to give both adhan and iqamah. This is the primary dalil.
The two shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) transmitted it, so it is authentic.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on a different hadith (in Muslim from Abu Hurairah) that mentions only iqamah. He argues that silence on adhan means it is not required.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the presence of adhan in other authentic narrations is an addition (ziyadah) that must be accepted. Acting upon the more complete narration is preferable (al-akhdh bi al-ziyadah awla).
Also supported by the Battle of the Trench incident where four missed prayers were made up with both adhan and iqamah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi will say both adhan and iqamah when making up a missed prayer; a Shafi'i will only say iqamah. Both are valid within their schools, but the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْإِقَامَة حِيْنَ نَامُوا عَنِ الصُّبْحِ وَصَلُّوهَا بَعْدَ ارْتِفَاعِ الشَّمْسِ یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بلال کو اذان واقامت کا حکم دیا جس وقت که اصحاب رسول سے صبح کی نماز سے سو گئے اور سورج نکلنے کے بعد اس کو ادا کیا۔ شیخین نے اس واقعہ کو اس طرح نقل کیا ہے:
عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي فَتَادَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ سِرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ لَيْلَةً فَقَالَ بَعْضُ الْقَومِ لَوْ عَرَسْتَ بِنَا يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ قَالَ أَخَافُ أَنْ تَسَامُوا عَن الصَّلوة قَالَ بِلال اَنَا أَوْقِظُكُمْ فَاضْطَجَعُوا وَاسْتَدَ بِلَالٌ ظَهْرَهُ إِلَى رَاحِلَةِ فَعَلَمَتَهُ عَيْنَاهُ فَنَامَ فَاسْتَيْقَظَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَ قَدْ طَلَعَ حَاجِبُ الشَّمْسُ فَقَالَ يَا بِلَالُ اَيْنَ مَا قُلْتَ قَالَ مَا الْقِيتُ عَليَّ نَوْمَةٌ مِثْلُهَا قَطَّ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَبَضَ أَرْوَاحَكُمْ حِيْنَ شَاءَ يَا بِلَالُ قُمْ فَإِنَّ النَّاسَ بِالصَّلوةِ فَتَوَضَّأَ فَلَمَّا ارْتَفَعَتِ الشَّمْسُ وَابْيَضَّتُ قَامَ فَصَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ جَمَاعَةً دونوں روایتوں سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لیلۃ التعریس کی صبح کو دن نکلنے کے بعد اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ فجر کی نماز کی قضا فرمائی ہے۔ امام شافعی نے اس روایت سے استدلال کیا ہے جو مسلم میں حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے مروی ہے یعنی أَمَرَ بِلَالًا فَاقَامَ الصَّلاةَ فَصَلَّى ربهِمُ الصُّبحُ یعنی آپ نے بلال کو حکم کیا پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صحابہ کو اقامت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائی ۔ اس حدیث میں اذان کا ذکر نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قضا نماز کے لئے اقامت پر اکتفا کرنا کافی ہے۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ دوسری صحیح روایتوں میں اذان کا ذکر موجود ہے لہذا زیادت پر عمل کرنا اولی ہے۔ ہمارے مسلک کی تائید اس روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ غزوہ خندق کے موقعہ پر جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی چار نماز میں فوت ہو گئیں تو آپ نے اذان واقامت کے ساتھ ان کی قضا فرمائی ۔ پس اتنی احادیث صحیحہ کے ہوتے ہوئے امام شافعی کا اختلاف کرنا مناسب معلوم نہیں ہوتا ۔
And the iqamah when they slept through the dawn prayer and performed it after the sun had risen – meaning the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah when the companions had slept through the Fajr prayer, and they performed it after sunrise. The two shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) transmitted this incident as follows: 'Abdullah ibn Abi Fadada from his father said: We travelled with the Messenger of Allah one night, and some people said: Would you not halt with us, O Messenger of Allah? He said: I fear you would sleep through the prayer. Bilal said: I will wake you. They lay down, and Bilal leaned his back against his mount, and his eyes overcame him, so he slept. The Prophet (peace be upon him) woke up when the edge of the sun had appeared. He said: O Bilal, what happened to your statement? He said: I have never had a sleep like it. He said: Allah the Exalted took your souls when He willed. O Bilal, get up and call the people to prayer. So he performed ablution, and when the sun had risen and become white, he got up and led the people in congregation. From both narrations it is understood that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of the night of stopping after sunrise with adhan and iqamah. Imam Shafi'i used as evidence the narration in Muslim from Abu Hurairah: 'He commanded Bilal, so he gave iqamah for the prayer, and he led them in the morning prayer.' That hadith does not mention adhan, so it established that for a missed prayer, it is sufficient to rely on iqamah. The response to this is that other sound narrations mention adhan, so acting upon the addition is preferable. Our school is also supported by the narration that during the Battle of the Trench, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) missed four prayers, he made them up with adhan and iqamah. So with so many sound hadith, Imam Shafi'i's disagreement does not seem appropriate.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling of adhan and iqamah for a missed (qada) prayer. The Hanafi position is that both adhan and iqamah are recited, based on the well-known incident of Laylat al-Ta'ris (the night of stopping) when the Prophet (SAW) and companions slept through Fajr. The Prophet commanded Bilal to give both adhan and iqamah before making up the prayer. This is recorded in Bukhari and Muslim. Imam Shafi'i argues, based on a different hadith in Muslim (from Abu Hurairah) that only iqamah is sufficient, because that hadith only mentions iqamah. The Hanafi response is that the presence of adhan in other authentic narrations is an addition (ziyadah) that must be accepted, and acting upon the more complete narration is preferable. Additionally, another incident from the Battle of the Trench confirms that the Prophet made up four missed prayers with both adhan and iqamah. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains that for any qada prayer, adhan and iqamah are both Sunnah Muakkadah.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, used to announce the time of prayer and invite people to it.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer, just before the prayer starts, with slightly different wording than adhan.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time has elapsed.
زيادة (ziyadah): An addition in a narration that is not present in another equally authentic narration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the Shafi'i proof that only iqamah is needed for qada?
A) Because the Shafi'i hadith is weaker in chain.
B) Because other authentic narrations include adhan, and the addition is accepted.
C) Because the Hanafi school does not accept any hadith from Abu Hurairah.
D) Because iqamah is never sufficient even for on-time prayers.

Key Takeaway
For qada prayers, the Hanafi school requires both adhan and iqamah as sunnah muakkadah, based on the Prophet's practice in multiple incidents, and the principle of accepting an addition (ziyadah) in narrations.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling for Multiple Missed Prayers: First with Adhan and Iqamah, Rest Optional
Ruling with proof for qada of multiple missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for multiple missed prayers and distinguish between the first and subsequent prayers in qada.

Core Idea
The first missed prayer gets full adhan and iqamah; for the rest, you have a choice.

When a person has missed several obligatory prayers, they must make them up in order. The first qada is performed with both adhan and iqamah, as the Prophet did. For subsequent qada, the Hanafi school gives flexibility: you may repeat adhan and iqamah or suffice with iqamah only. This lesson explains the evidence and the reasoning behind this differentiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The making up (qada) of multiple missed prayers. Specifically, the recitation of adhan and iqamah during qada.
The ruling differs between the first missed prayer and the rest.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris and the incident of Ahzab where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each of the four missed prayers.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this proof establish the ruling? The Prophet's explicit command for each prayer to have adhan and iqamah indicates the practice for qada. The reasoning for the choice in subsequent prayers is that adhan is for summoning, and the people are already present.
The wisdom (hikmah) behind the choice is istihsan based on necessity.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad (in a non-Zahir al-Riwayah narration) holds that only iqamah is sufficient for subsequent prayers. The mashayikh suggest this may be the unanimous view of the three founders. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the choice.
The difference affects whether one has the option to repeat adhan or not.

حدیث لیلۃ العرمیں ہے اور باقی نمازوں کے حق میں اختیار ہے۔ جی چاہے ہر نماز کے لئے اذان بھی دے اور اقامت بھی کہے تا کہ ضاء اداء کے موافق ہو جائے اسکی تائید اس روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو علامہ ابن الہمام نے امام ابو یوسف کے واسطے سے بیان کیا ہے إِنَّهُ حِيْنَ شَغَلَهُمُ الْكُفَّارُ يَوْمَ الْأَحْزَابِ عَنْ اَرْبَعِ صَلواتٍ عَنِ الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ وَالعِشَاءِ قَضَاهُنَّ عَلَى الْوَلَاء وَاَمَرَ بِلَالًا أنْ يُؤَذِنَ وَيُقِيمَ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُنَّ ۔ غزوہ احزاب کے موقعہ پر کفار نے آپ کو چار نمازوں سے مشغول کر دیا۔ یعنی ظہر، عصر، مغرب اور عشاء سے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کی علی الترتیب قضاء فرمائی اور بلال کو حکم دیا کہ وہ ان میں سے ہر نماز کے لئے اذان بھی دے اورا قامت بھی کہے اور جی چاہے اقامت پر اکتفاء کرے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ اذان ہوتی ہے استحضار کے لئے اور یہاں سب حاضر میں اس لئے اذان کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں رہی۔
غیر روایت اصول میں امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ اگر چند نمازیں فوت ہو جائیں تو پہلی نماز کی قضاء اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ کرے اور باقی نمازوں کی قضاء نصرف اقامت کے ساتھ کرے۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ قول امام محمد ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام ابو حنیفہ سب کا ہے
For many missed prayers, for the first there is adhan and iqamah, and for the rest it is sufficient to rely on iqamah only. If several prayers are missed, he gives adhan for the first and iqamah because of what we narrated, and he has a choice for the rest: if he wishes, he can give adhan and iqamah so that the qada matches the ada, and if he wishes, he can restrict to iqamah because adhan is for summoning and they are present. The author said: It is narrated from Muhammad that iqamah is performed for what comes after them. They said: It is possible that this is their statement. Translation: Then if several prayers are missed, he gives adhan and iqamah for the first. Because of the hadith we narrated, and for the rest he has a choice: if he wishes, he gives adhan and iqamah for each so that qada matches ada, and if he wishes, he suffices with iqamah because adhan is to summon and they are all present. The author said that it is narrated from Muhammad that iqamah will be said for the prayers after the first. The mashayikh said that it is possible that this is the saying of all of them. Explanation: If a person misses several prayers, for the first he gives adhan and iqamah. The proof is the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris. For the rest, he has a choice. The supporting narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is that when the disbelievers on the Day of Ahzab occupied the Prophet from four prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha), he made them up in order and commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each one. And if he wishes, he may suffice with iqamah because adhan is for summoning and they are present. In another narration (Usul), it is narrated from Muhammad that if several prayers are missed, he makes up the first with adhan and iqamah, and for the rest he makes up with only iqamah. The mashayikh said: It is possible that this is the saying of Imam Muhammad, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Abu Hanifah all.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for someone who has missed multiple prayers (fawa'it kathirah). The Hanafi position is that for the first missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah are recited, based on the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'ris. For the remaining missed prayers, the person has a choice: either repeat adhan and iqamah for each so that the qada resembles the ada (on-time prayer), or suffice with only iqamah. The reason is that adhan is meant to summon people, and when making up multiple prayers, the people are already present. However, there is a narration from Imam Muhammad (in the Usul) that only iqamah should be said for the subsequent prayers, and the mashayikh (later scholars) indicated that this might be the consensus of the three founders (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The passage also cites the incident of the Battle of the Trench where the Prophet made up four prayers with adhan and iqamah for each, supporting the permissibility of doing so. The core lesson is that the first qada is emphasized, and thereafter flexibility is given.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that need to be made up (qada).
أول (awwal): The first missed prayer in chronological order among the fawa'it.
استحضار (istihdar): Summoning or calling people to gather for prayer; the purpose of adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only iqamah is recited.
B) Both adhan and iqamah are recited.
C) Neither adhan nor iqamah is recited.
D) Only adhan is recited.

Key Takeaway
In making up multiple missed prayers, the first requires adhan and iqamah; subsequent prayers give the choice to repeat both or suffice with iqamah.

Adhan and Iqamah without Wudu: Ruling and Dispute with Awza'i
States that adhan without wudu is valid and wudu is mustahab, while iqamah without wudu is makrooh; refutes Awza'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah without wudu and evaluate the dispute with Imam al-Awza'i by identifying the basis of each school's interpretation.

Core Idea
Adhan is dhikr, not prayer — so wudu is recommended, not required; iqamah is directly tied to prayer, so its lack of wudu is disliked.

This lesson examines the Hanafi distinction between adhan and iqamah regarding the requirement of wudu. While both are calls to prayer, the adhan is considered a form of dhikr, making wudu merely recommended (mustahab). The iqamah, however, is directly connected to the prayer, so performing it without wudu is disliked (makruh). We will also explore the opposing view of Imam al-Awza'i, who considered wudu a condition for adhan based on a hadith, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What is the ruling for adhan without wudu? For iqamah without wudu?
2
Locate the proof
What evidence is given for the Hanafi position? (dhikr analogy)
3
Examine the opposing proof
What hadith does Awza'i cite?
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school interpret that hadith? (istihbab)
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? (validity vs. invalidity)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُؤَذِنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى طُهْرٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ ذِكْرُ وَلَيْسَ بِصَلُوةٍ فَكَانَ الْوُضُوءَ فِيهِ اسْتِحْبَابًا كَمَا فِي الْقِرَاءَةِ ترجمہ اور مناسب ہے کہ اذان دے اور اقامت کہے طہارت کی حالت میں۔ پس اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اذان ذکر ہے نماز نہیں ہے پس وضو ہونا اس میں مستحب ہوگا جیسے قرآن پڑھنے میں ہے۔ تشریح مستحب یہ ہے کہ اذان واقامت باوضوری جائے لیکن اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اذان ذکر اللہ ہے نہ کہ نماز اور ذکر کرنے کے لئے وضو مستحب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ واجب ، اس لئے اذان دینے کے لئے وضو کرنا مستحب ہوگا جیسا کہ قرآن پڑھنے کے لئے باوضو ہونا مستحب ہے۔
امام اوزاعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اذان کے لئے وضو کرنا شرط ہے کیونکہ ترمذی نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے روایت کی قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ الله لَا يُون إلا الوی یعنی ابو ہریرہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اذان وہی دے جو باوضو ہو۔ مگر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس يُؤَدِّنُ المُتَوَضّى سے استحباب ہی مراد ہو گا۔
بغیر وضوا قامت کہنا مکروہ ہے
وَيُكْرَهُ أَن تُقِيمَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وَضُوءٍ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْفَصْلِ بَيْنَ الْإِقَامَةِ وَالصَّلوةِ وَيُروى أَنَّهُ لَاتَكُرَهُ الإِقَامَةُ أَيضاً لأنَّه اَحَدُ الأَذَانَيْنِ وَيُروى أَنه يَكْرَهُ الأَذَانُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ دَاعِيًا إلى مَالَا يُجِيبُ بِنَفْسِه
It is proper (yambaghi) that you give adhan and iqamah in a state of purity. If he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible, because it is a dhikr and not a prayer, so wudu is recommended (istihbab) just as in recitation (qira'ah). Translation: It is appropriate to give adhan and iqamah in a state of purity. If he gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible because adhan is dhikr, not prayer, so wudu is mustahab like in reciting Quran. Explanation: It is mustahab that adhan and iqamah be done with wudu. But if he gave adhan without wudu, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is valid without karahah. The proof is that adhan is dhikr of Allah, not prayer, and for dhikr, wudu is mustahab not wajib. So doing adhan with wudu is mustahab, just as reciting Quran with wudu is mustahab. Imam Awza'i says that wudu is a condition (shart) for adhan, because Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'None gives adhan except the one with wudu.' But we say that 'la yu'adhdhin illa al-mutawadda' (no one gives adhan except the one with wudu) implies recommendation (istihbab), not condition. Giving iqamah without wudu is makruh, because of the separation (fasl) between the iqamah and prayer. And it is narrated that iqamah is also not makruh because it is one of the two calls. And it is narrated that adhan is also makruh because it becomes a call to that which he himself does not answer.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of performing adhan and iqamah without wudu. It begins by stating that it is recommended (yambaghi) to give both with wudu. If someone gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible (ja'iz) because adhan is a form of dhikr, not a prayer, and wudu is only mustahab for dhikr, as with Quran recitation. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is no karahah (dislike) for adhan without wudu. The passage then presents the view of Imam al-Awza'i, who considered wudu a condition for adhan based on a hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'None gives adhan except the one with wudu.' The Hanafi response interprets this hadith as indicating recommendation (istihbab), not obligation (wujub) or condition. The reasoning is that the same wording can be used for recommendation, as in similar contexts. For iqamah, the ruling is different: giving iqamah without wudu is makruh because it creates a separation (fasl) between the iqamah and the prayer, as iqamah immediately precedes the prayer. However, there is a narration that iqamah is also not makruh (because it is one of the two adhans), and another that adhan is makruh because the caller would be summoning others to something he himself does not attend to (if he has no wudu). The relied-upon Hanafi position is: adhan without wudu is valid without karahah, but iqamah without wudu is makruh. This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
وضوء (wudu): Ritual ablution; washing of specific body parts for prayer.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an action that is encouraged but not obligatory or conditionally required.
فصل (fasl): Separation; a break between the iqamah and the prayer that is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if someone gives the iqamah without wudu?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but makruh.
C) It is valid and not makruh.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, adhan is dhikr, so wudu is mustahab; iqamah is directly tied to prayer, so wudu is recommended and its absence is disliked.

Wudu for Adhan and Iqamah is Mustahabb, Not Wajib
Ruling that adhan and iqamah should be with wudu, and wudu is mustahabb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu for adhan and iqamah, and explain why the imperative in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation.

Core Idea
Wudu is recommended for adhan, not required — because adhan is dhikr, not salah.

This passage clarifies that while wudu is a condition for prayer, it is not obligatory for the call to prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts of worship that require purification and those that do not. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary imposition of conditions upon permissible acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that the act under discussion is giving adhan (and iqamah), and the ruling is that wudu is mustahabb (recommended). The passage states it is appropriate (yanbaghi) to be with wudu, but if done without, it is permissible.
The phrase 'yanbaghi' indicates recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof given is an analogy (qiyas) with Quran recitation: adhan is dhikr, just like reciting Quran; wudu is recommended for dhikr, not wajib. This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
No explicit textual evidence mandates wudu for adhan.
3
Analyze the opposing view
Imam Awza'i considers wudu a condition (shart) for adhan, based on the hadith 'La yu'adhdhinu illa al-mutawaddi' (Only the one with wudu gives adhan). Understand his evidence.
The hadith is reported by Tirmidhi.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret the imperative in the hadith as indicating istihbab (recommendation), not obligation, because of contextual evidence: adhan is dhikr, and there is no other evidence making it wajib.
This is a key usul principle: an imperative can be for recommendation if there is a qarinah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis say adhan without wudu is valid and not disliked; Awza'i says it is invalid or sinful. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
This difference affects daily practice for muazzins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُؤَذِنَ وَيُقِيمَ عَلَى طُهْرٍ فَإِنْ أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ ذِكْرُ وَلَيْسَ بِصَلُوةٍ فَكَانَ الْوُضُوءَ فِيهِ اسْتِحْبَابًا كَمَا فِي الْقِرَاءَةِ ترجمہ اور مناسب ہے کہ اذان دے اور اقامت کہے طہارت کی حالت میں۔ پس اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اذان ذکر ہے نماز نہیں ہے پس وضو ہونا اس میں مستحب ہوگا جیسے قرآن پڑھنے میں ہے۔ تشریح مستحب یہ ہے کہ اذان واقامت باوضوری جائے لیکن اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اذان ذکر اللہ ہے نہ کہ نماز اور ذکر کرنے کے لئے وضو مستحب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ واجب ، اس لئے اذان دینے کے لئے وضو کرنا مستحب ہوگا جیسا کہ قرآن پڑھنے کے لئے باوضو ہونا مستحب ہے۔ امام اوزاعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اذان کے لئے وضو کرنا شرط ہے کیونکہ ترمذی نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے روایت کی قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ الله لَا يُؤَنُ إلَّا الْمُتَوَضِّى یعنی ابو ہریرہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اذان وہی دے جو باوضو ہو۔ مگر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس يُؤَدِّنُ المُتَوَضّى سے استحباب ہی مراد ہو گا۔
And it is appropriate that you give adhan and iqamah on taharah. So if one gave adhan without wudu, it is permissible, because it is dhikr and not salah. So wudu in it is mustahabb, as in Quran recitation. Translation: And it is appropriate that one gives adhan and iqamah in a state of purification. So if one gave adhan without wudu, it is permissible because adhan is dhikr, not salah, so having wudu is mustahabb in it, like in Quran recitation. Commentary: It is mustahabb that adhan and iqamah be with wudu, but if one gave adhan without wudu, according to Zahir al-Riwayah it is permissible without dislike. The proof is that adhan is dhikr of Allah, not salah, and for dhikr, wudu is mustahabb, not wajib. So for adhan, wudu is mustahabb, just as for Quran recitation, being with wudu is mustahabb. Imam Awza'i says that wudu is a condition for adhan because Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Hurairah who said the Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'Only the one with wudu gives adhan.' But we say that 'the one with wudu gives adhan' indicates mustahabb only.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof. The author states the general principle: it is recommended (mustahabb) to be in a state of wudu when giving adhan or iqamah. However, if one gives adhan without wudu, it is still valid (ja'iz) and not disliked, according to the established transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah). The proof is that adhan is dhikr, not salah, and wudu for dhikr is only mustahabb, not wajib. This is analogous to Quran recitation. The passage then mentions the opposing view of Imam Awza'i, who considers wudu a condition based on a hadith from Tirmidhi. The Hanafi response is that the imperative form (li-yu'adhdhin) in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab) due to the absence of evidence making it obligatory. This demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle that an imperative does not automatically obligate if there is a contextual indication (qarinah) suggesting non-obligation.

Key Terms
اذان (adhān): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases recited to announce the beginning of the prescribed prayer time.
اقامت (iqāmah): The second call to prayer, recited just before the prayer begins, signaling the congregation to stand in rows.
وضو (wuḍū’): Ritual washing of specific body parts with water, performed to purify from minor ritual impurity (hadath asghar).
مستحب (mustaḥabb): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; performing it earns reward, omitting it does not incur sin.
طہارت (ṭahārah): Ritual purity, either from minor impurity (wudu) or major impurity (ghusl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving adhan without wudu?
A) It is invalid (batil).
B) It is valid but makruh (disliked).
C) It is valid and not disliked (ja'iz bila karahah).
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Wudu for adhan and iqamah is mustahabb, not wajib, because adhan is dhikr and does not require ritual purity.

Iqamah Without Wudu: Makruh or Not?
Ruling on iqamah without wudu with two riwayat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqamah without wudu and identify the two riwayat regarding adhan without wudu, explaining the basis of each position.

Core Idea
Iqamah without wudu is makruh due to disrupting continuity; adhan without wudu has two narrations.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on giving iqamah (and adhan) without wudu. While the base text (matn) clearly states that iqamah without wudu is disliked (makruh), two narrations from Imam Karkhi introduce alternative views. Understanding this dispute requires examining the legal reasoning behind each position and how the school resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Read the matn's first statement: 'وَيُكْرَهُ أَن تُقِيمَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وَضُوءٍ' – it is disliked to give iqamah without wudu. Note the reason given: the separation (fasl) it creates between iqamah and salah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
2
Analyze the first alternative riwayah
The text then mentions a narration that iqamah is not makruh because it is one of the two adhans, and adhan without wudu is not makruh. Understand the qiyas: iqamah is analogous to adhan, which is permissible without wudu.
This riwayah is attributed to Imam Karkhi.
3
Analyze the second alternative riwayah
Another narration states that adhan itself is makruh without wudu, based on the ethical principle that the caller should not invite to something he himself neglects (Quran 2:44). If adhan is makruh, then iqamah, being like adhan, would also be makruh.
This strengthens the original ruling.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi who follows the primary ruling will consider iqamah without wudu as makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). One who follows the first riwayah will see no dislike. The majority practice adopts the first ruling from the matn.
Knowing this ikhtilaf avoids confusion in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ أَن تُقِيمَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وَضُوءٍ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْفَصْلِ بَيْنَ الْإِقَامَةِ وَالصَّلوةِ وَيُروى أَنَّهُ لَاتَكُرَهُ الإِقَامَةُ أَيضاً لأنَّه اَحَدُ الأَذَانَيْنِ وَيُروى أَنه يَكْرَهُ الأَذَانُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ دَاعِيًا إلى مَالَا يُجِيبُ بِنَفْسِه ترجمہ اور بے وضوا قامت کہنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس میں اقامت اور نماز کے درمیان فصل لازم آتا ہے اور روایت کیا گیا کہ اقامت بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بھی دو زانوں میں سے ایک اذان ہے۔ اور روایت ہے کہ اذان بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ ایسی چیز کی طرف دعوت دینے والا ہوگا جس کو وہ خود قبول نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح، مسئلہ، بے وضو اقامت کہنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں مؤذن کی اقامت اور نماز کے درمیان فصل لازم آتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اقامت نماز سے متصلا مشروع کی گئی ہے۔ امام کرختی نے روایت کی ہے کہ اقامت بھی بے وضو مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اقامت دوازانوں میں سے ایک ہے اور اذان بلا وضو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اقامت بھی بلا وضو مکروہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور امام کرختی نے یہ بھی روایت کی ہے کہ بے وضو اذان بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ مؤذن اذان کے ذریعہ لوگوں کو نماز کی تیاری کی دعوت دیتا ہے اور خود اس نے تیاری نہیں کی ہے لہذا یہ لوگوں کو ایسی چیز کی طرف دعوت دینے والا قرار پائے گا۔ جس کو خود قبول نہیں کرتا پس یہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول أَتَامُرُونَ النَّاسَ بِالْبِرِّ وَ تَنسَوْنَ اَنْفُسَكُمْ کے تحت داخل ہوگا ۔
And it is disliked to give iqamah without wudu because of the separation (fasl) it creates between iqamah and salah. And it is narrated that iqamah is also not disliked (makruh) because it is one of the two adhans. And it is narrated that adhan is also disliked because the caller becomes a caller to what he himself does not fulfill. Translation: And giving iqamah without wudu is makruh because it necessitates a separation between iqamah and salah. And it is narrated that iqamah is not makruh because it is one of the two adhans. And it is narrated that adhan is also makruh because the caller would be inviting to something he himself does not accept. Commentary: The issue is that giving iqamah without wudu is makruh because in this case there is a separation between the mu'adhdhin's iqamah and salah, whereas iqamah is prescribed to be immediately consecutive (muttasil) to salah. Imam Karkhi narrated that iqamah without wudu is not makruh because iqamah is one of the two adhans, and adhan without wudu is not makruh. Therefore iqamah without wudu would also not be makruh. And Imam Karkhi also narrated that adhan without wudu is makruh because through adhan the mu'adhdhin calls people to prepare for salah while he himself has not prepared, so he becomes a caller to something he himself does not accept, falling under Allah's statement 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon people while you forget yourselves?' (2:44).
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding iqamah and adhan without wudu. The matn states that iqamah without wudu is makruh (disliked) because it breaks the required continuity (muttasil) between iqamah and salah. However, two narrations (riwayat) are mentioned: one says iqamah is not makruh because it is considered one of the two adhans (the other being adhan itself), and since adhan without wudu is not makruh, iqamah follows suit. Another narration says adhan without wudu is makruh because the mu'adhdhin calls others to purification while he himself is unpurified, thus falling under Quranic criticism of hypocrisy. The commentary by Imam Karkhi supports both views. The net result: there is ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school on this issue. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) appears to be that iqamah without wudu is makruh tanzihi, while for adhan the stronger view is that it is also makruh tanzihi, but the matter is not strict.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makrūh): An act that is disliked in Islamic law; it is not sinful but should be avoided.
فصل (faṣl): A separation or break between two connected acts; in this context, the undesirable gap between iqamah and the start of salah.
متصلا (muttasil): Immediately consecutive; iqamah should be directly followed by salah without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is the ruling on giving iqamah without wudu?
A) It is invalid (batil).
B) It is makruh (disliked).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is not makruh because iqamah is one of the two adhans.

Key Takeaway
Iqamah without wudu is makruh tanzihi due to the required continuity with salah, though alternative riwayat exist within the school.

Adhan in Janabah: Ruling and Repetition
Ruling with proof via qiyas and citation from al-Jami' al-Saghir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan in janabah, explain the qiyas-based distinction from adhan without wudu, and apply the preferred view on repetition.

Core Idea
Adhan in janabah is valid but makruh; repeating it is mustahabb, not wajib.

This lesson examines the ruling of adhan while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah). The Hanafi school considers such an adhan makruh (disliked) based on a single narration, but it remains valid. The passage also addresses the question of repetition, distinguishing between adhan and iqamah based on established practice. Understanding this ruling clarifies the relationship between adhan and salah in terms of purity requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that giving adhan while in janabah is makruh. Confirm that this is based on a single narration (riwayah wahidah), meaning there is no conflicting narration of non-karahah.
Contrast with adhan without wudu, which has conflicting narrations.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The evidence is qiyas (analogy) on the resemblance (shabah) between adhan and salah. Both involve takbir, facing qiblah, and arranged words. Because of this resemblance, purification from major hadath is required, but not from minor hadath.
This is a form of qiyas shabah (analogy based on resemblance).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The specific point: the carrier of the analogy is the shared resemblance, and the ruling (purification from major hadath is emphasized) is transferred from salah to adhan. The text explains that the stricter requirement applies only to major impurity, not minor, because of two complementary aspects of resemblance.
The distinction between major and minor hadath is crucial.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on repetition
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: two narrations exist regarding whether a junub must repeat the adhan. The text from al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that repetition is ahabb (more beloved), i.e., mustahabb. The preferred view (ashbah) is to repeat adhan but not iqamah, because repetition of adhan is generally allowed (mashru').
The ikhtilaf is only on repetition, not on validity or karahah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa: adhan in janabah is makruh tanzihi; it is recommended (mustahabb) to repeat that adhan later when in a state of purity, but it is not obligatory. The iqamah is not repeated. The salah performed after the makruh adhan is valid without repetition.
This is based on Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir and the author's tarjih.

Source Text

وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ تُوَذِنَ وَهُوَ جُنُبْ رِوَايَةً وَاحِدَةً وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ عَلَى إِحْدَى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ هُوَ أَنَّ لِلأَذَانِ شَبِهَا بِالصَّلوة فَيشْتَرطُ الطَّهَارَةُ عَنْ أَغْلَةِ الْحَدَثَيْنِ دُونَ اَخَفِّهِمَا عَمَلًا بِالشَّبُهَيْنِ وَ فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ إِذَا أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوع وَاقَامَةٍ لَا يُعِيدُ وَالْجُنُّبُ اَحَبُّ إِلَى أَنْ تُعِبْدُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُعِدُ أَجْزَاهُ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَلِخِفَةَ الْحَدَثِ وَامَّا الثَّانِي فَفِي الإِعَادَةِ بِسَبَبِ الجَنَابَةِ رِوَايَتَانِ وَالأَشْبَهُ أنْ يُعَادَ الأَذَانُ دُونَ الإقامة لأنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْآذَانِ مَشْرُوعُ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ وَقَوْلُهُ إِن لَمْ يُعِدُ أَجْزَاهُ يَعْنِي الصَّلوةَ لِأَنَّهَا جَائِزَةٌ بِدُونِ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ ترجمہ اور جنسی کی اذان مکروہ ہے۔ روایت واحدہ ہے۔ اور وجہ فرق دو روایتوں میں سے ایک پر یہ ہے کہ اذان نماز کے ساتھ مشابہت رکھتی ہے۔ لہذا الغلظ حدثین سے طہارت شرط ہے نہ کہ اخب حدثین سے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کرنے کی وجہ سے ۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جب بے وضو اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو اعادہ نہ کرے اور جنبی (نے اگر ایسا کیا ) تو میرے نزدیک اعادہ کرنا پسندیدہ ہے ۔ اور اگر عادہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کافی ہو جائے گا۔ بہر حال اول تو حدث کے خفیف ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور رہا ثانی تو جنابت کی وجہ سے اس کے اعادہ میں دو روایتیں ہیں اور اشبہ بالفقہ یہ ہے کہ اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے نہ کہ اقامت کا۔ اس لئے کہ اذان کا تکرار مشروع ہے لیکن اقامت کا تکرار مشروع نہیں ہے۔ اور امام محمد کا قول إِن لَمْ يُعد أجزاه یعنی نماز، کیونکہ نماز بغیر اذان اورا قامت کے جائز ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بحالت جنابت اذان دینا مکروہ ہے اور اس میں فقط ایک ہی روایت ہے یعنی کراہت کی روایت اور عدم کراہت کی کوئی روایت نہیں ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ محدث کی اذان میں کراہت اور عدم کراہت کی دونوں روایتیں ہیں۔ پس جنسی کی اذان اور عدم کراہت کی روایات پر محدث کی اذان کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اذان نماز کے مشابہ ہے اس طور پر کہ دونوں کو تکبیر کے ساتھ شروع کیا جاتا ہے۔ دونوں استقبال قبلہ کے ساتھ ادا ہوتے ہیں اور کلمات اذان اسی طرح مرتب ہیں جس طرح ارکان نماز
And it is disliked to give adhan while in janabah, in a single narration (only one riwayah). And the reason for the distinction (between this and adhan without wudu) according to one of the two riwayat is that adhan has resemblance (shabah) to salah, so purification from the more severe of the two hadath (major impurity) is required, not from the lighter, acting upon both resemblances. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: When one gives adhan without wudu and iqamah (without wudu), he does not repeat. But for the junub, it is more beloved to me that he repeats. And if he does not repeat, it suffices him. As for the first (without wudu), it is due to the lightness of hadath. As for the second (janabah), there are two narrations regarding repetition. And the more suitable (ashbah) is that adhan is repeated, but not iqamah, because repetition of adhan is prescribed (mashru'), whereas repetition of iqamah is not prescribed. And his statement 'if he does not repeat, it suffices him' means the salah (is valid) because salah is permissible without adhan and iqamah. Translation: And the adhan of a junub is makruh, in a single narration. The basis for the distinction between the two riwayat is that adhan resembles salah; therefore, purification from the major hadath is , not the minor, by acting on both similarities. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: if one gives adhan without wudu and iqamah, he does not repeat. But if he is junub, it is preferable to repeat. If he does not repeat, it is sufficient. The first is due to the lightness of the hadath. The second has two narrations regarding repetition. The more appropriate is to repeat adhan, not iqamah, because repeating adhan is prescribed but not iqamah. Imam Muhammad says: 'if he does not repeat, it suffices him' meaning the salah, because salah is valid without adhan and iqamah. Commentary: This issue: giving adhan in janabah is makruh, and there is only one narration on this (the narration of karahah). There is no narration of non-karahah. It has passed earlier that regarding adhan without wudu, there are narrations of karahah and non-karahah. The reason for the distinction between adhan of junub and adhan of hadath (minor impurity) is that adhan resembles salah: both begin with takbir, both are performed facing the qiblah, and the words of adhan are arranged similarly to the pillars of salah.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for adhan while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah). It is makruh (disliked), and unlike the case of minor impurity (hadath asghar), there is no difference of opinion on the karahah; it is established in a single narration. The reason is that adhan shares similarities (shabah) with salah, and for major impurity, purification is more strictly emphasized. However, if a junub gives adhan, it is still valid, and the salah performed thereafter without repeating the adhan is valid. The text then cites Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir: for adhan without wudu, no repetition is needed; for janabah, repeating the adhan is preferable (ahabbu ilayya) but not obligatory. There are two narrations on whether repetition is required; the preferred view (ashbah) is to repeat the adhan but not the iqamah, because repeating adhan is generally allowed (mashru'), while repeating iqamah is not. The commentary further explains that the analogy between adhan and salah—both begin with takbir, face qiblah, and have arranged words—justifies the stricter rule for janabah. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi principle of distinguishing between minor and major hadath based on the severity of impurity and resemblance to salah.

Key Terms
جنابت (janābah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
حدث اصغر (ḥadath aṣghar): Minor ritual impurity removed by wudu
حدث اکبر (ḥadath akbar): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
اعادہ (iʿādah): Repetition of an act
اشبہ (ashbah): More suitable or more appropriate opinion

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Yes, the salah is valid because adhan is not a condition for salah.
C) Yes, but only if he repeats the iqamah instead.
D) No, the salah is valid only if he makes wudu before salah.

Key Takeaway
Adhan in janabah is valid but makruh; repeating the adhan is mustahabb but not obligatory, and iqamah is not repeated.
