Ruling on Iqama and Adhan without Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan/iqama without wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqama and adhan without wudu, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement, and explain the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Core Idea
Iqama without wudu is makruh; adhan without wudu is also makruh—don't call others to purity while neglecting your own.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines whether iqama and adhan are valid without wudu, and whether they are disliked. The text presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: one view holds that iqama without wudu is makruh due to the interval it creates with prayer, while Imam al-Karkhi narrates that it is not makruh. For adhan, a similar difference appears, supported by a Quranic verse. We will trace the arguments and understand the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling on iqama
The text first states that iqama without wudu is makruh because it forces a separation between the call and the prayer, while the Sunnah prescribes them to be consecutive.
The phrase 'فصل لازم آتا ہے' indicates a necessary interval.
2
Identify the ruling on adhan without wudu
A narration is presented that adhan without wudu is also makruh. The reason is that the mu'adhdhin calls others to prayer without preparing himself, falling under the Quranic reproach: 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon people and forget yourselves?'
The Quranic verse (2:44) is cited as the proof.
3
Examine the counter-narration from Imam al-Karkhi
Imam al-Karkhi narrates two seemingly contradictory reports: (1) iqama without wudu is not makruh because it is one of the two calls, and adhan without wudu is not makruh; (2) adhan without wudu is makruh. This creates an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
The text uses the term 'روایت ہے' to denote a weaker transmission.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The structure of al-Hidayah and the strength of the interval argument suggest that the makruh view is relied upon. The Quranic analogy for adhan reinforces the dislike. The mufta bihi is that both iqama and adhan without wudu are makruh.
Imam al-Karkhi's narration is considered a weaker transmission (nawadir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بھی دو زانوں میں سے ایک اذان ہے۔ اور روایت ہے کہ اذان بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ ایسی چیز کی طرف دعوت دینے والا ہوگا جس کو وہ خود قبول نہیں کرتا۔
تشریح، مسئلہ، بے وضو اقامت کہنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں مؤذن کی اقامت اور نماز کے درمیان فصل لازم آتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اقامت نماز سے متصلا مشروع کی گئی ہے۔ امام کرختی نے روایت کی ہے کہ اقامت بھی بے وضو مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اقامت دوازانوں میں سے ایک ہے اور اذان بلا وضو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اقامت بھی بلا وضو مکروہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور امام کرختی نے یہ بھی روایت کی ہے کہ بے وضو اذان بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ مؤذن اذان کے ذریعہ لوگوں کو نماز کی تیاری کی دعوت دیتا ہے اور خود اس نے تیاری نہیں کی ہے لہذا یہ لوگوں کو ایسی چیز کی طرف دعوت دینے والا قرار پائے گا۔ جس کو خود قبول نہیں کرتا پس یہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول أَتَامُرُونَ النَّاسَ بِالْبِرِّ وَ تَنسَوْنَ اَنْفُسَكُمْ کے تحت داخل ہوگا ۔ اس وجہ سے کہا گیا کہ بے وضواذان بھی مکروہ ہے۔
It is not makruh because it is also one of the two calls. And there is a narration that adhan is also makruh because it will be inviting to something that he himself does not accept. Explanation: The issue: Saying iqama without wudu is makruh because in this case there is an interval between the mu'adhdhin's iqama and the prayer, whereas the iqama is prescribed to be immediately connected to the prayer. Imam al-Karkhi narrated that iqama without wudu is not makruh because iqama is one of the two calls, and adhan without wudu is not makruh. Therefore iqama without wudu will not be makruh. And Imam al-Karkhi also narrated that adhan without wudu is makruh because the mu'adhdhin calls people to prepare for prayer while he himself has not prepared, so he becomes one who invites to something he does not accept. This falls under the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon people and forget yourselves?' For this reason it is said that adhan without wudu is makruh.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on saying iqama and adhan without wudu. The author first mentions that iqama without wudu is makruh because it creates an interval between the call and the prayer, contradicting the sunnah of immediate connection. However, Imam al-Karkhi narrates that iqama without wudu is not makruh, drawing an analogy with adhan without wudu, which is also not makruh according to one view. On the other hand, al-Karkhi also narrates that adhan without wudu is makruh because the mu'adhdhin is calling others to prayer while neglecting his own preparation, which is likened to the Quranic verse reproaching those who enjoin goodness but forget themselves. The text thus shows two narrations: one considers iqama without wudu makruh, another does not; and for adhan without wudu, there is a narration that it is makruh. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the structure suggests the first view (makruh) is the default.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases recited to announce the time of prayer.
اقامت (iqama): The second call to prayer, recited immediately before the prayer begins.
وضو (wudu): Ritual ablution required for prayer and other acts of worship.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an action that is blameworthy but not sinful enough to be haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is iqama without wudu considered makruh?
A) Because it is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Because it creates an interval between the iqama and the prayer.
C) Because the mu'adhdhin forgets to perform wudu.
D) Because the Quran explicitly forbids it.

Key Takeaway
Iqama and adhan without wudu are valid but makruh; the stronger evidence from the Sunnah and Quran supports this ruling.

Ruling on Adhan in Janabah: Makruh and the Qiyas of Resemblance
Explains the ruling and the qiyas reasoning for adhan in janabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan in janabah and explain the qiyas shabah reasoning that distinguishes it from adhan in minor impurity.

Core Idea
Adhan in janabah is makruh due to its resemblance to prayer, but not in minor impurity because the resemblance is weaker.

This lesson examines the ruling on giving the call to prayer (adhan) while in a state of major impurity (janabah). The Hanafi school holds it to be makruh, and this is based on a nuanced analogy (qiyas shabah) comparing adhan to prayer. Understanding this reasoning clarifies why adhan without wudu (minor impurity) is not disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon: giving adhan while in janabah. What is the hukm according to the text?
The text states it is makruh by a single narration (riwayah wahidah).
2
Locate the basis for the ruling
Identify the proof: the ruling is based on qiyas shabah (analogy of resemblance) comparing adhan to prayer. List the points of resemblance.
Both begin with takbir, face qibla, have arranged words, are time-specific, and prohibit speaking.
3
Understand the distinction between major and minor impurity
The text explains that adhan resembles prayer in some aspects and not in others. In janabah, the resemblance is given weight, so purity is required, making it makruh. In minor impurity, the non-resemblance is given weight, so purity is not required.
This is a key Hanafi method: acting on both the resemblance and difference (al-shabahayn).
4
Analyze the ruling on repetition
There are two narrations on whether to repeat the adhan if given in janabah. The preferred view (ashbah) is to repeat the adhan but not the iqama, because repetition of adhan is prescribed (e.g., Friday) while repetition of iqama is not.
Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir is that repetition is mustahab.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a junub gives adhan, it is valid but disliked. It is mustahab for another to repeat the adhan. The prayer after it is valid because prayer does not require adhan.
This shows the school's careful balance between respect for the adhan and practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالت جنابت میں اذان کہنے کا حکم
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ تُوَذِنَ وَهُوَ جُنُبْ رِوَايَةً وَاحِدَةً وَوَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ عَلَى إِحْدَى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ هُوَ أَنَّ لِلأَذَانِ شَبِهَا بِالصَّلوة فَيشْتَرطُ الطَّهَارَةُ عَنْ أَغْلَةِ الْحَدَثَيْنِ دُونَ اَخَفِّهِمَا عَمَلًا بِالشَّبُهَيْنِ وَ فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ إِذَا أَذَّنَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوع وَاقَامَةٍ لَا يُعِيدُ وَالْجُنُّبُ اَحَبُّ إِلَى أنْ تُعِبْدُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُعِدُ أَجْزَاهُ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَلِخِفَةَ الْحَدَثِ وَامَّا الثَّانِي فَفِي الإِعَادَةِ بِسَبَبِ الجَنَابَةِ رِوَايَتَانِ وَالأَشْبَهُ أنْ يُعَادَ الأَذَانُ دُونَ الإقامة لأنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْآذَانِ مَشْرُوعُ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ
وَقَوْلُهُ إِن لَمْ يُعِدُ أَجْزَاهُ يَعْنِي الصَّلوةَ لِأَنَّهَا جَائِزَةٌ بِدُونِ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ
ترجمہ اور جنسی کی اذان مکروہ ہے۔ روایت واحدہ ہے۔ اور وجہ فرق دو روایتوں میں سے ایک پر یہ ہے کہ اذان نماز کے ساتھ مشابہت رکھتی ہے۔ لہذا الغلظ حدثین سے طہارت شرط ہے نہ کہ اخب حدثین سے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کرنے کی وجہ سے ۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جب بے وضو اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو اعادہ نہ کرے اور جنبی (نے اگر ایسا کیا ) تو میرے نزدیک اعادہ کرنا پسندیدہ ہے ۔ اور اگر عادہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کافی ہو جائے گا۔ بہر حال اول تو حدث کے خفیف ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور رہا ثانی تو جنابت کی وجہ سے اس کے اعادہ میں دو روایتیں ہیں اور اشبہ بالفقہ یہ ہے کہ اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے نہ کہ اقامت کا۔ اس لئے کہ اذان کا تکرار مشروع ہے لیکن اقامت کا تکرار مشروع نہیں ہے۔ اور امام محمد کا قول إِن لَمْ يُعد أجزاه یعنی نماز، کیونکہ نماز بغیر اذان اورا قامت کے جائز ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بحالت جنابت اذان دینا مکروہ ہے اور اس میں فقط ایک ہی روایت ہے یعنی کراہت کی روایت اور عدم کراہت کی کوئی روایت نہیں ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ محدث کی اذان میں کراہت اور عدم کراہت کی دونوں روایتیں ہیں۔ پس جنسی کی اذان اور عدم کراہت کی روایات پر محدث کی اذان کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اذان نماز کے مشابہ ہے اس طور پر کہ دونوں کو تکبیر کے ساتھ شروع کیا جاتا ہے۔ دونوں استقبال قبلہ کے ساتھ ادا ہوتے ہیں اور کلمات اذان اسی طرح مرتب ہیں جس طرح ارکان نماز مرتب میں دونوں وقت کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اور دونوں کے درمیان کلام کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اس اعتبار سے اذان نماز کے مشابہ ہوئی
لیکن اذان حقیقت نماز نہیں ہے۔
حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اذان مین وجہ نماز کے مشابہ نہیں ہے اور من وجہ مشابہ نہیں ہے پس اگر مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو اذان حدث کے ساتھ بھی نا جائز ہونی چاہئے اور جنابت کے ساتھ بھی۔
اور اگر عدم مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو دونوں صورتوں میں اذان با اکراہت جائز ہونی چاہئے پس ہم نے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کیا چنانچہ جنابت کی صورت میں نماز کے ساتھ مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اذان کے لئے طہارت شرط ہے لہذا بحالت جنابت اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔ اور حدث کی صورت میں نماز کے ساتھ عدم مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اذان کے لئے طہارت شرط نہیں ہے لہذا بحالت حدث اذان دینا مکروہ نہیں ہوگا۔ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا کہ اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو اذان واقامت کا اعادہ نہ کرے اور اگر جنبی نے اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو میرے نزدیک اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے۔ شرح طحاوی میں مذکور ہے کہ چار آدمیوں کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے: (۱) جنبی، (۲) عورت، (۳) نشہ میں مست، (۴) دیوانہ
لیکن اگر جنبی کی اقامت و اذان کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کافی ہے۔ بہر حال محدث کی اذان اور اس کی اقامت کا اعادہ نہ کرنا اس لئے ہے کہ حدث خفیف نجاست ہے۔ اور رہا ثانی یعنی جنبی کی اذان واقامت تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں، ایک یہ کہ اعادہ کرے اور دوم یہ کہ اعادہ نہ کرے۔ اشبہ بالفقہ یہ ہے کہ جنبی کے اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے اور اقامت کا اعادہ نہ کیا جائے۔ کیونکہ اذان کے اندر فی الجملہ تکرار مشروع ہے جیسے جمعہ میں اذان دو بار دی جاتی ہے لیکن اقامت کا تکرار مشروع نہیں ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام محمد کا قول إِن لَم يُعِدُ اجزاہ ، اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ نماز کافی ہے کیونکہ نماز تو بغیر اذان اور اقامت کے جائز ہے۔ لہذا بغیر اعادہ کے بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگی۔
The ruling on giving adhan in a state of janabah: And it is makruh to give adhan while in janabah, in one narration. And the aspect of distinction according to one of the two narrations is that adhan has a resemblance to prayer, so purification from the major hadath is required, not from the minor one, acting on both resemblances. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If one gives adhan without wudu and iqama, he should not repeat; but for the junub, I prefer that he repeats, and if he does not repeat, it suffices. As for the first, it is due to the lightness of the hadath; as for the second, there are two narrations regarding repetition due to janabah, and the more appropriate is that the adhan should be repeated, not the iqama, because repetition of adhan is prescribed, while repetition of iqama is not. And his saying 'if he does not repeat, it suffices' means the prayer, because prayer is permissible without adhan and iqama. Translation: And the adhan of a junub is makruh; it is a single narration... Explanation: The matter is that giving adhan in janabah is makruh, and there is only one narration on this, i.e., the narration of karahah, and there is no narration of non-karahah. And it has passed earlier that regarding the adhan of one with minor impurity, there are both narrations of karahah and non-karahah. So the distinction between the adhan of a junub and the adhan of one with minor impurity is that adhan resembles prayer in that both begin with takbir, both are performed facing the qibla, the words of adhan are arranged like the pillars of prayer, both are specific to time, and speaking between them is prohibited. So from this aspect, adhan resembles prayer. But adhan is not actually prayer. The conclusion is that adhan resembles prayer in some respects and not in others. If we consider the resemblance, adhan would be impermissible with both minor and major impurity; if we consider the non-resemblance, it would be permissible with karahah in both cases. So we acted on both resemblances: in the case of janabah, we considered the resemblance to prayer and said that purity is a condition for adhan, hence adhan in janabah is makruh; in the case of minor impurity, we considered the non-resemblance and said purity is not a condition, hence adhan in minor impurity is not makruh. Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If one gives adhan and iqama without wudu, he should not repeat; if a junub does so, then in my view it is mustahab to repeat. It is mentioned in Sharh al-Tahawi that it is mustahab to repeat the adhan of four people: (1) junub, (2) woman, (3) intoxicated, (4) insane. But if the junub's iqama and adhan are not repeated, it is still sufficient. The non-repetition of the adhan and iqama of one with minor impurity is because minor impurity is a light impurity. As for the junub's adhan and iqama, there are two narrations: one says repeat, the other says do not repeat. The more appropriate is that the junub's adhan should be repeated, not the iqama, because repetition of adhan is prescribed generally, like the adhan on Friday is given twice, but repetition of iqama is not prescribed. The author of al-Hidayah said: Imam Muhammad's statement 'if he does not repeat, it suffices' means the prayer is sufficient, because prayer is permissible without adhan and iqama, so without repetition it is even more permissible.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on giving adhan while in a state of janabah (major impurity). The text states that it is makruh by unanimous narration, unlike minor impurity (without wudu) where there are two narrations. The key distinction is that adhan has a resemblance to prayer in several aspects: both begin with takbir, both face the qibla, their words are arranged like prayer, both are time-specific, and speaking during them is prohibited. Because of this resemblance, purity from major impurity is required for adhan, making it makruh in janabah. However, for minor impurity, the resemblance is weaker, so adhan without wudu is not makruh. The text also discusses repetition: according to Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, if one gives adhan without wudu, no repetition is needed; but for a junub, it is mustahab to repeat the adhan, though if not repeated, the prayer is still valid. The preferred view (ashbah) is to repeat the adhan but not the iqama, because repetition of adhan is prescribed (e.g., Friday adhan) while repetition of iqama is not. The commentary from Sharh al-Tahawi lists four persons whose adhan should be repeated: junub, woman, intoxicated, and insane. The author of al-Hidayah clarifies that Imam Muhammad's statement 'if he does not repeat, it suffices' refers to the prayer being valid without adhan and iqama altogether, so without repetition it is even more valid.

Key Terms
جنابت (janabah): A state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full ablution), typically after sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity; divided into minor (hadath asghar, removed by wudu) and major (hadath akbar, removed by ghusl).
مشابہت (mushabahat): Resemblance or similarity; used here to compare adhan to prayer in certain aspects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on giving adhan while in a state of janabah?
A) It is haram and invalid.
B) It is makruh, and it is mustahab to repeat the adhan.
C) It is permissible without any dislike.
D) It is invalid and requires repeating both adhan and iqama.

Key Takeaway
Adhan in janabah is makruh by single narration, and it is mustahab to repeat the adhan but not the iqama.

Ruling on a Woman Giving Adhan
States the ruling on a woman giving adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman giving adhan and explain why repeating it is mustahab.

Core Idea
A woman's adhan is valid but not sunnah; repeating it is mustahab to align with the prescribed practice of a male mu'adhdhin.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a woman giving adhan. The passage clarifies that while a woman's adhan is not invalid, it is not the ideal sunnah practice. The text explains the reasoning based on the nature of a woman's voice and the established sunnah. We will break down the ruling, the recommended repetition, and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman giving adhan. The ruling is that it is bid'ah (innovation) and mustahab to repeat the adhan by a man to achieve the sunnah manner.
The adhan itself is not invalid, but it is not the prescribed way.
2
Understand the basis for the ruling
The sunnah is that the mu'adhdhin be a man. A woman's adhan deviates from this ideal. If she raises her voice, she commits a haram act because her voice is considered 'awrah (must be concealed).
The ruling is rooted in the principle that a woman's voice can cause fitnah.
3
Analyze the recommended action
Because the adhan is not in the sunnah manner, it is mustahab to repeat it, just as it is mustahab to repeat the adhan of a junub (person in state of major impurity). This repetition restores the sunnah practice.
The comparison with a junub's adhan highlights that the deficiency is in the manner, not the validity.
4
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
If a woman gives adhan in a mosque, the congregation should consider it valid for notification but should repeat it by a male. If she used a loud voice, she may have sinned.
The adhan should be repeated quietly or by another man to avoid fitnah.

Source Text

عورت کی اذان کا حکم
قَالَ وَ كَذَلِكَ الْمَرْأةُ تُؤدَنُ مَعْنَاهُ يُسْتَحَبُّ أن تُعَادَ لِيَفَعَ عَلَى وَجْهِ السُّنَّةِ
ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا کہ یہی حکم ہے عورت کی اذان کا۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ عورت کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے تا کہ بطور سنت
واقع ہو۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح جنبی کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے اسی طرح اگر عورت نے اذان دی ہے تو اس کا اعادہ بھی مستحب ہے تا کہ اذان مسنون طریقہ پر واقع ہو کیونکہ مسنون یہ ہے کہ مؤذن مرد ہو۔
اور عورت کا اذان دینا مسنون نہیں بدعت ہے کیونکہ اگر عورت نے بآواز بلند اذان دی تو اس نے فعل حرام کا ارتکاب کیا اس لئے کہ عورت کی آواز بھی عورت ہوتی ہے یعنی جس طرح عورت واجب الستر ہے اسی طرح اس کی آواز بھی واجب الستر ہے اور اگر اس نے
The ruling on a woman's adhan. He said: And similarly the woman gives adhan. Its meaning is that it is mustahab to repeat it so that it occurs in the manner of the sunnah. Translation: The author said that the same ruling applies to a woman's adhan. Its meaning is that repeating a woman's adhan is mustahab so that it becomes in the manner of the sunnah. Explanation: The issue is that just as it is mustahab to repeat the adhan of a junub, similarly if a woman has given adhan, repeating it is mustahab so that the adhan occurs in the prescribed sunnah manner, because the sunnah is that the mu'adhdhin be a man. And a woman giving adhan is not sunnah; it is a bid'ah, because if a woman gives adhan with a loud voice, she commits a forbidden act, because a woman's voice is also 'awrah; just as a woman is required to conceal herself, her voice is also required to be concealed.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a woman giving adhan. The author states that just as it is mustahab to repeat the adhan of a junub, it is also mustahab to repeat a woman's adhan. The reason is that the sunnah (prescribed way) is that the mu'adhdhin should be a man. A woman giving adhan is not in accordance with the sunnah; it is considered a bid'ah (innovation). Furthermore, if a woman raises her voice in adhan, it becomes haram (forbidden) because a woman's voice is regarded as 'awrah (something to be concealed) just like her body. Therefore, her adhan should be repeated to rectify the situation. The text ends abruptly, but the complete ruling is that while the adhan itself may be valid in the sense that it notifies others, it is not the prescribed sunnah, and repeating it is recommended to bring the practice in line with the sunnah.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended; an action whose performance is rewarded but omission is not sinful.
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religious matters that is not based on the Sunnah; often blameworthy.
عورت کی آواز (awrat ki awaz): A woman's voice; the text states it is 'awrah and must be concealed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it mustahab to repeat a woman's adhan according to the passage?
A) Because a woman's adhan is invalid and must be redone.
B) So that the adhan occurs according to the sunnah, which requires a male mu'adhdhin.
C) Because a woman's voice is always forbidden to be heard.
D) Because the woman is likely to make mistakes.

Key Takeaway
A woman's adhan is valid but not sunnah; repeating it by a man is mustahab to follow the prescribed practice, and a loud voice makes it haram due to the voice being 'awrah.

Ruling on Adhan by a Junubi and a Woman (Hanafi)
Explaining ruling on adhan by junubi and woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan by a junubi and a woman, explain the reasoning based on similarity to prayer, and identify when repetition is mustahabb.

Core Idea
Adhan by a junubi is valid but makruh; repetition is mustahabb. A woman's adhan is valid but mustahabb to repeat to follow the sunnah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the rulings on adhan when performed by a person in major impurity (junubi) and by a woman. The author uses a nuanced reasoning based on the similarity of adhan to prayer and the distinctions between major and minor impurity. Understanding this will clarify common misconceptions about the validity and recommended repetition of adhan in these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the hukm for adhan by a junubi and by a woman as stated in the text.
For junubi: valid but makruh tanzih. For woman: valid but mustahabb to repeat.
2
Understand the dalil (proof)
The reasoning uses similarity (mushabahah) between adhan and prayer. Adhan resembles prayer in form but differs in legal status.
Similarity leads to requiring purification for janabah; dissimilarity allows adhan without wudu.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that repetition of adhan by junubi is mustahabb; another view says no repetition needed.
The mufta bihi is to repeat for junubi and woman.
4
Apply to women's adhan
A woman's adhan is valid, but because the sunnah is for a man to give adhan, repetition is mustahabb.
Women's voice is 'awrah; raising it in adhan is problematic. Hence, repeating adhan with a male is recommended.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a junubi or woman gives adhan, the prayer is still valid, but it is better to repeat the adhan.
This is unlike other schools that may consider such adhan invalid.

كتاب الصلوة
۳۱۲

مرتب میں دونوں وقت کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اور دونوں کے درمیان کلام کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اس اعتبار سے اذان نماز کے مشابہ ہوئی
لیکن اذان حقیقت نماز نہیں ہے۔
حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اذان مین وجہ نماز کے مشابہ نہیں ہے اور من وجہ مشابہ نہیں ہے پس اگر مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو اذان حدث کے ساتھ بھی نا جائز ہونی چاہئے اور جنابت کے ساتھ بھی۔
اور اگر عدم مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو دونوں صورتوں میں اذان با اکراہت جائز ہونی چاہئے پس ہم نے دونوں مشابہتوں پر عمل کیا چنانچہ جنابت کی صورت میں نماز کے ساتھ مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اذان کے لئے طہارت شرط ہے لہذا بحالت جنابت اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔ اور حدث کی صورت میں نماز کے ساتھ عدم مشابہت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اذان کے لئے طہارت شرط نہیں ہے لہذا بحالت حدث اذان دینا مکروہ نہیں ہوگا۔ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا کہ اگر بغیر وضو اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو اذان واقامت کا اعادہ نہ کرے اور اگر جنبی نے اذان دی اور اقامت کہی تو میرے نزدیک اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے۔ شرح طحاوی میں مذکور ہے کہ چار آدمیوں کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے: (۳) نشہ میں مست ، (۴) دیوانه
جنبی ،
۲) عورت،
لیکن اگر جنبی کی اقامت و اذان کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کافی ہے۔ بہر حال محدث کی اذان اور اس کی اقامت کا اعادہ نہ کرنا اس لئے ہے کہ حدث خفیف نجاست ہے۔ اور رہا ثانی یعنی جنبی کی اذان واقامت تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں، ایک یہ کہ اعادہ کرے اور دوم یہ کہ اعادہ نہ کرے۔ اشبہ بالفقہ یہ ہے کہ جنبی کے اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے اور اقامت کا اعادہ نہ کیا جائے۔ کیونکہ اذان کے اندر فی الجملہ تکرار مشروع ہے جیسے جمعہ میں اذان دو بار دی جاتی ہے لیکن اقامت کا تکرار مشروع نہیں ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام محمد کا قول إِن لَم يُعِدُ اجزاہ ، اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ نماز کافی ہے کیونکہ نماز تو بغیر اذان اور اقامت کے جائز ہے۔ لہذا بغیر اعادہ کے بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگی۔
عورت کی اذان کا حکم
قَالَ وَ كَذَلِكَ الْمَرْأةُ تُؤدَنُ مَعْنَاهُ يُسْتَحَبُّ أن تُعَادَ لِيَفَعَ عَلَى وَجْهِ السُّنَّةِ
ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا کہ یہی حکم ہے عورت کی اذان کا۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ عورت کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے تا کہ بطور سنت
واقع ہو۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح جنبی کی اذان کا اعادہ کرنا مستحب ہے اسی طرح اگر عورت نے اذان دی ہے تو اس کا اعادہ بھی مستحب ہے تا کہ اذان مسنون طریقہ پر واقع ہو کیونکہ مسنون یہ ہے کہ مؤذن مرد ہو۔
اور عورت کا اذان دینا مسنون نہیں بدعت ہے کیونکہ اگر عورت نے بآواز بلند اذان دی تو اس نے فعل حرام کا ارتکاب کیا اس لئے کہ عورت کی آواز بھی عورت ہوتی ہے یعنی جس طرح عورت واجب الستر ہے اسی طرح اس کی آواز بھی واجب الستر ہے اور اگر اس نے
آواز بلند نہیں کی تو مقصود اذان فوت ہو گیا اس لئے مستحب یہ ہے کہ اس کی اذان کا اعادہ کیا جائے۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ عورتوں پر نہ اذان ہے اور نہ اقامت کیونکہ یہ دونوں نماز با جماعت کی سنتیں ہیں اور عورتوں کی جماعت منسوخ ہوگئی ۔ ہاں اگر وہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا چاہیں تو بغیر اذان اور بغیر اقامت کے پڑھیں۔ حدیث رابطہ دلیل ہے قَالَتْ كُنَّا جَمَاعَةً مِنَ النِّسَاءِ امَتُنَا عَائِشَةُ بِلَا آذَانِ وَ لَا إِقَامَةٍ ،، رائطہ کہتی ہیں کہ ہم عورتوں کی جماعت حضرت عائشہ بلا اذ ان اور بلا اقامت امامت کرتی تھیں۔
Book of Prayer. ... In summary, the adhan is similar to prayer in one respect and not similar in another. If similarity is considered, then adhan with minor hadath and janabah should be invalid. If dissimilarity is considered, then in both cases adhan should be valid with dislike. So we acted upon both similarities: in case of janabah, considering similarity with prayer, we said purification is a condition for adhan, so giving adhan in janabah is makruh. In case of minor hadath, considering dissimilarity, we said purification is not a condition, so giving adhan with minor hadath is not makruh. Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If one gives adhan and iqamah without wudu, he should not repeat the adhan and iqamah; but if a junubi gives adhan and iqamah, in my view repeating is mustahabb. In Sharh al-Tahawi it is mentioned that repeating the adhan of four persons is mustahabb: the junubi, the woman, the intoxicated, the insane. But if the adhan and iqamah of a junubi are not repeated, it is sufficient. ... The ruling of a woman's adhan: The author said: and similarly the woman's adhan; its meaning is that it is mustahabb to repeat it so that it occurs in the sunnah manner. Explanation: Just as repeating the adhan of a junubi is mustahabb, similarly if a woman gives adhan, its repetition is mustahabb so that the adhan occurs in the sunnah manner, because the sunnah is that the muadhdhin be a man. And a woman's giving adhan is not sunnah, it is innovation, because if she gives adhan loudly she commits a prohibited act, since a woman's voice is also 'awrah; just as a woman is wajib al-satr, so is her voice wajib al-satr. And if she does not raise her voice, the purpose of adhan is lost. So it is mustahabb to repeat her adhan. Another point: Women are not obliged with adhan or iqamah, because both are sunnah of congregational prayer, and women's congregation is nullified. However, if they wish to pray in congregation, they should pray without adhan and iqamah. The hadith of Raiitah is evidence: She said: We were a congregation of women; 'A'ishah led us without adhan and iqamah.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings concerning the adhan (call to prayer) when performed by a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junubi) and by a woman. The author explains the reasoning behind the Hanafi position using the principle of similarity (mushabahah) between adhan and prayer. Since adhan resembles prayer in some aspects (e.g., it involves the remembrance of Allah and is performed in a specific manner) but differs in others (it is not an act of worship requiring purity), the Hanafi school takes a middle ground: for janabah (major impurity), adhan is valid but makruh (disliked) because purification is required for prayer; for minor hadath (without wudu), adhan is valid without dislike. Imam Muhammad's position from al-Jami' al-Saghir is quoted: if one performs adhan and iqamah without wudu, they need not repeat; but if a junubi does so, repetition is mustahabb (recommended). The text then cites Sharh al-Tahawi listing four persons whose adhan should be repeated: the junubi, the woman, the intoxicated, and the insane. However, if not repeated, it is still valid. Regarding women, the commentary explains that a woman's adhan is not the sunnah; the sunnah is that the muadhdhin be a man. If a woman gives adhan, it is mustahabb to repeat it so that the adhan is done in the proper sunnah manner. The reason is that a woman's voice is considered 'awrah (something to be concealed), so raising it in adhan would be makruh or even haram if it leads to fitnah. The passage also notes that women are not obligated to perform adhan or iqamah, as these are specific to congregational prayer for men. A hadith from 'A'ishah is cited to show that women's congregation without adhan is established.

Key Terms
جنبی (junubi): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
حدث (hadath): A state of minor ritual impurity requiring wudu.
مکروہ (makruh): An act that is disliked but not sinful; here it is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a woman giving the adhan?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but mustahabb to repeat so that it is done in the sunnah manner.
C) It is valid and no repetition is needed.
D) It is haram and the prayer must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Adhan by a junubi or a woman is valid, but repetition is mustahabb to align with the sunnah or to remove the dislike.

Adhan Before Time: The Hanafi Position and the Fajr Exception
Ruling on adhan before time and dispute for Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers adhan before the time invalid and how they refute the opposing view regarding Fajr.

Core Idea
An adhan given before its time misleads people and is invalid — must be repeated within the time.

This lesson examines the ruling on giving the adhan before the prescribed prayer time, with a focus on the dispute regarding Fajr. The Hanafi school, based on explicit hadith, holds that any adhan before the time is invalid and must be repeated. However, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i allow an exception for Fajr in the last half of the night. We will analyze the proofs and the Hanafi refutation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on adhan before time
Identify the general Hanafi position: adhan before the entry of prayer time is invalid (batil) and must be repeated within the time.
This is based on the principle that adhan is for notification; giving it earlier causes ignorance.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and al-Shafi'i allow adhan for Fajr in the last half of the night. Their basis is the continuous practice (tawatur) of the people of Makkah and Madinah and a hadith about Bilal.
3
Follow the opposing school's proof
Examine the hadith: 'Indeed Bilal gives the adhan at night, so eat and drink until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum.' This is cited to permit adhan before dawn.
The opposing school views this as evidence that adhan for Fajr can be given during the night.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to that proof
The Hanafi commentary explains that Bilal's adhan was for suhur and tahajjud, not for the Fajr prayer itself. The real Fajr adhan was given by Ibn Umm Maktum after true dawn. Thus the hadith actually supports the Hanafi view.
Also, the Prophet explicitly told Bilal: 'Do not give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you.'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, if adhan is given before time, it must be repeated. Under the opposing view, for Fajr it is valid and need not be repeated.
This difference affects the validity of the adhan and potentially the prayer if people act on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يُؤَذِّنُ لِصَلوةِ قَبْلَ دُخُولِ وَقْتِهَا وَيُعَادُ فِي الْوَقْتِ لِأَنَّ الْإِذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ وَقَبْلَ الْوَقْتِ تَجْهِيلُ وَقَالَ ابرُ يُوسُفَ وَهُوَ قَولُ الشَّافِعَى يَجُوزُ لِلْفَجْرِ فِى النَّصْفِ الْأَخِيرِ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ لِتَوَارُثِ أَهْلِ الْحَرَمَيْنِ وَالحُجَّةُ عَلَى الكُلِّ قَولُه عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام لِبِلَالٍ لَا تَوَذِنَ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْسَ لَكَ الْفَجُرُ هَكَذَا وَمَدَ يَدَيْهِ عَرْضا
ترجمہ اور نہ اذان دی جائے کسی نماز کے لئے اس کا وقت داخل ہونے سے پہلے اور وقت کے اندر اعادہ کیا جائے کیونکہ اذان تو دخول وقت کی خبر دینے کے لئے ہے اور وقت سے پہلے لوگوں کو جہالت میں ڈالنا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے کہ فجر کے واسطے رات کے نصف آخر میں جائز ہے کیونکہ اہل حرمین سے تو ارثا منقول ہے اور سب کے خلاف حجت حضرت بلال سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول
ہے کہ تو اذان مت دے یہاں تک کہ تیرے لئے فجر اس طرح ظاہر ہو جائے اور آپ نے اپنے دونوں ہاتھ چوڑائی میں پھیلائے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کا وقت داخل ہونے سے پہلے اذ ان معتبر نہیں ہوگی چنانچہ اگرکسی نے وقت سے پہلے اذان کہہ دی ہو تو وقت کے اندر اس کا اعادہ کیا جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اذان سے مقصود لوگوں کو دخول وقت نماز کی خبر دینا ہے اور وقت سے پہلے اذان دینا لوگوں کو جہالت میں ڈالنا ہے اس لئے وقت سے پہلے اذان شرعاً معتبر نہیں ہوگی ۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا اور یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے کہ فجر کے واسطے رات کے نصف اخیر میں اذان دینا جائز ہے۔ ان حضرات سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ تمام رات فجر کی اذان کا وقت ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل مکہ اور اہل مدینہ کے نزدیک یہ بات متوارتا چلی آرہی ہے کہ فجر کے واسطے رات کے نصف اخیر میں اذان دیتے ہیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا: إِنَّ بِلا لا يؤذِّنُ بِلَيْلٍ فَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى تَسْمَعُوا أَذَانَ إِبْن أُمِّ مَكْتُومٍ عنى بادل رات میں اذان دیتے ہیں سو تم کھاؤ اور پیو یہاں تک کہ ابن ام مکتوم کی اذان سنو ۔
یعنی
اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بلال فجر سے پہلے ہی رات میں اذان دے دیا کرتے تھے لیکن اگر غور کیا جائے تو یہ حدیث ہمارے لئے حجت ہے نہ کہ ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے لئے ۔ کیونکہ حضرت بابل کی یہ اذان نماز تہجد اور سحری کھانے کے لئے تھی نہ کہ نماز فجر کے لئے نماز فجر کے لئے ابن ام مکتوم کی اذان تھی جو د خول وقت فجر کے بعد ہوتی تھی ۔ ورنہ حَتَّى تَسْمَعُوا أَذَانَ ابْنِ أُمِّ مَكْتُومٍ کا کیا مطلب ہو گا۔ ان حضرات کے خلاف یہ حدیث بھی حجت ہوگی کہ حضرت بلال کو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اذان مت دے یہاں تک کہ فجر ظاہر ہو جائے ۔ راوی کہتا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے دونوں ہاتھ پورائی میں پھیلا کر اشارہ کیا جس سے صبح صادق کی طرف اشارہ تھا۔ اور ابن عبدالبر نے ابراہیم سے روایت کی قَالَ كَانُوا إِذَا أَذَّنَ الْمُؤذِّنُ بِلَيْلٍ قَالُوا لَهُ اتَّقِ اللَّهَ وَاعِدُ اذَانَكَ - ابرانیم
And do not give the adhan for a prayer before its time enters, and it should be repeated within the time, because the adhan is for notification, and before the time is causing ignorance. Abu Yusuf said—and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i—that it is permissible for Fajr in the last half of the night due to continuous practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries. The proof against all is his saying (peace be upon him) to Bilal: 'Do not give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you like this,' and he spread his hands wide. Commentary: The ruling is that adhan before the time is not valid; if someone gives adhan before the time, it must be repeated within the time. The proof is that adhan is meant to inform people of the entry of prayer time, and giving it before time leads to ignorance. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that adhan for Fajr is allowed in the last half of the night. Their proof is the continuous practice of the people of Mecca and Medina, and the hadith: 'Indeed Bilal gives the adhan at night, so eat and drink until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum.' But upon reflection, this hadith is evidence for us, not for them, because Bilal's adhan was for tahajjud and suhur, not for Fajr prayer. The adhan for Fajr was that of Ibn Umm Maktum, which occurred after the time of Fajr entered. Otherwise what would be the meaning of 'until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum'? Against them is also the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: 'Do not give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear to you.' The narrator says he spread his hands wide, indicating the true dawn (subh sadiq). And Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated from Ibrahim: 'When the muadhdhin gave adhan at night, they would say to him: Fear Allah and repeat your adhan.'
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on giving the adhan before the prescribed time for prayer. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that adhan given before the time is invalid and must be repeated within the time. The reason is that the purpose of adhan is to announce the entry of the time; doing so earlier misleads people. Imam Abu Yusuf (and Imam al-Shafi'i) hold an exception for Fajr: it is permissible to give the adhan during the last half of the night, citing the continuous practice (tawatur) of the people of Makkah and Madinah. They also cite the hadith in which the Prophet said: 'Indeed Bilal gives the adhan at night, so eat and drink until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum.' The Hanafi commentary refutes this by explaining that Bilal's adhan was for tahajjud and suhur, not for the Fajr prayer itself; the actual Fajr adhan was given by Ibn Umm Maktum after true dawn. Thus, the hadith actually supports the Hanafi position. The commentary further strengthens the Hanafi view with another hadith where the Prophet explicitly told Bilal not to give the adhan until the dawn becomes clear, gesturing to the true dawn (subh sadiq). Additionally, a narration from Ibrahim indicates that the practice of the early Muslims was to reprimand any muadhdhin who gave the adhan at night and order him to repeat it. Therefore, the reliable Hanafi position is that adhan is only valid after the time has entered; any adhan before time must be repeated.

Key Terms
تجہیل (tajhil): Causing ignorance; giving adhan before time misleads people about the entry of prayer time.
متواتر (mutawatir): Continuously transmitted practice; here applied to the practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone gives the adhan for Fajr during the last half of the night?
A) It is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) It is invalid and must be repeated after true dawn.
C) It is permissible with dislike.
D) It is valid for Fajr but not for other prayers.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is only valid after the prayer time has entered; any adhan before time must be repeated, even for Fajr.

Ruling on Adhan Before Time: Hanafi Position and Dispute for Fajr
Inter-madhhab dispute on Fajr adhan before time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan before the time and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding Fajr adhan, including the proofs and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Adhan before time invalidates the adhan; the relied-upon Hanafi position requires i'adah for all prayers, including Fajr.

This lesson examines one of the most practical disputes in the adhan: can the Fajr adhan be given before dawn? While the Hanafi school uniformly holds that adhan before time is invalid, Imam Abu Yusuf—a major Hanafi authority—and Imam al-Shafi'i allowed it for Fajr in the latter half of the night. We will unpack the proofs on both sides and see why the relied-upon position is that adhan before time must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on adhan before time
Identify the general ruling: adhan given before the entry of prayer time is invalid and must be repeated (i'adah) within the time. Determine the hukm level and the underlying rationale (adhan is for announcement, before time it misleads).
This applies to all prayers, not just Fajr.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proponents
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that for Fajr specifically, adhan in the latter half of the night is permissible. Recognize that this is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute.
Abu Yusuf's view is not the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the evidence cited by Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: the continuous practice (tawāruṡ) of the people of Makkah and Madinah, and the hadith that Bilal (RA) used to give adhan at night for Fajr.
The hadith: 'Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opponent's proof
Understand how the Hanafi school refutes these proofs: (a) the practice of the people of the Haram is not authoritative against explicit Sunnah; (b) Bilal's adhan was for Tahajjud and Suhur, not for Fajr—the actual Fajr adhan was given by Ibn Umm Maktum after dawn; (c) the Prophet's instruction to Bilal to wait until dawn clearly indicates the correct time.
The hadith 'Let not Bilal's adhan deceive you' actually supports the Hanafi position by warning against relying on it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Contrast the practical outcomes: According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, if adhan is given before time, it must be repeated. According to Abu Yusuf/Shafi'i, the adhan is valid and need not be repeated. This affects whether the prayer based on that adhan is considered notified correctly.
The thamarah is whether i'adah is wajib or not.

اعتبار نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کے ساتھ دھوکا کھانے اور اس کا اعتبار کرنے سے منع کیا ہے۔
And one should not give adhan for a prayer before its time enters, and it is repeated within the time because adhan is for informing, and before the time it is ignorance. Abu Yusuf said, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i: it is permissible for Fajr in the latter half of the night due to the continuous practice of the people of the two sanctuaries. The proof against all is his (peace be upon him) saying to Bilal: 'Do not give adhan until dawn becomes clear to you like this,' and he spread his hands widthwise. Translation: And the adhan should not be given for any prayer before its time enters, and it is repeated within the time because adhan is to inform of the time's entry, and before time it is to put people into ignorance. And Abu Yusuf said, and this is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i, that for Fajr it is permissible in the latter half of the night because it is continuously transmitted from the people of the two sanctuaries. And the proof against all is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Bilal: 'Do not give adhan until dawn becomes clear to you like this,' and he spread his hands widthwise. Explanation: The issue is that adhan given before the prayer time enters is not valid. Therefore, if someone gave adhan before time, it should be repeated within the time. The proof is that the purpose of adhan is to inform people of the entry of prayer time, and giving adhan before time puts people into ignorance, so adhan before time is not valid according to Sharia. Imam Abu Yusuf said, and this is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i, that for Fajr it is permissible to give adhan in the latter half of the night. According to these scholars, a narration states that the entire night is the time for Fajr adhan. Their proof is that the people of Mecca and Medina have continuously practiced giving adhan for Fajr in the latter half of the night, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum.' This hadith also indicates that Bilal used to give adhan at night before Fajr, but if we reflect, this hadith is proof for us, not for Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i, because Bilal's adhan was for the Tahajjud prayer and Suhur, not for Fajr prayer. The adhan for Fajr was given by Ibn Umm Maktum after the entry of Fajr time. Otherwise, what would be the meaning of 'until you hear the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum'? Against these scholars, this hadith will also be proof that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: 'Do not give adhan until dawn appears.' The narrator says that the Prophet (peace be upon him) spread his hands widthwise indicating the true dawn. And Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated from Ibrahim: 'He said: When the mu'adhdhin gave adhan at night, they said to him: Fear Allah and repeat your adhan.' The tabi'i says that the Companions had this practice: when a mu'adhdhin gave adhan at night, they said to him: 'Fear Allah and repeat your adhan.' But if it is objected that the hadith says: 'Let not Bilal's adhan deceive you,' indicating that Bilal used to give adhan before time, the answer is that this is also proof for us because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not consider Bilal's adhan as reliable, but rather forbade being deceived by it and relying on it.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of giving the adhan before the entry of the prayer time, specifically for Fajr. The Hanafi position is that adhan before time is invalid and must be repeated. The reason is that the purpose of adhan is announcement of the time; doing so before time misleads people. Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that for Fajr, adhan in the latter half of the night is permissible, citing the continuous practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah and the hadith that Bilal used to give adhan at night. The Hanafi response distinguishes Bilal's adhan as being for Tahajjud and Suhur, not for Fajr; the actual Fajr adhan was given by Ibn Umm Maktum after dawn. The Prophet's instruction to Bilal to wait until dawn clearly indicates that the valid adhan is after the time enters. The commentary also refutes the objection that the hadith 'Let not Bilal's adhan deceive you' supports permissibility, by noting that the Prophet warned against relying on it, confirming that it is not the time for Fajr. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains that adhan before the time is not valid, and if given, it must be repeated within the time.

Key Terms
اعادہ (i'adah): Repeating the adhan after the time has entered.
توارث (tawāruṡ): Continuous inherited practice from one generation to the next.
حجت (hujjah): Authoritative proof or argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on giving the Fajr adhan after midnight but before dawn?
A) Valid and needs no repetition.
B) Invalid and must be repeated after dawn.
C) Permissible only if the mu'adhdhin intends it as a reminder for Suhur.
D) Recommended for virtue.

Key Takeaway
Adhan before the time is invalid; the relied-upon Hanafi position requires i'adah (repetition) within the time for all prayers, and the dispute about Fajr is resolved by distinguishing Bilal's adhan as being for Suhur.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Adhan and Iqamah for the Traveller
Ruling that traveller should say both adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for the traveller and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
For the traveller, both adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting both is disliked but permissible.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses an important question: what should a traveller do regarding the call to prayer when travelling? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the Prophet's command to the sons of Abu Mulaykah, allowing flexibility while strongly encouraging both adhan and iqamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the traveller's performance of adhan and iqamah. Note the hukm level (recommended, disliked, etc.)
The passage says it is disliked to leave both, indicating sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited: the Prophet's command 'When you travel, give adhan and iqamah' to the sons of Abu Mulaykah.
This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith yields the ruling. The imperative form indicates a command, but the permission to suffice with iqamah alone shows it is not obligatory.
The school uses the permission to infer it is sunnah, not fard.
4
Note the flexibility
Observe that if the traveller omits only adhan and gives iqamah, it is permissible because the companions are already present. This shows adhan is not fard.
The iqamah serves to announce the start, which is needed even when all are present.
5
Consider the city-dweller case
Contrast with the ruling for one praying alone in the city: giving adhan and iqamah is recommended to maintain the form of congregation, but omitting both is permissible because the neighborhood adhan suffices.
Based on the saying of Ibn Mas'ud.

وَالْمَسَافِرُ يُؤَذِّنُ وَ يُقِيمُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام لِأَبْنِ أَبِي مُلَيْكَةَ إِذَا سَافَرُ تُمَا فَاذْنَا وَ أُقِيْمَا فَإِنْ تَرَكَهُمَا جَمِيعًا يُكْرَهُ ولوا كَتَفى بِالْإِقَامَةِ جَازَ لِأَنَّ الْآذَانَ لِإِسْتِحْضَارِ الغَائِبِينَ وَالرُّفَقَةُ حَاضِرُونَ وَالْإِقَامَةُ لِإِعْلَامِ الإِفْتِتَاحِ وَهُمْ إِلَيْهِ مُحْتَاجُونَ فَإِنْ صَلَّى فِي بَيْتِهِ فِى الْمِصْرِ يُصَلِّى بِآذَانِ وَإِقَامَةٍ لِيَكُونَ الأَدَاءُ عَلَى هَيَّأَةِ الجَمَاعَةِ وَإِن تَرَكَهُما جَازَ لقول ابن مَسْعُودٍ أَذَانُ الْحَى يَكْفِينَا
ترجمہ اور مسافر اذان دے اور اقامت کہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابو ملیکہ کے دو بیٹوں سے فرمایا جب تم دونوں سفر کرو تو دونوں اذان اذ ان دو اور دونوں اقامت کہو۔ پس اگر دونوں کو ترک کیا تو مکروہ ہے اور اگر اقامت پر اکتفاء کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اذان تو غیر موجودلوگوں کو حاضر کرنے کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور سفر کے ساتھی سب حاضر ہیں اور اقامت نماز شروع کرنے کے لئے دینے کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور وہ سب اس کے محتاج ہیں۔ پھر اگر اس نے اپنے گھر میں شہر کے اندر نماز پڑھی۔ تو بھی اذان واقامت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے۔ تا کہ ادائے نماز بصورت جماعت ہو اور اگر اس نے اذان واقامت دونوں کو چھوڑا تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ ابن مسعودؓ کا قول ہے کہ ہم کو محلہ کی اذان کافی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر کو اذان واقامت دونوں کہنا چاہئے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابوملیکہ کے دو صاحبزادوں کو فر مایا تھا إذَا سَافَرْتُمَا فَادْنَا وَأَقِيمَا - صاحب نہایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ مبسوط میں یہ حدیث ابو ملیکہ کے بیٹوں کے علاوہ کے خطاب کے ساتھ مذکور ہے۔ وَقَالَ رُوِيَ عَنِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ لِمَالِكِ ابْنِ الحُوَيْرِث وَ ابْنِ عَمَّ لَهُ إِذَا سَافَرْتُمَا فَاذْنَا وَأَقِيمَا وَلْيُؤْتُكُمَا اكْثَرُ كُمَا فُرَانًا وَرَوى فَخَرُ الإِسلام وَلْيَؤْمَكُمَا أَكْبَرُ كُمَاسِنا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مالک ابن الحویرث اور ان کے چچازاد بھائی سے کہا جب تم دونوں سفر کرو تو از ان دو اور اقامت کہو اور تم دونوں میں سے امامت وہ کرے جو تم میں سے زیادہ قرآن پڑھا ہوا ہو۔ اور فخر الاسلام نے روایت کیا کہ امامت وہ کرے جو تم میں عمر میں بڑا ہو ۔ ابوداؤداور نسائی میں ہے يُعْجِبُ رَبَّكَ مِنْ رَاعِي غَنَمٍ فِي رَأْسِ شَطَيَةٍ يُؤَذِّنُ بِالصَّلَاةِ وَيُصَلِّي فَيَقُولُ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَل انظُرُوا إلى عَبْدِى هَذَا يُؤَذِّنُ وَيُقِيمُ لِلصَّلَاةِ يَخَافُ مِني قَدْ غَفَرْتُ لِعَبْدِي وَادْخِلْهُ الْجَنَّةَ ـ یعنی تیرا رب پسند کرتا ہے اس بکریوں کے چرواہے کو جو پہاڑ کی چوٹی پر اذان دیتا اور نماز پڑھتا ہے۔ پس اللہ تعالیٰ فرماتا ہے کہ میرے اس بندہ کو دیکھو کہ اذان دیتا اور نماز کے لئے اقامت کہتا ہے، مجھ سے ڈرتا ہے میں نے اپنے بندہ کو بخش دیا اور جنت میں داخل کیا۔
And the traveller gives adhan and iqamah due to his (peace be upon him) saying to the two sons of Abu Mulaykah: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqamah.' If he leaves both, it is disliked; if he suffices with iqamah, it is permissible because adhan is for calling the absent, and the companions are present, while iqamah is for informing of the commencement, and they need it. Then if he prays in his house in the city, he prays with adhan and iqamah so that the performance is in the form of congregation; and if he leaves both, it is permissible because of the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The adhan of the neighborhood suffices us.' Translation: And the traveller should give adhan and iqamah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the two sons of Abu Mulaykah: 'When you travel, then give adhan and iqamah.' So if he leaves both, it is disliked; and if he suffices with iqamah, it is permissible because adhan is for summoning those who are absent, and the traveling companions are present, while iqamah is for informing of the commencement, and they are in need of it. Then if he prays in his house within the city, he prays with adhan and iqamah so that the performance is in the form of congregation; and if he leaves both, it is permissible because of the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The adhan of the neighborhood suffices us.' Explanation: The issue is that the traveller should say both adhan and iqamah. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the two sons of Abu Mulaykah: 'When you travel, then give adhan and iqamah.' The author of al-Nihayah wrote that in al-Mabsut this hadith is mentioned with addressing others. And it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and his cousin: 'When you travel, give adhan and iqamah, and the one of you who has more Quran should lead you in prayer.' And Fakhr al-Islam narrated: 'And the older of you in age should lead you in prayer.' In Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i: 'Your Lord is pleased with a shepherd of goats at the top of a mountain peak who gives adhan for prayer and prays. Then Allah Almighty says: Look at this servant of Mine, he gives adhan and iqamah for prayer, fearing Me. I have forgiven My servant and admitted him to Paradise.'
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a traveller concerning adhan and iqamah. According to the Hanafi school, a traveller should generally give both adhan and iqamah when praying in a group during travel. This is based on a direct command from the Prophet (peace be upon him) to the sons of Abu Mulaykah. However, the ruling has flexibility: if the traveller omits both, it is disliked (makruh), but if he omits only the adhan and suffices with iqamah, it is permissible because the companions are already present and the iqamah serves to announce the start of prayer. If a person prays alone in his house in a city, he should also give adhan and iqamah to maintain the form of congregation, but if he omits both, it is permissible because the neighborhood's adhan from the mosque suffices, as reported from Ibn Mas'ud. The passage also cites additional proofs: the hadith to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and his cousin, emphasizing adhan and iqamah in travel, and the hadith about the shepherd, showing the virtue of performing adhan and iqamah even in isolation.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, announcing the entry of time and inviting people to congregate.
اقامت (iqamah): The second call immediately before the prayer, informing of its commencement.
مسافر (musafir): One who is travelling a distance that allows shortening of prayers (approx. 88 km).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a traveller omits both adhan and iqamah and prays alone?
A) Prayer is invalid
B) It is permissible but disliked
C) It is forbidden
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
The traveller should give adhan and iqamah; omitting both is disliked, but iqamah alone suffices.
